Buyu — Sales and Trade

The Hanafi Principle of Genus Determination in Sales
States difference in genus for vinegars and animal fibers based on origin and purpose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criterion for whether two items are of the same genus (jins) based on origin (asl) or purpose (maqsad), and state the ruling on exchanging them with disparity.

Core Idea
Two items are same genus only if they share origin or purpose; otherwise, disparity in exchange is allowed.

In Hanafi fiqh, determining whether two items belong to the same genus is crucial for contracts of exchange, especially to avoid riba. This lesson uses two concrete examples from al-Hidayah—date vinegar vs grape vinegar and goat hair vs sheep wool—to demonstrate the criteria: origin for processed liquids, and purpose for animal fibers. Understanding this principle enables you to correctly classify commodities in sales and other transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Pairs
The passage discusses two comparisons: date vinegar with grape vinegar, and goat hair with sheep wool. Identify what the author is comparing in each case.
The vinegars are processed from fruits; the fibers come from different animals.
2
Extract the Ruling for Each Pair
For each pair, the author states that they are different genera (jinsān). This means they can be exchanged with disparity (e.g., one cup of one for two cups of the other) without falling into riba.
If they were the same genus, disparity would be prohibited if the items are weighable/measurable and of the same type.
3
Identify the Criterion
The author gives the reason: for vinegars, it is due to different origins (asl); for fibers, it is due to different purposes (maqāṣid). Thus, the Hanafi criterion for determining genus is: origin for derived items, and purpose for natural items.
This is a form of ta‘līl (causal reasoning) based on ʿurf (custom) and ma‘nā (legal meaning).
4
Apply the Criterion to Another Example
Consider apple vinegar vs grape vinegar. Using the origin criterion, they are different genera because apples and grapes are different fruits. Similarly, consider cow hair vs sheep wool: different purposes (cow hair used for brushes, sheep wool for clothing) → different genera.
The criterion is not the final appearance or name but the underlying source or intended use.
5
Note the Cross-Madhhab Difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi‘i) may consider all vinegars as one genus because they all undergo fermentation and become vinegar, focusing on the final state rather than the original fruit. This difference leads to different rulings on exchange.
The Ḥanafī position relies on the principle that the origin (aṣl) imparts its ruling to the derivative (far‘).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کھجور کے سر کے کی انگور کے سر کے کے عوض بیع کا حکم
قال وكذا خل الدقل بخل العنب للاختلاف بين أصليهما فكذا بين مائيهما ولهذا كان عصيرا هما جنسين وشعر المعز صوف الغنم جنسان لاختلاف المقاصد
ترجمہ اور اسی طرح کھجور کا سرکہ انگور کے سرکہ کے عوض ، کیونکہ ان دونوں کی اصل میں اختلاف ہے۔ پس اسی طرح ان دونوں کے پانی میں بھی اختلاف ہے اور اسی وجہ سے ان دونوں کے شیرے دو جنس ہیں اور بکری کی اون اور بھیڑ کے بال دو جنس ہیں کیونکہ ان کے مقاصد میں اختلاف ہے۔
Ruling on selling date vinegar for grape vinegar. He said: Similarly, date vinegar (from inferior dates) for grape vinegar (is permissible with disparity) because of the difference between their origins; thus their liquids (vinegars) also differ. For this reason, their syrups are two genera. And goat hair and sheep wool are two genera due to difference in their purposes.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage provides rulings on two items: vinegar and animal fibers. It states that vinegar made from dates and vinegar made from grapes are different genera because their sources (dates and grapes) are different. Therefore, they can be exchanged with disparity. Similarly, goat hair and sheep wool are different genera because their purposes (uses) differ. This is consistent with the Hanafi principle that genus is determined either by origin (as in vinegars) or by purpose (as in hairs/wools). The passage concludes the discussion on sales of food items and extends it to non-food items like fibers.

Key Terms
خل (khal): Vinegar; a processed liquid considered a separate genus based on its source.
شعر (sha'r): Hair; here specifically goat hair.
صوف (suf): Wool; from sheep.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are date vinegar and grape vinegar considered different genera according to the passage?
A) They have different colors
B) Their origins (dates and grapes) are different
C) One is sweeter than the other
D) They are processed differently

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, genus (jins) is determined by origin for processed items and by purpose for natural items, so date vinegar and grape vinegar are different genera, as are goat hair and sheep wool.

Milk Exchange with Disparity: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Hanafi ruling on milk sale with proof and Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on selling milk from different animals with disparity and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Milk from different animals is of different genera because their origins differ, so disparity is allowed.

In the Hanafi school, the permissibility of exchanging milk from different animals hinges on whether they belong to the same genus. This passage presents the Hanafi ruling and contrasts it with the Shafi'i view. Understanding the reasoning—rooted in the principle that the ruling on the branch follows the origin—reveals how the Hanafis prioritize the source animal's species over the shared purpose of nutrition.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school permits selling camel milk for cow milk with disparity (e.g., 2 litres for 1 litre).
This is because the milks are considered different genera.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i prohibits disparity, requiring equal exchange, based on the idea that all milk is one genus due to common purpose (nutrition).
The Shafi'i view relies on purpose (maqsud) to determine genus.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
Examine the Hanafi evidence: the source animals are different species, as shown by the rule that zakat nisab is not combined across species. Therefore, their branches (milk, meat) are also different genera.
This is an argument from asl (origin) to far' (branch).
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Note how the Hanafis respond to the Shafi'i: difference in origins necessarily creates difference in branches; the common purpose is secondary and does not unify the genus.
The principle 'al-furu' tabi'ah li al-usul' is key.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis allow unbounded disparity in milk exchange; Shafi'is require equal weight or volume.
This affects daily transactions between farmers and traders.

قال كذالك ألبان البقر والغنم وعن الشافعى لايجوز؛ لأنها جنس واحد لاتحاد المقصود ولنا أن الأصول مختلفة حتى لايكمل نصاب أحدهما بالآخر فى الزكوة فكذا أجزائها إذا لم تتبدل الصنعة ترجمہ اور اسی طرح گائے اور بکری کا دودھ ہے اور امام شافعی سے مروی ہے کہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ سب دودہ مقصود کے متحد ہونے کی وجہ سے ایک ہی جنس ہیں۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان جانورں کی اصل مختلف ہیں حتی کہ زکوۃ میں ان میں سے ایک جنس ایک ہے تو اونٹ، گائے ، بکری میں سے ایک کے گوشت کو دوسرے کے گوشت کے عوض اور ایک کے دودھ کو دوسرے کے دودھ کے عوض برابر، برابر بیچنا تو جائز ہے لیکن کمی ، زیادتی کے ساتھ بیچنا جائز نہیں ہماری دلیل یہ کے گوشت کے عوض اور ایک کا دودھ دوسرے کے دودھ کے عوض کمی ، زیادتی کے ساتھ بیچنا جائز ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اونٹنی ، گائے اور بکری کا دودھ اس وقت تک مختلفۃ الاجناس میں جب تک کہ کاریگری کے ذریعہ ان میں تبدیلی نہ کی گئی ہو یعنی دودھ ہوں اور اگر تبدیلی کر دی گئی مثلاً مینوں کے دودھ کا پنیر بنالیا تو اب یہ ایک ہی جنس شمار ہوگا اور کی زیادتی کے ساتھ بیچنا جائز نہ ہوگا اگر چہ اصل یعنی دودھ مختلفۃ الاجناس ہیں۔
He said: Similarly, the milk of cows and goats. From al-Shafi'i, it is not permissible because they are one genus due to unity of purpose. For us, the origins are different, so that the nisab of one is not completed by the other in zakat, and likewise their parts, as long as the craftsmanship has not transformed them. The commentary: Sheikh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri says that the milk of camel, cow, and goat also differ in genus, so selling the milk of one for the milk of another with disparity is permissible. However, from Imam al-Shafi'i there is a narration that it is not permissible because all meat is one genus and all milk is one genus, due to common purpose (nutrition). So equal exchange is permissible but not with disparity. Our proof: milk and meat are branches, and their origins (animals) are different genera, and difference in origins necessitates difference in branches. Since these animals are different genera, even their nisab in zakat cannot be combined, so their branches differ. Therefore selling with disparity is permissible. Sahib al-Hidayah says that camel, cow, and goat milk are different genera as long as no craftsmanship has transformed them (e.g., if made into cheese), then they become one genus and disparity is not permissible.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on exchanging milk from different animals (camel, cow, goat) with disparity (riba al-fadl). The Hanafi school holds that these milks are of different genera because their source animals are different species, as evidenced by the zakat ruling where nisab cannot be completed by mixing animals of different species. Therefore, selling them with disparity is permissible. Imam al-Shafi'i considers them one genus due to the common purpose (nutrition), allowing only equal exchange. The Hanafi respond that the origin (asl) determines the branch (far'), and since origins differ, so do the milks. A key nuance: if the milk is processed (e.g., made into cheese), it becomes a single genus and disparity is prohibited. This is a classic inter-madhhab dispute based on legal reasoning.

Key Terms
صنعة (san'ah): Craftsmanship or processing that changes the nature of the milk, e.g., making it into cheese.
متفاضل (mutafadil): Exchange with disparity in quantity or weight.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school allow selling camel milk for cow milk with disparity?
A) Because both are milk, which is one genus
B) Because the source animals are different species, making the milks different genera
C) Because the Prophet (PBUH) allowed it
D) Because milk is not subject to riba rules

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits selling milk from different animals with disparity because the milks belong to different genera, as determined by the difference in their source animals, provided the milk is unprocessed.

Selling Date Vinegar for Grape Vinegar: Genus Determination by Origin
Ruling on vinegar exchange based on origin difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exchanging vinegars from different fruits with disparity and explain the principle that the genus of a product is determined by its source.

Core Idea
The genus of a derivative product is determined by its primary source, not its final form.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a seemingly specific transaction: selling date vinegar for grape vinegar in unequal quantities. The ruling may appear counterintuitive because both are vinegar, but the Hanafi school classifies them as different genera due to their fruit origins. Understanding this principle clarifies many other cases, such as syrups and even animal fibers like goat hair and sheep wool.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specific ruling
What is the act being judged? Selling date vinegar for grape vinegar with disparity (unequal exchange). What is its permissibility?
The ruling is that it is permissible.
2
Locate the principal dalil
What evidence is cited for the ruling? The difference between their two origins (fruits). The author argues that because dates and grapes are different genera, their products (vinegars) are also different genera.
The dalil is an extended qiyas based on the concept of genus determined by source.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the difference in origins prove that vinegars are different genera? The Hanafi principle: a product retains the genus of its primary source material. Since the fruits are different, the vinegars are different.
This is analogous to syrups (date syrup vs grape syrup) being different genera.
4
Apply the analogy to animal fibers
The text also compares goat hair and sheep wool, equating them to different genera due to difference in purposes. Even though both animals are from the same genus (Capra and Ovis), their fibers are distinct because of different uses.
This reinforces that the 'illah (effective cause) for genus differentiation is either source or purpose.
5
Confirm the Hanafi position
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is mufta bihi. There is no intra-Hanafi or inter-madhhab dispute mentioned here.
The ruling is clear and relied upon for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وكذا خل الدقل بخل العنب للاختلاف بين أصليهما فكذا بين مائيهما ولهذا كان عصيرا هما جنسين وشعر المعز صوف الغنم جنسان لاختلاف المقاصد ترجمہ اور اسی طرح کھجور کا سرکہ انگور کے سرکہ کے عوض ، کیونکہ ان دونوں کی اصل میں اختلاف ہے۔ پس اسی طرح ان دونوں کے پانی میں بھی اختلاف ہے اور اسی وجہ سے ان دونوں کے شیرے دو جنس ہیں اور بکری کی اون اور بھیڑ کے بال دو جنس ہیں کیونکہ ان کے مقاصد میں اختلاف ہے۔ تشریح دقل .... ردی اور گھٹیا کھجور خل سرکہ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ کھجو کر سرکہ کو انگور کے سرکہ کے عوض کمی ، زیادتی کے ساتھ فروخت کرنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ جب ان دونوں کی اصل یعنی کھجور اور انگور کے درمیان اختلاف ہے تو ان دونوں کے پانی یعنی سرکوں میں بھی اختلاف ہوگا اور جب کھجور اور انگور کے سرکوں میں اختلاف ہے تو کھجور کا سرکہ اور انگور کا سرکہ دو الگ الگ جنس ہو ئیں یہی وجہ ہے کہ کھجور کے شیرے اور انگور کے شیرے میں بالا جماع اختلاف جنس ہے اور پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ اختلاف جنس کی صورت میں کمی ، زیادتی کے ساتھ بیع کرنا جائز ہے اسلئے کھجور کے سرکہ کی بیع انگور کے سرکہ کے عوض متفاضل جائز ہو گی۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ بکری کے بال اور بھیٹر کی اون الگ الگ دو جنس ہیں ۔ اگر چہ خود بکری اور بھیٹر دونوں کی ایک جنس ہے۔ بال اور بھیڑ دو جنس اسلئے نہیں کہ ان کے مقاصد میں اختلاف ہے کیونکہ اون سے دوشالہ اور قیمتی کپڑے بنتے ہیں اور بالوں سے کمبل اور رسیاں بنتی ہیں۔ پس جب بال اور اون دو جنس ہیں تو ان کا مبادلہ بھی کمی زیادتی کے ساتھ جائز ہے۔
He said: Similarly, vinegar from inferior dates with vinegar from grapes, due to the difference between their two origins, likewise between their two liquids. For this reason, their two syrups are two genera. And goat hair and sheep wool are two genera due to difference in purposes. Translation: Similarly, date vinegar in exchange for grape vinegar, because there is difference between their two origins, so there is difference between their two liquids. And for this reason, their two syrups are two genera. And goat hair and sheep wool are two genera because their purposes differ. Commentary: This is the ruling: selling date vinegar for grape vinegar with disparity is permissible. Because when their origins (dates and grapes) differ, their liquids (vinegars) also differ. So they are two different genera. Similarly, date syrup and grape syrup are different genera. It has already passed that when genera differ, selling with disparity is permissible. Sahib al-Hidayah says that goat hair and sheep wool are two separate genera, even though the animals are of the same genus. They differ in purposes: wool is for shawls and valuable clothes, hair for blankets and ropes. So their exchange with disparity is permissible.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage extends the principle that the genus of a product is determined by its source. Date vinegar and grape vinegar are from different fruits, so they are different genera, allowing sale with disparity. The same applies to syrups. Additionally, it clarifies that goat hair and sheep wool are different genera despite similar animal origins, because their purposes and uses differ. This illustrates the Hanafi method of considering 'illah (effective cause) for genus determination.

Key Terms
دقل (daqal): Low-quality dates, used as a source for vinegar.
خل (khall): Vinegar, a product derived from fruits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is selling date vinegar for grape vinegar with disparity permissible?
A) Because both are vinegar
B) Because their source fruits are different, making them different genera
C) Because disparity is always allowed in vinegar
D) Because the Prophet (PBUH) allowed it

Key Takeaway
The genus of a derivative product is determined by its source; differences in sources permit disparity in exchange.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
beginner
6 min
Permissibility of Exchanging Belly Fat for Tail Fat or Meat with Disparity
Ruling on fat and meat exchange based on genus difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exchanging belly fat for tail fat or meat with disparity and explain the reasoning based on difference in genus.

Core Idea
Different genera allow disparity in sale; same genera trigger riba al-fadl.

In this passage, Imam al-Quduri and al-Marghinani address a specific transaction: selling belly fat (shahm al-batn) for tail fat (iliyah) or meat (lahm) with unequal amounts. The key question is whether this falls under riba al-fadl, which prohibits disparity when exchanging items of the same genus. The Hanafi school rules that these items belong to different genera, making the transaction permissible. Let's explore the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that selling belly fat for tail fat or meat is permissible even with disparity (tafadul).
2
Recognize the proof
The proof given is that they are different genera (ajnas mukhtalifah) due to gross difference in forms (suwar), essences (ma'ani), and benefits (manafi').
3
Understand the criteria for genus difference
The Hanafi school considers three criteria: form (e.g., shape and appearance), essence (distinct legal definitions and names), and benefit (different medical properties).
These criteria are used to determine whether items are considered the same genus for riba purposes.
4
Contrast with same genus case
If the items were of the same genus (e.g., two types of fat that share form, essence, and benefit), then disparity would be prohibited as riba al-fadl.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, any transaction involving items that are clearly distinct in these three aspects is permissible with disparity.
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is mufta bihi.

Source Text

قال وكذا شحم البطن بالإلية أو باللحم؛ لأنها أجناس مختلفة لاختلاف الصور والمعانى والمنافع اختلافا فاحشا ترجمہ اور اسی طرح پیٹ کی چربی کو دنبہ کی چکتی یا گوشت کے عوض بیع کرنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ صورتوں اور معانی اور منافع کے فاحش اختلاف کی وجہ سے ان کی اجناس مختلف ہیں۔ تشریح شحم ، چربی، البتہ ، دنبہ کی چکتی سرین کا گوشت۔ صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ پیٹ کی چربی کو دنبہ کی چکنی یا گوشت کے عوض متفاضلا بیچنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ چربی ، چپکتی اور گوشت تینوں کی جنس الگ الگ ہے اور ان کی اجناس میں اختلاف کا ہونا تو ظاہر ہے۔ اور معانی میں اختلاف اسلئے ہے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک کی حقیقت الگ الگ ہے۔ چنانچہ ان میں سے ایک کا نام حسم ہے دوسرے کا البتہ اور تیسرے کالم ہے اور منافع میں اختلاف کا علم علم طب کے ذریعہ ہو سکتا ہے۔ پس جب ان اشیائے ثلاثہ کی اجناس مختلف ہیں تو ان کا مبادلہ کی ، زیادتی کے ساتھ بھی جائز اور درست ہے۔
He said: Similarly, belly fat with tail fat or with meat, because they are different genera due to gross difference in forms, essences, and benefits. Translation: Similarly, selling belly fat for tail fat or for meat is permissible, because their genera are different due to gross difference in forms, essences, and benefits. Commentary: Fat, tail fat, and meat are separate genera. Quduri says it is permissible to sell belly fat for tail fat or meat with disparity. Their difference in genera is obvious. Difference in essences is that each has a distinct reality: one is called shahm, another aliyah, and the third lahm. Difference in benefits is known through medicine. Since they are different genera, exchange with disparity is permissible.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage rules on exchanging belly fat, tail fat, and meat. The Hanafi school deems them different genera because they have distinct forms, definitions, and medical benefits. Therefore, selling them with disparity is permissible. The commentary emphasizes that the difference is 'gross' (fahish), meaning clearly distinct, not subtle. This is consistent with the principle that only items of the same genus fall under riba al-fadl.

Key Terms
شحم البطن (shahm al-batn): Belly fat, a type of fat from animal abdomen.
إلية (iliyah): Tail fat, specifically from sheep.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because disparity is always allowed in meat products
D) Because the Prophet (PBUH) allowed it

Key Takeaway
Belly fat, tail fat, and meat are different genera in Hanafi fiqh, so exchange with disparity is permissible.

Selling Date Vinegar for Grape Vinegar with Disparity
Ruling on permissibility of selling date vinegar for grape vinegar with disparity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits selling date vinegar for grape vinegar with disparity and apply the principle of genus determination to other commodity exchanges.

Core Idea
Vinegars from different fruits are different genera, so disparity in exchange is permissible.

This passage addresses a specific exchange: selling date vinegar for grape vinegar with unequal quantities. The key legal question is whether the two vinegars belong to the same genus (jins) or different genera, because Hanafi rules require equality in weight only if they are the same genus. The ruling here is that they are different, so disparity is allowed. The proof relies on the difference in their origins (dates vs grapes) and is supported by an analogy with goat hair and sheep wool, which are also different genera due to differing purposes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selling date vinegar for grape vinegar with inequality (zayd wa nuqsan). The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz). Note the hukm level: mubah.
2
Locate the underlying principle
The ruling is based on the principle that when two items are from different genera, disparity in exchange is allowed. The passage concludes that date vinegar and grape vinegar are different genera because their origins (dates and grapes) are different.
This is an application of the general rule in riba al-fadl: inequality is only prohibited for same genus items.
3
Analyze the proof: distinction by origin
The proof starts from the difference between dates and grapes. Since they are different fruits, their derived products (syrups, vinegars) are also different genera. The passage mentions 'consensus' that date syrup and grape syrup are different genera.
The reasoning is qiyas: the vinegar takes the genus of its source.
4
Examine the supporting analogy (sheep wool vs goat hair)
The author cites Sahib al-Hidayah: goat's hair and sheep's wool are two genera, even though goats and sheep are of the same species (genus in zoology). Why? Because their purposes differ: wool makes valuable clothing, hair makes coarse items. Thus, purpose (maghsad) determines genus in exchange.
This analogy reinforces that even if origins are similar, differing purposes can separate genera.
5
Apply the principle to new cases
Now you can apply this to other vinegars: e.g., apple vinegar vs date vinegar would also be different genera. Test your understanding by stating whether exchange with disparity is allowed.
Always identify the origin and purpose of each commodity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ کھجو کر سرکہ کو انگور کے سرکہ کے عوض کمی ، زیادتی کے ساتھ فروخت کرنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ جب ان دونوں کی اصل یعنی کھجور اور انگور کے درمیان اختلاف ہے تو ان دونوں کے پانی یعنی سرکوں میں بھی اختلاف ہوگا اور جب کھجور اور انگور کے سرکوں میں اختلاف ہے تو کھجور کا سرکہ اور انگور کا سرکہ دو الگ الگ جنس ہو ئیں یہی وجہ ہے کہ کھجور کے شیرے اور انگور کے شیرے میں بالا جماع اختلاف جنس ہے اور پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ اختلاف جنس کی صورت میں کمی ، زیادتی کے ساتھ بیع کرنا جائز ہے اسلئے کھجور کے سرکہ کی بیع انگور کے سرکہ کے عوض متفاضل جائز ہو گی۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ بکری کے بال اور بھیٹر کی اون الگ الگ دو جنس ہیں ۔ اگر چہ خود بکری اور بھیٹر دونوں کی ایک جنس ہے۔ بال اور بھیڑ دو جنس اسلئے نہیں کہ ان کے مقاصد میں اختلاف ہے کیونکہ اون سے دوشالہ اور قیمتی کپڑے بنتے ہیں اور بالوں سے کمبل اور رسیاں بنتی ہیں۔ پس جب بال اور اون دو جنس ہیں تو ان کا مبادلہ بھی کمی زیادتی کے ساتھ جائز ہے۔
The issue is that selling date vinegar for grape vinegar with increase or decrease is permissible. Because when there is a difference between their origins, i.e., dates and grapes, then there will also be a difference in their liquids, i.e., vinegars. And when there is a difference between date vinegar and grape vinegar, then date vinegar and grape vinegar are two different genera. This is why there is consensus that date syrup and grape syrup are different genera, and it has passed previously that in case of difference of genus, buying and selling with increase or decrease is permissible. Therefore, selling date vinegar for grape vinegar with disparity is permissible. Sahib al-Hidayah says: Goat's hair and sheep's wool are two different genera, even though goat and sheep themselves are of one genus. Hair and wool are not one genus because their purposes differ: wool is used for shawls and expensive clothes, and hair for blankets and ropes. So when hair and wool are two genera, their exchange with increase or decrease is also permissible.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the permissibility of selling date vinegar for grape vinegar with disparity. The reasoning is based on the principle that when the origins (dates and grapes) are different, their derived products (vinegars) are also different genera. This is supported by the analogy of goat's hair and sheep's wool: although goats and sheep are the same genus in terms of species, their hair and wool are different due to differing purposes and benefits. Therefore, disparity in exchange is permitted.

Key Terms
خل (khal): Vinegar, specifically the product of dates or grapes
جنس (jins): Genus or type; in fiqh of exchange, determines whether equality in weight is required

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on selling date vinegar for grape vinegar with disparity?
A) Not permissible because both are vinegar
B) Permissible because they are different genera
C) Permissible only if equal in weight
D) Not permissible under any condition

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the genus of a commodity is determined by its origin and purpose; therefore, date vinegar and grape vinegar are different genera, making disparity in exchange permissible.

Selling Bread for Wheat or Flour with Disparity: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ribawi exchange including salam and qard.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on selling bread for wheat or flour with disparity, including the conditions for sale, salam, and qard, and identify the mufta bihi position among the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
Bread is not measured by volume, so disparity in exchange with wheat is permissible, but Abu Hanifa's rare view prohibits it entirely.

This passage addresses a classic fiqh problem: can bread, which is either counted or weighed, be exchanged for wheat or flour (measured by volume) with disparity? The Hanafi school generally permits it under certain conditions, but a rare tradition from Abu Hanifa holds it invalid. The text also extends the ruling to salam and qard contracts involving bread, revealing nuanced disagreements among the three great imams. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning and the practical fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on selling bread for wheat with disparity.
Identify the general ruling according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the mufta bihi view): it is permissible when both are cash and possession occurs in the session.
2
Identify the minority view and its source.
Abu Hanifa (in nawadir) says it is not permissible at all, based on homogeneity between bread and wheat requiring equality.
3
Analyze the condition of cash (naqd) and credit.
The ruling is when both are cash. If wheat is on credit (salam), it is also permissible. If bread is on credit, it is permissible only according to Abu Yusuf, and the fatwa follows his view.
4
Examine the salam contract in bread.
Salam in bread is valid in the correct view (Abu Yusuf), with the condition that bread is weighed or numerated and its attributes can be described.
5
Examine the qard of bread.
Abu Hanifa prohibits borrowing bread by count or weight due to variation; Muhammad allows it by custom; Abu Yusuf allows by weight but not count.

Source Text

قال ويجوز بيع الخبز بالحنطة والدقيق متفاضلا؛ لأن الخبز صار عدديا أو موزونا فخرج من أن يكون مكيلا من كل وجه والحنطة مكيلة وعن أبي حنيفة أنه لا خير فيه والفتوى على الأول وهذا إذا كانا نقدين فإن كانت الحنطة نسيئة جاز أيضا وإن كان الخبز نسيئة يجوز عند أبي يوسف وعليه الفتوى وكذا السلم في الخبز جائز فى الصحيح ولا خير فى استقراضه عددا أو وزنا عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأنه يتفاوت بالخبز والخباز والتنور والتقدم والتأخر وعند محمد يجوز بهما للتعامل وعند أبي يوسف يجوز وزنا ولا يجوز عددا للتفاوت في آحاده تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ہمارے علمائے ثلاثہ کے نزدیک روٹی کو گندم یا آنے کے عوض کمی ، زیادتی ، کے ساتھ بیچنا جائز ہے بشر طیکہ مجلس میں عوضین پر قبضہ تحقیق ہو جائے کیونکہ روٹی یا تو عددی ہے اور یا وزنی ہے لیکن کیلی نہیں ہے اور گندم کیلی چیز ہے اور اسی طرح آٹا بھی کیلی چیز ہے کیونکہ آٹا، گندم کا جز ہے پس جب گندم اور آٹا کیلی ہوئے اور روٹی غیر کیلی ہوئی تو اتحاد قد رفوت ہونے کی وجہ سے تفاضل جائز ہوگا۔ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ سے نوادر کی روایت یہ ہے کہ روٹی کی بیچ گندم کے عوض یا آنے کے عوض بالکل جائز نہیں ہے نہ مساویا اور نہ متفاضلا۔ یہی قول امام شافعی اور امام احمد کا ہے۔ اس روایت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ روٹی اور گندم یا اسکے آنے میں چونکہ ایک گونہ مجانست موجود ہے اسلئے ان کے مبادلہ میں مساوات اور برابری شرط ہو گی۔ اور روٹی اور گندم اور آئے میں مساوات کا علم چونکہ ممکن نہیں ہے اسلئے ان کا مبادلہ ہی جائز نہ ہوگا۔ لیکن فتویٰ قول اول پر ہے یعنی فتویٰ جواز پر ہے۔ بہر حال جواز بیع اس وقت تھا جبکہ دونوں عوض یعنی روئی اور گندم یا آٹا نقد ہوں اور اگر گندم اور آنا ادھار ہو یعنی روٹی کا ان دونوں میں عقد سلم کیا بایں طور کہ روٹی کو راس المال بنا کر نقد دے دیا اور گندم یا آئے کو مسلم فیہ بنا کر ادھار کیا تو بھی جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ موزونی چیز یعنی روٹی کا عقد سلم ایک ایسی مکیلی چیز یعنی گندم یا آئے میں گیا ہے جس کی صفت اور مقدار کا پہچان لینا ممکن ہے اور اگر روٹی کو ادھار کیا اور گندم یا آٹے کو نقد دے دیا تو امام امام ابو یوسف کے صحیح قول کے مطابق روٹی کے اندر بیع سلم کرنا بھی جائز ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک روٹی کا قرضہ لینا نہ گن کر جائز ہے اور نہ تول کر جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ روٹیاں پکانے کی وجہ سے متفاوت ہوتی ہیں۔ چنانچہ بعض روٹیاں پتلی ہوتی ہیں اور بعض موٹی ہوتی ہیں اور بعض بڑی ہوتی ہیں اور بعض چھوٹی ہوتی ہیں اور اسی طرح پکانے والے کی وجہ سے متفاوت ہوتی ہیں۔ چنانچہ ماہر طباخ کی روٹیاں عمدہ ہوں گی اور اناڑی کے ہاتھ کی پکائی ہوئیں اس قد رعدہ نہ ہوں گی اور خود تنور کی وجہ سے متفاوت ہوتی ہیں چنانچہ نئے تنور کی روٹیاں اچھی ہوتی ہیں اور پرانے کی اس کے مقابلہ میں خراب
He said: And selling bread for wheat and flour with disparity is permissible because bread has become numerated or weighed, so it has exited from being measured by volume in every respect, while wheat is measured by volume. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that there is no good in it, but the fatwa is on the first [view]. And this is when both are cash. If the wheat is on credit, it is also permissible. And if the bread is on credit, it is permissible according to Abu Yusuf, and on it is the fatwa. Similarly, salam in bread is permissible in the correct view, and there is no good in borrowing it by number or weight according to Abu Hanifa because it varies by bread and baker and oven and being early or late. According to Muhammad, it is permissible with both due to customary practice. According to Abu Yusuf, it is permissible by weight but not by number due to variation in its individual items. Explanation: The form of the issue is that according to our three imams, selling bread for wheat or flour with increase or decrease is permissible, provided that possession of both items takes place in the session, because bread is either numerated or weighed but not measured by volume, and wheat is measured by volume, and similarly flour is measured by volume because flour is a part of wheat. So when wheat and flour are measured by volume and bread is not, then disparity is permissible due to the loss of unity of measure. From Imam Abu Hanifa, a rare transmission (nawadir) states that selling bread for wheat or flour is absolutely not permissible, neither equally nor with disparity. This is also the view of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad. The proof of this transmission is that because between bread and wheat or its flour there is a type of homogeneity, so equality in exchange is required. And since equality between bread and wheat or flour cannot be known, their exchange is not permissible at all. But the fatwa is on the first view, i.e., the view of permissibility. In any case, the permissibility of sale is when both items, i.e., bread and wheat or flour, are cash. And if wheat or flour is on credit, meaning a salam contract is made with bread as the capital (paid immediately) and wheat or flour as the subject matter (delayed), it is also permissible because the salam of a weighed item (bread) is in a measured item (wheat/flour) whose description and quantity can be known. And if bread is on credit and wheat or flour is cash, it is permissible according to Abu Yusuf because according to him, bread is a weighed item and salam in a weighed item is permissible. So salam in bread is permissible. This is the view of fatwa. Sahib al-Hidayah says that according to the correct view of Abu Yusuf, salam in bread is permissible. Sahib al-Hidayah says that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, borrowing bread by count or weight is not permissible because bread varies due to baking. Some breads are thin, some thick, some big, some small; similarly, they vary due to the baker; a skilled baker's bread will be good while an unskilled baker's will not be; and they vary due to the oven; new oven's bread is good while old oven's is bad.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage is a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute on the permissibility of selling bread for wheat or flour with disparity. The general ruling, supported by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (and the relied-upon position), is that it is permissible when both items are handed over in the session, because bread is not measured by volume (kayl) but by number or weight, while wheat and flour are measured by volume. There is a rare transmission from Abu Hanifa that it is not permissible at all due to the similarity between bread and wheat, but the fatwa is on the permissibility view. The passage also discusses the salam contract with bread as capital or subject matter, and the borrowing (qard) of bread, with differences among the three imams.

Key Terms
خبز (khubz): Bread, considered in fiqh as either counted (adadi) or weighed (wazni)
حنطة (hintah): Wheat, a commodity measured by volume (kayl)
دقيق (daqeeq): Flour, considered a part of wheat and also measured by volume
سلم (salam): A sale where the price is paid in advance and the goods are delivered later
قرض (qard): Loan, borrowing of fungible items expected to be returned with similars

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, is selling bread for wheat with disparity permissible?
A) No, because they are similar
B) Yes, but only if both are cash and possession occurs in the session
C) Yes, without any conditions
D) No, because bread is not measured by volume

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits selling bread for wheat or flour with disparity as long as they belong to different measurement categories and the transaction is spot, unless structured as salam.

Selling Bread for Wheat or Flour with Excess: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains permissibility and Hanafi imams' differences on selling bread for wheat/flour

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling bread for wheat with excess, explain the differences among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, and identify the mufta bihi position for sale, salam, and loan.

Core Idea
Bread is not a measure (kayl) like wheat, so excess is allowed — but permissibility is qualified by conditions and disagreement among the Hanafi imams.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a practical question: can you sell bread for wheat with an excess? At first glance, both are food grains, so riba may be suspected. However, the Hanafi school distinguishes between items sold by measure (kayl) and those sold by count or weight. Bread has left the category of kayl, so excess is allowed. But the three primary imams differ on the details, especially when credit or loans are involved. Understanding these nuances is essential for valid transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue and the general ruling
The issue is selling bread (a non-kayli item) for wheat/flour (kayli items) with an excess. The general Hanafi ruling: permissible, because bread is no longer a measure.
2
Trace the basis of the ruling: the shift from kayl to adad/wazn
Understand that bread, after processing, is sold by count or weight, not measured by volume. This removes it from the same ribawi category as wheat, so excess is allowed.
The key principle: riba only applies when both items share the same 'illah of measurement (kayl) or weight (wazn) and are of the same genus.
3
Map the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
List the views: Abu Hanifa (nawadir) prohibits absolutely (sale, salam, loan). Abu Yusuf allows by weight only, not by count. Muhammad allows by both count and weight due to custom.
The fatwa follows the first opinion (permissibility) for sale. For salam, Abu Yusuf's weight-only view is mufta bihi. For loan, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ, with no single mufta bihi stated.
4
Apply the ruling to specific transactions: spot sale, salam, and loan
Spot sale: permissible if both considerations are taken in the session. Salam (bread as capital, wheat as subject matter): permissible according to Abu Yusuf (weight) and Muhammad (both). Loan of bread: Abu Hanifa prohibits entirely; Muhammad allows both; Abu Yusuf allows only by weight.
The variation in bread due to baking etc. makes it not a standard item (dhat al-mithal), affecting loan validity.
5
State the practical outcome and mufta bihi
The mufta bihi for sale is permissibility. For salam, Abu Yusuf's view (weight) is relied upon. For loan, the text does not fix a single fatwa, but custom (ta'amul) is considered.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi can transact these exchanges while Shafi'i/Hanbali cannot.

Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary on Hidaya, Volume 8. Book of Sales. And [the matter of] the oven and precedence and delay. According to Muhammad, it is permissible by both [counting and weighing] due to customary practice. According to Abu Yusuf, it is permissible by weight, not by count, due to variation in its individual units. Translation: And selling bread for wheat or flour with excess is permissible because bread has become of counting or weighing type, hence bread has exited from being a measure (kayl) in every respect, and wheat is a measure. And from Abu Hanifa it is narrated that there is no good in it, and the fatwa is on the first opinion. This ruling is when both considerations are spot. Then if the wheat is on credit, it is also permissible. And if the bread is on credit, it is permissible according to Abu Yusuf, and upon that is the fatwa. Similarly, selling bread as a salam (forward sale) is permissible according to the correct opinion of Abu Yusuf. And according to Abu Hanifa, taking bread as a loan by count or weight has no good, because bread varies due to baking, the baker, the oven, and precedence and delay. According to Imam Muhammad, due to customary practice, it is permissible by both count and weight. According to Abu Yusuf, it is permissible by weight, not by count, due to variation in its individual units. Elaboration: The issue is that according to our three imams, selling bread for wheat or flour with excess is permissible, provided that the two considerations are taken possession of in the session, because bread is either by count or weight, not a measure, and wheat is a measure, similarly flour is a measure because flour is a part of wheat. So when wheat and flour are measures and bread is not a measure, due to the absence of unity of measure, excess is permissible. From Imam Abu Hanifa, a rare transmission (nawadir) is that selling bread for wheat or flour is absolutely not permissible, neither equally nor with excess. This is also the opinion of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad. The proof of this transmission is that because there is a kind of similarity (jinsiyyah) between bread and wheat or flour, equality is required in their exchange, and since equality between bread and wheat is not knowable, their exchange is not permissible. But the fatwa is on the first opinion, i.e., the fatwa is on permissibility. Anyway, permissibility of sale is when both considerations, i.e., bread and wheat or flour, are spot. And if the wheat or flour is on credit, meaning a salam contract is made with bread as the capital delivered spot and wheat/flour as the subject matter on credit, it is also permissible, because a salam contract of a weighable item (bread) is made for a measurable item (wheat/flour) whose description and quantity can be known. And if the bread is made on credit and wheat/flour is given spot, it is permissible according to Imam Abu Yusuf because according to him bread is a weighable item and salam is permissible in weighable items, so salam in bread is permissible. Upon this opinion is the fatwa. The author of Hidaya says that according to the correct opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf, salam in bread is also permissible. The author of Hidaya said that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, taking bread as a loan is not permissible by count nor by weight, because breads vary due to baking: some breads are thin, some thick, some large, some small; similarly due to the baker: a skilled cook's bread will be fine while an amateur's will not be as good; due to the oven itself: new oven's bread is good, old oven's is bad; due to precedence and delay: the first breads after lighting the oven are not very good, while the later ones are fine. So when there is such variation in breads, they are not among items of similar quality (dhawat al-amthal), and when they are not among them, taking them as a loan is not permissible. According to Imam Muhammad, due to people's custom, taking bread as a loan is permissible by both count and weight. According to Abu Yusuf, it is permissible by weight but not by count – by weight because breads are weighable according to him, and not by count because of great variation in individual units, leading to dispute at repayment.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the permissibility of selling bread for wheat or flour with excess (تفاضل). The passage type is an intra-Hanafi dispute combined with a ruling statement. The author, Ashraf al-Hidaya, is commenting on the matn of al-Hidaya, expanding on the views of the three primary Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The core issue is whether bread and wheat are of the same genus (jins) such that riba rules apply, or whether they differ in measure (kayl) so that excess is allowed. The relied-upon opinion (mufta bihi) is that selling bread for wheat with excess is permissible, provided both are spot or, if one is deferred, specific conditions are met. The passage details the reasons: bread is either sold by count or weight, not by measure (kayl), while wheat is a measure, so they are not of the same type (jins), thus excess is allowed. However, a rare narration (nawadir) from Abu Hanifa holds it impermissible due to similarity (jinsiyyah). The fatwa follows the permissibility opinion. The passage also discusses salam (forward sale) and loans of bread, showing that Abu Yusuf allows salam and loans by weight, while Muhammad allows by both count and weight due to custom, and Abu Hanifa prohibits loans entirely due to variation in breads. The key legal reasoning (talil) is that bread is not a standard item (dhat al-mithal) because of variability in baking, baker, oven, and time, so it cannot be loaned reliably. The mufta bihi for salam is Abu Yusuf's view allowing it by weight.

Key Terms
ربی (riba): Usury or interest, particularly in exchange transactions where excess or delay occurs in specific items.
کیلی (kayli): Measured by volume (a ribawi category). Wheat and flour are kayli.
عدد (adad): Counting (number) as a means of determining quantity for items not measured by volume or weight.
قرض (qard): Loan of fungible items that are to be repaid in kind. The conditions for a valid qard include that the item must be dhat al-mithal (standardized).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon opinion (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, is it permissible to sell bread for wheat with excess (تفاضل) when both are delivered immediately?
A) Yes, it is permissible because bread is not a measure like wheat.
B) No, it is impermissible because bread and wheat are of the same kind.
C) Yes, but only if the bread is weighed, not counted.
D) No, because excess in any exchange of food items is prohibited.

Key Takeaway
Selling bread for wheat or flour with excess is permissible in the Hanafi school because bread is not a measure (kayl), but the permissibility is subject to conditions of spot exchange or valid salam, and the imams differ on loans and salam details.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
No Riba Between Master and Slave: Conditions and Intra-Hanafi Nuance
Ruling with proof on riba between master and slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which riba applies between a master and his authorized slave, explain the intra-Hanafi difference on the legal basis, and apply the ruling to new scenarios.

Core Idea
Unity of ownership suspends riba, but slave's debts break that unity.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a subtle fiqh question: can riba occur between a master and his own slave? At first glance, the answer is no, because the slave's property belongs to the master, so any exchange is not a real sale. However, the ruling changes when the slave has debts. We will explore the reasoning behind this exception and the nuanced differences among the Hanafi masters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling
State the general rule: no riba between master and slave. Understand the underlying reason: the slave and his property belong to the master, so a sale is not truly between two independent parties.
This is the default position when conditions are met.
2
List the conditions for the rule
Find the two conditions mentioned: (1) the slave must be authorized for trade (ma'dhun lahu), and (2) the slave must have no debts that cover his value. Both must be present for the rule to apply.
If either condition is missing, the ruling changes.
3
Identify the exception
When the slave has debts that equal or exceed his value, the ruling flips: riba applies by consensus (bil-ittifaq). Understand why: the master becomes like a stranger (ajnabi) regarding the slave's property.
This is the mufta bihi position.
4
Analyse the intra-Hanafi difference
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that when debts cover the slave's value, the property is no longer owned by the master. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that it remains the master's property but creditors' rights are attached. Both agree on the outcome but differ on the legal reason (illa).
This difference in usul does not affect the final ruling.
5
Apply to analogous cases
Consider the analogy with a mukatab (slave under contract of manumission). The passage notes that riba is realized between master and mukatab, just as when the slave has debts. Recognise the principle: any separation of ownership (even partial) triggers riba.
This reinforces the concept of 'ajnabi' (stranger).

قال ولا ربا بين المولى وعبده؛ لأن العبد وما في يده ملك لمولاه فلا يتحق الربا وهذا إذا كان مأذونا له ولم يكن عليه دين وان كان عليه دين لايجوز بالاتفاق ؛ لأن ما في يده ليس ملك المولى عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما تعلق به حق الغرماء فصار كالأجنبى فيتحقق الربا كما يتحقق بينه وبين مكاتبه
ترجمہ اور مولی اور اسکے غلام کے درمیان سود نہیں ہے کیونکہ غلام اور جو کچھ اس کے قبضہ میں ہے اپنے مولیٰ کی ملک ہے اسلئے سود محقق نہ ہوگا اور یہ اس وقت ہے جبکہ غلام ماذون لہ ہو اور اس پر قرضہ نہ ہو۔ اور اگر اس پر قرضہ ہو تو بالا تفاق جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک جو کچھ غلام کے قبضہ میں ہے وہ مولیٰ کی ملک نہیں ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اس کے ساتھ قرض خواہوں کا حق متعلق ہے۔ پس مولی بمنزلہ اجنبی کے ہو گیا۔ پس ریو امتحقق ہوگا۔ جیسا کہ مولیٰ اور اس کے مکاتب کے درمیان متحقق ہوتا ہے۔

No riba between master and slave. He said: And there is no riba between the master and his slave because the slave and whatever is in his possession are the property of his master, so riba is not realized. And this is when [the slave] is authorized [for trade] and has no debt upon him. And if he has a debt upon him, it is not permissible by consensus; because what is in his possession is not the property of the master according to Abu Hanifa, and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the right of the creditors is attached to it. So the master becomes like a stranger, thus riba is realized, just as it is realized between him and his mukatab (slave under contract of manumission). Translation: And there is no usury between the master and his slave, because the slave and whatever is in his possession belong to his master, so usury is not realized. This is when the slave is authorized [for trade] and has no debt upon him. And if he has a debt, it is not permissible by consensus, because according to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is in the slave's possession is not the master's property, and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the right of the creditors is attached to it. So the master becomes like a stranger, thus usury is realized, just as it is realized between the master and his mukatab. Elaboration: The issue is that if the slave is authorized for trade and does not have a debt on him that covers his value, then between this slave and his master, riba is not established. That is, among ribawi principles, if these two buy and sell with excess, it will not be riba. For example, Khalid gave his slave wealth and permitted him to trade, then the slave bought two mans of wheat for one man of wheat – this will not be riba, because the slave and whatever wealth is in his possession are all the property of his master. So when the slave and what is in his possession are the master's property, then a sale between the master and this slave is not even realized, and when a sale is not realized, riba is also not established. And if the slave has a debt on him that covers his value, then between this slave and his master, buying and selling among ribawi items with excess is not permissible by consensus. Because in this case, what is in the slave's possession is, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, not the master's property, and according to the two, even though it is the master's property, the right of the creditors is attached to it. In any case, according to Imam Abu Hanifa and the two, the slave has become like a stranger for his master. And between two strangers, a sale is realized, and when a sale is realized, if the condition of riba is found, riba will also be realized, just as between a master and his mukatab, a sale is realized and riba is also realized.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) regarding riba between a master (mawla) and his slave. The matn states that there is no riba between them because the slave and his property belong to the master, so a sale transaction is not truly between two parties. However, this applies only when: (1) the slave is authorized for trade (ma'dhun lahu fi al-tijarah), and (2) he does not have debts that encumber his value. If the slave is indebted such that his debts cover his value (i.e., his market value is consumed by debts), then the ruling changes: riba is realized and such a sale is impermissible by consensus (bil-ittifaq). The reason for this change is that, according to Abu Hanifa, when the slave is in debt, his property is no longer the master's property; according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), although it remains the master's property, the creditors' rights are attached to it, effectively making the master a third party (ajnabi) relative to the slave's property. Thus, a genuine sale occurs, and riba rules apply. The passage gives an example: if the master and his authorized slave (with no debts) exchange two mans of wheat for one man, it is not riba. But if the slave has debts, it is prohibited. This is intra-Hanafi in the sense that the two imams differ in the legal reason (ownership vs. attachment of creditors' rights) but both agree on the outcome. The passage also analogizes to the case of a mukatab (a slave under a contract of manumission), where riba is realized between master and mukatab.

Key Terms
مولی (mawla): Master, the owner of the slave.
عبد مأذون له (abd ma'dhun lahu): A slave who is authorized by his master to engage in trade. The slave's property is considered the master's, but the slave has the capacity to contract.
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of manumission (kitabah) with his master, agreeing to pay a sum for freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does riba become applicable in transactions between a master and his authorized slave?
A) Never, because the slave's property belongs to the master.
B) Only when the slave is not authorized for trade.
C) When the slave has debts that equal or exceed his value.
D) When the transaction is by weight rather than count.

Key Takeaway
No riba between master and authorized slave unless the slave's debts consume his value, making the master a stranger.

Riba in Dar al-Harb: The Hanafi Exception
Ruling that riba does not apply between Muslim and Harbi in Dar al-Harb with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on riba between a Muslim and a harbi in Dar al-Harb, explain the proofs, and evaluate the inter-madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
In Dar al-Harb, riba does not apply between Muslim and Harbi—explicit hadith overrides qiyas.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a unique exception to the general prohibition of riba. While riba is strictly forbidden in Dar al-Islam, the Hanafi school holds that it is permissible between a Muslim and a harbi (enemy non-Muslim) in Dar al-Harb (enemy territory). This ruling, based on a specific hadith and the principle that harbi property is mubah (permissible to take), contrasts with the view of other schools and even a leading Hanafi scholar, Imam Abu Yusuf. Understanding this dispute reveals how textual evidence and contextual reasoning interact in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the Issue
Identify the contested ruling: whether riba applies between a Muslim and a harbi when both are in Dar al-Harb, especially when the Muslim has entered with aman (safe conduct).
The core question: can a Muslim sell one ribawi item for two of the same kind to a harbi in enemy territory?
2
Identify the Hanafi Position and Its Dalil
The Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad) holds that no riba exists in this scenario. Their primary proof is the prophetic hadith: 'La riba bayna al-muslim wa al-harbi fi dar al-harb.' Also, harbi property in Dar al-Harb is mubah, so taking it with excess is permissible as long as there is no treachery.
The hadith is explicit (qati' al-dalala) and takes precedence over analogical reasoning.
3
Identify the Opposing Position and Its Dalil
Imam Abu Yusuf (within Hanafi school) and Imam al-Shafi'i (also Malik, Ahmad) argue that riba applies. They draw an analogy (qiyas) to the case of a musta'min (harbi with aman) in Dar al-Islam, where riba is unanimously prohibited. They say the same should apply when a Muslim enters Dar al-Harb with aman.
Opponents use qiyas, considering the presence of aman as the operative cause (illah) for prohibition.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The Hanafis respond with two points: (1) The explicit hadith overrides qiyas; (2) The underlying rationale differs: the harbi's property in Dar al-Harb is mubah (not protected), while the musta'min's property becomes protected by the aman contract. Therefore, the analogy is flawed.
The distinction: mubah property can be taken in any manner without incurring riba, but protected property cannot.
5
Conclude with Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf): According to the Hanafi school, a Muslim may sell one dirham for two dirhams to a harbi in Dar al-Harb. According to the opposing view, this transaction is prohibited as riba.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is the majority view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, based on the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا بين المسلم والحربى فى دار الحرب خلافا لأبي يوسف والشافعى لهما الاعتبار بالمستامن منهم فى دارنا ولنا قوله عليه السلام لاربو بين المسلم والحربى فى دار الحرب؛ ولأن مالهم مباح في دارهم فبأي طريق أخذه المسلم أخذ مالا مباحا إذا لم يكن فيه غدر بخلاف المستأمن منهم؛ لأن ماله صار محظورا بعقد الأمان
ترجمہ اور دار الحرب میں مسلمان اور حربی کے درمیان ربوا نہیں ہے امام ابو یوسف اور امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے ان دونوں حضرات نے اس پر قیاس کیا ہے جو ہر بیوں میں سے ہمارے دار الاسلام میں امان لے کر آیا ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ دارالحرب میں مسلمان اور حربی کے درمیان ربوا نہیں ہے اور اسلئے کہ حربیوں کا مال ان کے کردار میں مباح ہے پس مسلمان اسکو جس طریقہ سے لے گا مال مباح کو لے گا۔ بشرطیکہ اس میں دھوکہ نہ ہو۔ برخلاف امان لے کر آنے والے کے کیونکہ عہد امان کی وجہ سے اس کا مال ممنوع ہو گیا ہے۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ دار الحرب میں مسلمان اور حربی کے درمیان ربوانہیں ہے یعنی اگر کوئی مسلمان امان لے کر دار الحرب میں گیا اور کسی حربی کے ہاتھ ایک درہم دو درہم کے عوض فروخت کیا تو یہ حلال اور جائز ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف اور امام شافعی کے نزد یک مسلمان اور حربی کے درمیان دار الحرب میں ربوا ہوتا ہے۔ یعنی ایک درہم کا دو درہم کے عوض بیچنانا جائز ہے اور یہی قول امام مالک اور امام احمد کا ہے۔ ان حضرات کی دلیل قیاس ہے۔ یعنی اگر تر بی امان لے کر دار الاسلام میں داخل ہوا اور اس نے ایک درہم دو درہم کے عوض بیچا تو یہ بالا تفاق ناجائز ہے۔ پس اسی طرح اگر مسلمان امان لے کر دار الحرب میں داخل ہوا اور اس نے یہ کام کیا یعنی ایک درہم دو درہم کے عوض بیچا تو بھی نا جائز ہوگا۔
ہماری دلیل ... رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول لا ربوا بین المسلم والحربی فی دار الحرب ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ دار الحرب میں حربیوں کا مال مباح الاصل اور غیر معصوم ہے اس کو ہر طرح سے لینے کی اجازت ہے بشرطیکہ دھوکہ دے کر نہ لیا ہو ۔ کیونکہ عذر اور دھو کہ حرام ہے۔ برخلاف اس حربی کے جوامان لے کر دار الاسلام میں آیا ہو ۔ کیونکہ اس کا مال عقد امان کی وجہ سے محفوظ ہو گیا ہے۔ اور جب اس کا مال محفوظ ہو گیا تو اس سے زیادہ لینے کی اجازت نہ ہوگی۔ جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
He said: And there is no riba between the Muslim and the Harbi in Dar al-Harb, contrary to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i. For them, they analogize to the musta'min among them in our Dar. For us, we have his saying, peace be upon him: There is no riba between the Muslim and the Harbi in Dar al-Harb. And because their property is permissible (mubah) in their abode, so in whatever way the Muslim takes it, he takes permissible property, provided there is no treachery. Unlike the musta'min among them, because his property becomes prohibited by the covenant of aman. Translation: And in Dar al-Harb, there is no riba between a Muslim and a Harbi; Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Shafi'i differ. They analogize to the musta'min (one who enters with aman) among them in our Dar al-Islam. Our proof is that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: There is no riba between a Muslim and a Harbi in Dar al-Harb. And because the property of Harbis in their abode is mubah (permissible to take). So the Muslim, in whatever way he takes it, takes mubah property, provided there is no treachery. Unlike the musta'min, because his property becomes prohibited due to the covenant of aman. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri says that in Dar al-Harb, there is no riba between a Muslim and a Harbi. That is, if a Muslim enters Dar al-Harb with aman and sells one dirham for two dirhams to a Harbi, it is halal and permissible. According to Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Shafi'i, there is riba between a Muslim and a Harbi in Dar al-Harb. That is, selling one dirham for two dirhams is not permissible. This is also the saying of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad. Their proof is qiyas: if a Harbi enters Dar al-Islam with aman and sells one dirham for two dirhams, it is unanimously impermissible. Similarly, if a Muslim enters Dar al-Harb with aman and does this, it would also be impermissible. Our proof: The saying of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him: 'There is no riba between a Muslim and a Harbi in Dar al-Harb.' The second proof: In Dar al-Harb, the property of Harbis is mubah al-asl (originally permissible) and not inviolable, so it is permitted to take it in any manner provided it is not taken by deceit, because deceit and trickery are haram. Unlike the Harbi who enters Dar al-Islam with aman, because his property becomes protected due to the covenant of aman. When his property becomes protected, taking excess from him is not permitted.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the application of riba between a Muslim and a harbi (non-Muslim at war) in Dar al-Harb (the enemy territory). The Hanafi position, based on a hadith of the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam), is that there is no riba in such a transaction, meaning it is permissible to exchange ribawi items with an excess. The opponents, including Imam Abu Yusuf (within the Hanafi school) and Imam al-Shafi'i, argue by analogy to the case of a musta'min (a harbi who enters Dar al-Islam with a covenant of aman). In that case, riba is prohibited unanimously. They say the same should apply when a Muslim enters Dar al-Harb with aman. The Hanafi response has two pillars: (1) the explicit hadith is the primary evidence, overriding qiyas; (2) the underlying rationale: the harbi's property in Dar al-Harb is mubah (lawfully accessible), so taking it with excess is not considered wrongful riba, as long as there is no deceit. The musta'min's property, by contrast, is protected by the aman contract, so it cannot be taken unjustly. Thus, the Hanafi school permits such transactions, while Shafi'i and others prohibit them.

Key Terms
حربی (ḥarbī): A non-Muslim who is in a state of war with Muslims; no covenant protects his life/property in Dar al-Harb.
مستأمن (musta'min): A non-Muslim who enters Dar al-Islam with a covenant of aman (safe conduct). His property becomes inviolable.
دار الحرب (dār al-ḥarb): Territory under non-Muslim control with which Muslims are in a state of war.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is riba not applicable between a Muslim and a harbi in Dar al-Harb?
A) Because harbis are not obligated to follow Islamic law
B) Because a hadith explicitly states no riba in that context, and harbi property is mubah
C) Because the transaction occurs outside Dar al-Islam
D) Because the Muslim is on a military expedition

Key Takeaway
In Dar al-Harb, the explicit hadith and the mubah status of harbi property override the general prohibition of riba, allowing transactions with excess.

Rights Included in Property Sale: Types of Dwellings and the Zulla Dispute
Definition of rights automatically included in property sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between bayt, manzil, and dar in Hanafi law, and state which subordinates (upper storey, toilet, shed) are automatically included in a sale of each type.

Core Idea
The upper storey is automatically included only in a dar, not in a bayt or manzil; the shed is included only if its entrance lies inside the dar.

This passage from the chapter on Rights (Bāb al-Ḥuqūq) defines the three types of dwellings in Hanafi jurisprudence and clarifies which rights (huquq) enter into a sale without explicit mention. Understanding these classifications is essential for drafting clear property contracts and avoiding disputes. The passage also records an intra-Hanafi disagreement on the inclusion of a shed built over public airspace.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three dwelling types
Parse the definitions of bayt, manzil, and dar as given in the text. Note their key characteristics: bayt is a single room, manzil has multiple rooms and amenities but no courtyard, dar is a larger property with multiple manazil and a courtyard.
These definitions are based on the custom of Arabs and Kufans; regional custom may vary.
2
Apply the rule for inclusion of the upper storey
For each type, state whether the upper storey (ulu) is automatically included. In a dar, it is included as a subordinate (tabi'). In a bayt, it is not included because a bayt and an upper bayt are similar, and one cannot be a subordinate of its like. For a manzil, the ruling is intermediate: due to resemblance to dar, it is included when subordinates are mentioned; due to resemblance to bayt, it is not included without explicit mention.
Customary practice in the commenter's region includes the upper storey in all dwellings because every dwelling is called 'khana' and typically has an upper part.
3
Examine the inclusion of the toilet (kanif)
The toilet is always included as a subordinate of the dar, just like the upper storey.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on the shed (zulla)
According to Abu Hanifa, the zulla (a shed built over the airspace of a road) is not included in the sale unless explicitly mentioned, because it takes the ruling of the road. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if its entrance (maftah) is inside the dar, it is included automatically as a subordinate, similar to the toilet.
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of the Sahibayn, as it aligns with custom and convenience.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The text indicates that the view of the Sahibayn (inclusion if entrance inside) is the operative ruling. The author of the sharh supports this by analogy with the toilet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایت جلد هشتم
باب الحقوق
ترجمہ یہ باب حقوق کے بیان میں ہے
كتاب البيوع
تشریح حقوق، حق کی جمع ہے اس سے وہ حقوق مراد ہیں جو مبیع کے تابع ہو کر بغیر ذکر کے مبیع میں داخل ہوتے ہیں۔ علامہ ابن الہمام نے فرمایا کہ اس باب کو باب خیار سے پہلے ذکر کرنا مناسب تھا مگر چونکہ مصنف نے جامع صغیر کی ترتیب پر کتاب کو مرتب کیا ہے اسلئے باب الربط کے بعد باب الحقوق کو ذکر کیا ہے۔ دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ حقوق توابع ہیں اور توابع کا ذکر متبوع کے بعد ہوتا ہے۔ اسلئے مسائل بیوع کے بعد حقوق کا ذکر کیا گیا ہے۔
بیت، چہار دیواری، چھت اور دروازہ کا نام ہے جس میں رات گزاری جا سکے۔ ہمارے زمانہ میں اس کو کوٹھری اور کمرہ اور حجرہ کہتے ہیں۔ منزل اس سے بڑھ کر جس میں چند کمرے ہوں اور باورچی خانہ اور پائخانہ ہو مگر اس میں صحن نہیں ہوتا ہے اور دار جس میں چند منزل ہوں۔ یہ تفصیل اہل عرب اور اہل کوفہ کے عرف کے مطابق ہے لیکن ہمارے یہاں سب کو فاری میں خانہ اور اردو میں گھر کہا جاتا ہے۔ کسی نے اوپر کی منزل خریدی اس کے واسطے اوپر کی منزل مکمل تب ہوگی کہ ہر حق مع المرافق خریدے
ومن اشترى منزلا فوقه منزل فليس له الاعلى الا ان يشتريه بكل حق هو له او بمرافقه او بكل قليل وكثير هو فيه او منه ومن اشترى بيتا فوقه بيت بكل حق هو له لم يكن له الاعلى ومن اشترى دارا بحدودها فله العلو والكنيف جمع بين المنزل والبيت والدار فاسم الدار ينتظم العلو لانه اسم لما ادير عليه الحدود والعلو من توابع الاصل واجزائه فيدخل فيه والبيت اسم لما يبات فيه والعلو مثله والشيء لا يكون تبعا لمثله فلا يدخل فيه الا بالتنصيص عليه والمنزل بين الدار والبيت لانه يتاتى فيه مرافق السكنى مع ضرب قصور اذ لا يكون فيه منزل الدواب فلشبهه بالدار يدخل العلو فيه تبعا عند ذكر التوابع ولشبهه بالبيت لا يدخل فيه بدونه وقيل في عرفنا يدخل الغلو في جميع ذالك لان كل مسكن يسمى بالفارسية خانه ولا يخلو عن علو وكما يدخل العلو في اسم الدار يدخل الكنيف لانه من توابعه ولا يدخل الظلة الا بذكر ما ذكرنا عند ابي حنيفة لانه مبنى على هواء الطريق فاخذ حكمه وعندهما ان كان مفتحه فى الدار يدخل من غير ذكر شيء مما ذكرنا لانه من توابعه فشابه الكنيف
ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نے ایسی منزل خریدی جس کے اوپر منزل ہے تو اس کے واسطے اوپر کی منزل نہ ہوگی مگر جبکہ نیچے والی منزل کو مع ہر حق کے جو اسکے واسطے ثابت ہے یا مع مرافق کے یا مع ہر قلیل و کثیر کے جو آسمیں ہے یا اس سے ہے خریدے اور اگر کسی نے ایسا بیت جس پر دوسرا بیت ہے مع ہر حق کے جو اس کے واسطے ثابت ہے خریدا تو بالائی بیت اس کے واسطے نہیں ہوگا اور اگر کسی نے ایک دار مع اس کے حدود کے خریدا تو بالائی بیت اس کے واسطے نہیں ہوگا۔ اور اگر کسی نے ایک دار مع اس کے حدود کے خریدا تو مشتری
Translation: This chapter is about rights (huquq). Commentary: Huquq is the plural of haqq. Here it refers to rights that follow the sold item (mabi') and enter into it without explicit mention. Ibn al-Humam said it would have been more appropriate to mention this chapter before the chapter on khiyar, but since the author arranged the book according to the order of al-Jami' al-Saghir, he placed this chapter after the chapter on riba. Another answer: Rights are subordinate (tawabi'), and subordinates are mentioned after the principal. Therefore, rights are mentioned after issues of sales. Bayt: the name for a structure with four walls, a roof, and a door where one can spend the night. In our time it is called a room (kothri/ghar). Manzil: larger, containing several rooms, a kitchen, and a toilet, but without a courtyard. Dar: containing several manazil. This detail is according to the custom of Arabs and Kufans. In our region, all are called 'khana' in Farsi and 'ghar' in Urdu. If someone buys a lower manzil, the upper manzil is not included unless he buys it with all rights (bi kulli haqq) or with its amenities (marafiq) or with everything. And whoever buys a manzil above which is another manzil, he does not have the upper storey unless he buys it with every right that belongs to it or with its amenities or with every small and big thing that is in it or from it. And whoever buys a bayt above which is another bayt with every right that belongs to it, he does not have the upper bayt. And whoever buys a dar with its boundaries, he has the upper storey and the toilet. A comparison between manzil, bayt, and dar: the name dar includes the upper storey because it is a name for what is enclosed by boundaries, and the upper storey is a subordinate (tabi') of the original and its parts, so it is included. Bayt is a name for what is slept in, and the upper storey is similar to it; a thing does not become a subordinate of its like, so it is not included without explicit mention. Manzil is between dar and bayt because it includes amenities of dwelling with some deficiency, as it does not have a stable for animals. Due to its resemblance to dar, the upper storey enters as a subordinate when subordinates are mentioned; due to its resemblance to bayt, it does not enter without mention. It is said in our custom that the upper storey enters in all such cases because every dwelling is called 'khana' in Farsi and is not free of an upper storey. Just as the upper storey is included in the name dar, the toilet (kanif) is also included because it is a subordinate. The shed (zulla) is not included without explicit mention according to Abu Hanifa because it is built over the air of the road, so it takes its ruling. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if its entrance is inside the dar, it is included without mention because it is a subordinate, similar to the toilet. Translation: And if someone buys a manzil above which is another manzil, he does not have the upper manzil unless he buys it with every right that belongs to it or with its amenities or with every small and big thing that is in it or from it. And if someone buys a bayt above which is another bayt with every right that belongs to it, he does not have the upper bayt. And if someone buys a dar with its boundaries, he has the upper storey and the toilet.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on 'Rights' (Bāb al-Ḥuqūq) defines the legal terms for types of dwellings and explains which parts are automatically included when buying a property. The author first defines the terms: bayt (a single room), manzil (a dwelling with multiple rooms but no courtyard), and dar (a larger property with several manzil and a courtyard). These definitions are based on the custom ('urf) of the Arabs and Kufans, but the commentator notes that in their region (India), all are simply called 'house' (ghar). The core ruling is about whether an upper storey ('ulu) is included in the sale of a lower property. If someone buys a lower manzil, the upper manzil is not included unless explicitly stated with phrases like 'with every right' or 'with its amenities'. For a bayt, the upper bayt is never included unless explicitly mentioned because bayt and upper bayt are similar and one cannot be a subordinate of its like. For a dar, the upper storey is automatically included because the term dar encompasses all structures within its boundaries, making the upper storey a subordinate (tabi') of the original. The toilet (kanif) is also included as a subordinate. A specific intra-Hanafi dispute arises regarding the zulla (shed or canopy) built over the airspace of the road. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is not included in the sale of the dar without explicit mention because it is built on public airspace and takes a separate ruling. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), if the entrance (maftaḥ) of the shed opens into the dar, it is included automatically as a subordinate, similar to the toilet. The relied-upon position for fatwa is the view of the Sahibayn, as it is more practical.

Key Terms
حقوق (huquq): Rights that are subordinate (tawabi') to the sold item and enter into the sale without explicit mention.
بیت (bayt): A simple dwelling consisting of four walls, a roof, and a door, used for sleeping (a single room).
منزل (manzil): A dwelling larger than a bayt, containing multiple rooms, a kitchen, and a toilet, but without a courtyard.
دار (dar): A large property containing multiple manazil and a courtyard, with defined boundaries.
ظلة (zulla): A shed or canopy built over the airspace of a public road, attached to the dar.
كنيف (kanif): Toilet or latrine, considered a subordinate of the dar and automatically included in its sale.
علو (ulu): Upper storey or upper part of a building.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi law, when is the upper storey automatically included in the sale of a property?
A) Only when the property is a dar
B) In all types of dwellings
C) Only when explicitly mentioned
D) In a manzil but not a dar

Key Takeaway
The type of dwelling (bayt, manzil, dar) determines which subordinates are automatically included in a property sale; the upper storey is automatic only for dar, and the shed is included only if its entrance is inside the dar, per the relied-upon Hanafi view.
