The Ruling on Sale by a Non-Owner (Bay' al-Fuduli): Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Introduces bay' al-fuduli, defines fuduli, and presents Hanafi vs Shafi'i dispute on validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on bay' al-fuduli as a suspended (mawquf) sale, state the Shafi'i counter-argument, and derive the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of the dispute.

Core Idea
A sale by a non-owner is concluded but suspended until the owner's permission; the Hanafi school establishes legal capacity through benefit, not just explicit ownership.

This lesson introduces bay' al-fuduli—a sale by someone who is neither owner, agent, nor executor. The central question is whether such a contract is valid from the outset (though suspended) or void. The Hanafi school holds it is concluded but suspended on the owner's permission (ijazah), while Imam al-Shafi'i holds it is void ab initio due to lack of legal capacity. Understanding the Hanafi proof for establishing capacity via benefit and implied permission is key to grasping the dispute.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds: the sale by a fuduli is concluded (mun'aqid) but suspended (mawquf) on the owner's permission. The owner has the option to authorize or rescind.
This position is also held by Malik and one narration from Ahmad.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the sale is not concluded (lam yan'aqid) because it lacks legal capacity (wilayah shar'iyyah), which can only come from ownership or explicit permission.
Imam Muhammad has a similar narration within the Hanafi school.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i proof: wilayah is required for a valid contract, and it is absent here, so the contract is void (batil) ab initio.
The absence of explicit ownership or permission is considered fatal.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: the contract is a transfer of ownership (tamlik) from a qualified person (ahl) in its proper place (mahall). There is no harm to the owner due to his option; rather, benefit exists for all parties. Legal capacity is established through these benefits and implied permission (dalalah), because a rational owner would permit a beneficial transaction.
The Hanafi proof is based on qiyas and istihsan, not on a direct text.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if the owner later permits, the Hanafi school says the sale is valid retroactively and ownership transfers from the moment of the fuduli's contract. The Shafi'i school says a new contract is needed; the fuduli's sale is void and cannot be revived.
This affects ownership of the item and risk (damān) between the contract and permission.

Source Text

Chapter on the sale of a fuduli. Translation: Chapter on the explanation of sale by a fuduli. Book of Sales. Explanation: 'Fuduli' is with a damma on the fa. In the terminology of the jurists, a fuduli is a person who is neither the principal (asil), nor an agent (wakil), nor a guardian (wasi). Rather, according to the saying of Hadrat Maulana Miraj al-Haq (may his shadow continue), 'fuduli' means an intruder. The author of al-'Inayah said that the dot of the fa is wrong. The appropriateness between this chapter and the chapter on istihqaq is clear, because the sale of a fuduli is one of the cases of istihqaq. Because when the claimant (mustahiqq) says: 'This thing is my property, and the one who sold it to you sold it without my permission,' this is exactly the sale of a fuduli. The ruling of bay' al-fuduli, the viewpoint of Imam al-Shafi'i. He (the author) said: 'And whoever sells the property of another without his command, then the owner has the option: if he wishes, he may authorize the sale, and if he wishes, he may rescind it.' Al-Shafi'i said: 'It is not concluded (la yan'aqid) because it did not issue from a legal capacity (wilayah shar'iyyah), because legal capacity is by ownership or by the permission of the owner, and both are absent. And there is no conclusion except with legal capacity.' Our proof is: It is a transfer of ownership (tasarruf tamlik) and it has issued from the one who is qualified (ahl) and in its proper place (mahall), so it is necessary to hold that it is concluded, because there is no harm to the owner with his option; rather, there is benefit for him, as it saves him the trouble of seeking a buyer and settling the price and other matters. And there is benefit for the contractor (al-aaqid), as his speech is saved from nullity. And there is benefit for the buyer. So legal capacity is established to achieve these considerations. Moreover, permission is established by implication (dilalah), because a rational person permits a beneficial transaction.' Translation: If someone sold another's property without his command, the owner has the option: if he wishes, he may allow the sale, and if he wishes, he may nullify it. Imam al-Shafi'i said that the sale of a fuduli is not concluded, because it did not issue from a legal capacity, because legal capacity is by ownership or by the owner's permission, and both are absent, and without legal capacity there is no conclusion. Our proof is: The sale is an act of transferring ownership, and it issued from the one qualified in its proper place, so it is necessary to say it is concluded. Because with the owner having the option, there is no harm; rather, there is benefit for him. It saves him the hardship of finding a buyer and arranging the price, etc. And there is benefit for the contractor, as his speech is saved from being futile. And there is benefit for the buyer. So legal capacity is established to achieve these considerations. How could it not be concluded, while permission is established by implication? Because every rational person permits a beneficial transaction. Explanation: The case is that if a person sold another's owned property without the owner's permission, the owner has the option: if he wishes, he may authorize the sale, and if he wishes, he may annul it. This is the school of Imam Malik, and it is a narration from Imam Ahmad. Imam al-Shafi'i said that the sale of a fuduli is absolutely not concluded. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, all transactions of a fuduli are invalid (batil). There is also a narration from Imam Muhammad to this effect.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on 'Bay' al-Fuduli' – the sale by an unauthorized person. It defines a fuduli as someone who is neither the owner (asil), nor the agent (wakil), nor the executor (wasi), essentially a stranger who acts without authority. The text notes the connection between this chapter and the previous chapter on istihqaq (claim of ownership), because in both cases a third party asserts ownership over something sold without authorization. The core of the lesson is the dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the legal status of such a sale. The author quotes the Hanafi position (which is also the position of Imam Malik and one narration from Imam Ahmad): the sale is suspended (mawquf) – it is not immediately effective but becomes binding upon the owner's subsequent permission (ijazah). The owner has the option (khiyar) to either authorize or rescind. Imam al-Shafi'i, on the other hand, holds that the sale is void ab initio (la yan'aqid) because it lacks legal capacity (wilayah shar'iyyah), which is derived from ownership or permission, both of which are absent. The Hanafi response provides a rational proof: the transaction is an act of transferring ownership (tamlik), and it has been performed by a competent person (ahl) in its proper place (mahall) – meaning the fuduli is a sane adult who can perform contracts, and the subject matter is property that can be sold. The proof is that there is no harm to the owner since he retains the option to reject it; rather, there is benefit as it saves him the trouble of finding a buyer. Additionally, the fuduli's contract is not completely futile because his words are given effect if the owner approves, and the buyer also benefits. Legal capacity is thus established through these considerations. Moreover, permission is assumed by implication (dilalah) because a rational owner would naturally permit a beneficial transaction. The Urdu commentary clarifies that Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) has a narration agreeing with Shafi'i, considering the sale void, but the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the Hanafi view of suspension. This shows that even within the Hanafi school there is an alternative view, but the majority position is as stated.

Key Terms
فضولی (fuduli): A person who acts without authority; neither owner, agent, nor executor.
ولایت شرعیة (wilayah shar'iyyah): Legal capacity or authority derived from ownership or permission of the owner to conduct a transaction.
إجازة (ijazah): The subsequent permission or ratification by the owner that makes the fuduli's sale effective retroactively.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented, what is the status of a sale by a fuduli before the owner's permission?
A) Void (batil) and cannot be validated.
B) Valid and binding immediately without permission.
C) Concluded but suspended (mawquf) on the owner's permission.
D) Valid only if the buyer is aware of the fuduli's lack of authority.

Key Takeaway
A sale by a non-owner is not void but suspended; the Hanafi school validates it on the basis of benefit and implied permission, unlike the Shafi'i school which requires explicit legal capacity.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

10 min
The Sale by a Non-Owner: Hanafi vs Shafi'i Views
Explains Hanafi ruling on fuduli sale and rebuts Shafi'i objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on bay' al-fuduli and explain the Shafi'i objection and the Hanafi rebuttal using the concept of implicit permission.

Core Idea
A fuduli's sale is not void but suspended – the owner's ratification makes it effective from the start.

The sale of another's property without permission raises a fundamental question: does the contract have any legal effect? Imam Abu Hanifa held that such a sale is concluded but suspended, while Imam al-Shafi'i regarded it as void. This lesson unpacks the proofs and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
Define the fuduli
Identify who is a fuduli: a person who acts without being owner, agent, or guardian. The term literally means 'intermeddler'.
Fuduli is not necessarily fraudulent; his action may be beneficial.
2
State the Hanafi position
The sale is concluded (mun'aqid) but suspended (mawquf) on the owner's ratification. The owner has the option to ratify (ijazah) or annul (faskh).
This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; Imam Muhammad has a narration agreeing with Shafi'i.
3
Present the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the sale is void because it lacks legal capacity (wilayah). Wilayah comes from ownership or explicit permission; both are absent.
The Shafi'i premise: a contract without capacity is void ab initio.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response: (1) The fuduli is a qualified person (ahliyyah) and the object is valuable property (mahall), so the act is from its proper subject in its proper place; (2) Permission is established implicitly (dalalat al-izn) because a rational owner would permit a beneficial transaction.
Implicit permission is derived from the benefit to all parties (owner, fuduli, buyer).

Source Text

ترجمہ اگر کسی نے دوسرے کی ملک کو بغیر اسکے حکم کے فروخت کیا تو مالک کو اختیار ہے چاہے بیچ کی اجازت دے اور چاہے اس کو نسخ کر دے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ فضولی کی بیچ منعقد نہیں ہوتی ہے کیونکہ یہ بیع کسی ولایت شرعیہ سے صادر نہیں ہوئی۔ کیونکہ ولایت شرعیہ ملک سے ہوتی ہے یا مالک کی اجازت سے ہوتی ہے حالانکہ یہ دونوں مفقود ہیں اور بغیر قدرت شرعیہ کے انعقاد نہیں ہوتا اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ بیج مالک کرنے کا تصرف ہے اور یہ اپنے محل میں اپنے اہل سے صادر ہوا ہے۔ اسلئے اس کا انعقاد کا قائل ہونا واجب ہوا کیونکہ مالک کو اختیار دینے کی وجہ سے اس کیلئے اس میں کوئی ضرر نہیں ہے بلکہ اس میں مالک کا نفع ہے۔ چنانچہ اس کو مشتری ڈھونڈنے کی مشقت اور ثمن وغیرہ پھہرانے کی مشقت سے کفایت ہے۔ اور اس میں عاقد کا بھی نفع ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کا کلام لغو ہونے سے بچ گیا اور اس میں مشتری کا بھی نفع ہے۔ پس ان وجوہ کو حاصل کرنے کے پیش نظر قدرت شرعیہ ثابت ہوگئی اور بیع کیوں کر منعقد نہ ہوگی۔ حالانکہ اجازت دلالہ ثابت ہے۔ اسلئے کہ ہر عاقل اپنے نافع تصرف کی اجازت دیتا ہے۔

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی آدمی نے دوسرے کی مملوکہ چیز کو بغیر مالک کی اجازت سے فروخت کر دیا تو مالک کو اختیار ہوگا چاہے تو بیع کی اجازت دے اور چاہے اس کو فتح کر دے۔ یہی امام مالک کا مذہب ہے اور یہی امام احمد کی ایک روایت ہے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ فضولی کی بیچ بالکل منعقد نہیں ہوگی۔ امام شافعی کے نزدیک فضولی کے تمام تصرفات باطل ہوتے ہیں۔ امام محمد کی ایک روایت بھی یہی ہے۔

امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دوسرے کی مملوکہ چیز کی بیع شرعی ولایت سے صادر نہیں ہوتی ہے کیونکہ شرعی ولا بیت یا تو مالک ہونے سے ثبات ہوتی ہے اور یا مالک کی اجازت سے ثابت ہوتی ہے حالانکہ یہاں دونوں موجود نہیں ہیں کیونکہ فضولی نہ تو خود بیع کا مالک ہے اور نہ اس کو مالک کی اجازت حاصل ہے۔ بہر حال فضولی کی بیع شرعی ولایت سے صادر نہیں ہوئی اور جو چیز شرعی ولایت سے ...... صادر نہ ہو وہ منعقد نہیں ہوتی۔ کیونکہ بغیر ولایت شرعیہ اور قدرت شرعیہ کے انعقاد نہیں ہوتا۔ اسلئے فضولی کی بیع بھی منعقد نہ ہوگی۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ بیج مالک کرنے کا تصرف ہے یعنی بیچ کے ذریعہ مشتری کو بیع کا مالک کیا جاتا ہے اور بائع کوشن کا مالک کرنا ہوتا ہے اور یہ تصرف اس کے اہل سے اس کے محل میں صادر ہوا ہے۔ اہل تو اسلئے ہے کہ فضولی عاقل بالغ ہے اور محل اسلئے ہے کہ بیچ کا مل مال متقوم ہوتا ہے۔ اور فضولی کی ملک معدوم ہونے سے مبیع کی مالیت اور تقوم کا معدوم ہونا لازم نہیں آتا پس جب تصرف کرنے والا یعنی فضولی تصرف کا اہل بھی ہے اور جس محل میں تصرف کیا گیا ہے یعنی بیچ وہ صرف کا محل بھی ہے تو بیچ منعقد ہونے میں کیا اشکال ہے۔ اور اس انعقاد بیچ میں مالک اور عاقدین میں کسی کا ضرر بھی نہیں ہے۔ مالک کا ضر ر تو اسلئے نہیں کہ مالک کو قبول کرنے اور نہ کرنے کا اختیار ہے یعنی اگر مالک ضرور محسوس کرے تو بی فسخ کردے اور اگر نفع محسوس کرے تو اجازت دے دے بلکہ مالک کو ایک گونہ نفع ہے اور وہ یہ کہ مالک اپنی مملوکہ چیز فروخت کرنے کیلئے مشتری تلاش کرنے کی مشقت سے نجات پا گیا اور اس طرح ثمن متعین کرنے کی محنت سے بچ گیا اور بیع سے عاجز ہونے کی صورت میں وکیل ڈھونڈھنے سے نجات مل گئی۔ اور انعقاد بیچ میں فضولی کا نفع یہ ہے کہ اس کا کلام لغو ہونے سے بچ گیا ور نہ بیچ منعقد نہ ہونے کی صورت میں اس کا کلام افو ہو جاتا اور مشتری کا نفع اسلئے ہے کہ مشتری نے برضاء ورغبت اس چیز کو خریدنے کا اقدام کیا ہے۔ اگر اس میں مشتری کا کوئی نفع نہ ہوتا تو وہ اقدام نہ کرتا۔ پس ان منافع کو حاصل کرنے کیلئے فضولی کیلئے قدرت شرعیہ اور ولا بیت شرعیہ ثابت ہو جائے گی اور جب فضولی کیلئے قدرت شرعیہ ثابت ہوگئی تو فضولی کی کی ہوئی بیع بھی منعقد ہو جائے گی۔ صاحب ہدایہ امام شافعی کا جواب دیتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں کہ آپ کا یہ کہنا کہ ولایت شرعیہ ملک سے ثابت ہوتی ہے یا ما لک کی اجازت سے ثابت ہوتی ہے اور یہاں دونوں باتیں موجود نہیں ہیں، غلط ہے۔ کیونکہ مالک کی طرف سے اجازت دلالہ ثابت ہے اسلئے کہ اس بیع میں مالک کا نفع ہے اور مالک الحمد اللہ عاقل ہے اور ہر عاقل آدمی نفع بخش تصرف کی اجازت دیتا ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ مالک کی طرف سے فضولی کو اجازت حاصل ہے اور جب فضولی کو قدرت شرعیہ حاصل ہے تو اس کی کی ہوئی بیج بھی منعقد ہو جائے گی۔ مالک کو معقود علیہ کی موجودگی تک اجازت قال وله الإجازة اذا كان المعقود عليه باقيا والمتعاقدان بحالهما لان الاجازة تصرف في العقد فلابد من قیامه و ذالك بقيام العاقدين والمعقود عليه واذا اجاز المالك كان الثمن مملوكا له امانة في يده بمنزلة الوكيل لان الاجازة اللاحقة بمنزلة الوكالة السابقة وللفضولى ان يفسخ قبل الاجازة دفعا للحقوق عن نفسه بخلاف الفضولى فى النكاح لانه معبر محض هذا كان الثمن دينافان كان عرضا معينا انما تصح الاجازة اذا كان العرض باقيا ايضا ثم الاجازة اجازة نقد لا اجازة عقد حتى يكون العرض الثمن مملوكا للفضولي وعليه مثل المبيع ان كان مثليا او قيمته ان لم يكن مثليا لانه شراء من وجه والشراء لا يتوقف على الاجازة و لو هلك المالك لا ينفذ باجازة الوارث فى الفصلين لانه توقف على اجازة المورث لنفسه فلا
Chapter on the sale of a non-owner (fuduli). He said: Whoever sells the property of another without his permission, then the owner has the choice: if he wishes he may ratify the sale, and if he wishes he may annul it. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not concluded because it did not issue from a valid legal capacity (wilaya), for legal capacity is through ownership or the owner's permission, and both are absent, and there can be no conclusion except with legal capacity. Our proof is that it is a transfer of ownership and it issued from its proper subject in its proper place, so it must be considered concluded, for there is no harm to the owner given his option; rather there is benefit for him as it saves him the trouble of seeking a buyer and settling the price, etc. And there is benefit for the contracting party (fuduli) in preserving his words from being void, and there is benefit for the buyer. So legal capacity is established to achieve these objectives. Moreover, permission is established implicitly because a rational person permits a beneficial transaction. The explanation of the issue is that if a person sells another's property without the owner's permission, the owner has the option to ratify or annul. This is the view of Imam Malik and one narration from Imam Ahmad. Imam Shafi'i said the sale is absolutely not concluded; according to him all transactions of a fuduli are invalid. There is also a narration from Imam Muhammad to that effect. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that the sale of another's property does not issue from legal capacity because legal capacity is established either by being the owner or by the owner's permission, and both are absent here; the fuduli is neither the owner nor has the owner's permission. Since the sale did not issue from legal capacity, it is not concluded. Our proof is that the sale is a transfer of ownership: through the sale the buyer becomes owner of the sold item and the seller becomes owner of the price, and this transaction issued from its proper subject in its proper place. The subject is proper because the fuduli is a sane adult; the place is proper because the sold item is valuable property. The fact that the fuduli does not own it does not negate the value and appraisability of the item. So when the person acting (fuduli) is qualified and the object of the transaction is suitable, there is no obstacle to conclusion. Moreover, there is no harm to the owner because he has the choice to accept or reject; indeed there is profit for the owner as he is saved the trouble of finding a buyer, setting the price, and finding an agent if unable to sell. The fuduli benefits because his words are not rendered vain, and the buyer benefits because he acted willingly. To achieve these benefits, legal capacity is established for the fuduli. The commentator of al-Hidayah responds to al-Shafi'i saying: Your statement that legal capacity is through ownership or permission and both are absent is incorrect, because permission is established implicitly—since there is benefit for the owner, and the owner is rational, and every rational person permits a beneficial transaction. So permission is established. Therefore the fuduli has legal capacity and his sale is concluded. The owner has the right to ratify as long as the subject matter remains and the contracting parties are still in their original state. He said: He (the owner) may ratify as long as the subject matter remains and the two contracting parties are in their state, because ratification is a disposition on the contract, so the contract must be extant; that is through the existence of the two parties and the subject matter. If the owner ratifies, the price becomes owned by him as a trust in his hand like an agent, because subsequent ratification is like prior agency. The fuduli may cancel before ratification to avoid liabilities upon himself, unlike the fuduli in marriage because he is merely an intermediary. If the price is a debt (dayn), it is a debt; if it is a specific commodity ('ayn), ratification is valid only if that commodity remains. Then ratification is ratification of the price (cash), not ratification of the contract, so that the commodity is owned by the fuduli, and he owes the like of the sold item if it is fungible (mithli), or its value if not fungible, because it is a purchase in some respect, and purchase is not suspended on ratification. If the owner dies, it is not effective by the ratification of the heir in both cases, because it was suspended on the ratification of the deceased himself, so...
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the sale of another's property without permission (bay' al-fuduli). The Hanafi position, stated by Imam Abu Hanifa and supported by the author of al-Hidayah, is that such a sale is suspended on the owner's ratification (mawquf). The owner has the choice to either ratify (ijazah) or annul (faskh). Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the sale is absolutely void (batil) because it lacks legal capacity (wilayah). The Shafi'i argument is that a valid sale requires either ownership or authorization from the owner; since the fuduli has neither, the sale cannot be concluded. The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) The fuduli is a qualified person (sane adult) and the object is valuable property, so the act is from its proper subject in its proper place, thus it can be concluded; the contract is merely suspended pending ratification. (2) Permission is implicitly established because the owner is rational and would naturally permit a beneficial transaction. Thus the fuduli has implicit legal capacity. The passage then explains the conditions for ratification: the subject matter must still exist, and the contracting parties must be in the same state. If the owner ratifies, the price becomes his property and the fuduli is considered like an agent. The fuduli may cancel the sale before ratification to avoid personal liability. The passage also distinguishes between fuduli in sale and fuduli in marriage: in marriage the fuduli is a mere intermediary. The price if a debt (dayn) remains a debt; if a specific commodity ('ayn), it must still exist for ratification. The fuduli owes the like or value of the sold item because he is considered to have purchased it from himself in a sense. If the owner dies, the heirs cannot ratify because the right of ratification was personal to the deceased. The text then cuts off mid-sentence.

Key Terms
فضولی (fudūlī): A person who acts in a transaction without being the owner, agent, or guardian; an intermeddler or unauthorized agent.
إجازة (ijāzah): Ratification or approval by the owner of a contract made without his prior permission; it makes the contract effective retrospectively.
ولاية شرعية (wilāyah sharʿiyyah): Legal capacity or authority to conduct a transaction; derived from ownership or authorization by the owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the status of a sale by a fuduli (non-owner) before the owner's ratification?
A) Void (batil) from the start
B) Valid (sahih) and binding immediately
C) Suspended (mawquf) pending the owner's ratification
D) Valid only if the fuduli is an agent

Key Takeaway
A fuduli's sale is concluded but suspended; the owner's ratification makes it effective retroactively, based on implicit permission.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Ratification and Its Conditions: Consequences of the Suspended Sale
Details conditions and effects of ratification in fuduli sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for ratification in a fuduli sale and explain the legal consequences of ratification, including the fuduli's liability and the owner's rights.

Core Idea
Ratification retroactively converts the fuduli into an agent, but the subject matter must still exist and the parties must be unchanged.

The fuduli sale is not automatically valid; it requires the owner's ratification under specific conditions. Once ratified, the fuduli's position changes to that of an agent, and he may become liable for the subject matter. This lesson details the rules governing ratification and its effects.

Guided Path
1
List the conditions for valid ratification
Ratification is valid only if the subject matter (al-ma'qud 'alayh) still exists and both contracting parties (the fuduli and the buyer) are still in their original state (i.e., have not died or become incapacitated).
If the subject matter is destroyed or one party dies, ratification is ineffective.
2
Explain the effect of ratification on the price
Upon ratification, the price becomes owned by the owner as a trust in the fuduli's hand, like an agent. The fuduli is then responsible for delivering the price to the owner.
The principle: al-ijazah al-lahiqah ka al-wikalah al-sabiqah.
3
Describe the fuduli's right to cancel before ratification
The fuduli may unilaterally cancel the contract before ratification to avoid personal liability. This is different from the fuduli in marriage, where he is a mere intermediary and cannot cancel.
In sale, the fuduli is considered a principal in some respects; in marriage, he is a pure messenger.
4
Analyze the fuduli's liability after ratification
If the price is a debt (dayn), it remains a debt; if it is a specific commodity ('ayn), ratification is valid only if that commodity still exists. The fuduli owes the like (mithli) or value (qimah) of the sold item because he is considered to have purchased it from himself in a sense.
This is because the fuduli's act is a purchase in some respect (shira' min wajh).

كتاب البيوع
تشریح فضولی، فاء کے ضمہ کے ساتھ ہے فقہاء کی اصطلاح میں فضولی وہ شخص ہے جو نہ اصیل ہو، نہ وکیل ہو اور نہ وصی ہو۔ بلکہ بقول حضرت مولانا معراج الحق صاحب مدظلہ کے فضولی، خواہمخواہ کو کہتے ہیں۔ صاحب عنایہ نے کہا کہ فاء کا تختہ غلط ہے۔ اس فصل اور باب الاستحقاق میں مناسبت ظاہر ہے کیونکہ فضولی کی بیج استحقاق کی صورتوں میں سے ایک صورت ہے۔ کیونکہ مستحق جب یہ کہتا ہے کہ یہ چیز میری ملک ہے اور جس نے تجھ کو فروخت کی ہے بغیر میری اجازت کے فروخت کی ہے۔ بعینہ یہی فضولی کی بیج ہے۔

بیع فضولی کا حکم، امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر
قال و من باع ملک غیره بغیر امره فالمالک بالخيار ان شا اجاز البيع وان شاء فسخ وقال الشافعي لا ينعقد لانه لم يصدر عن ولاية شرعية لانها بالملك او باذن المالک وقد فقدا ولا انعقاد الا بالقدرة الشرعية ولنا انه تصرف تملیک وقد صدر من اهله فى محله فوجب القول بانعقاده اذ لا ضرر فيه للمالك مع تخییره بل فيه نفعه حيث يكفى مؤنة طلب المشترى وقرار الثمن وغيره وفيه نفع العاقد لصون كلامه عن الالغاء وفيه نفع المشتري فيثبت القدرة الشرعية تحصيلا لهذه الوجوه كيف وان الاذن ثابت دلالة لان العاقل ياذن في التصرف النافع

ترجمہ اگر کسی نے دوسرے کی ملک کو بغیر اسکے حکم کے فروخت کیا تو مالک کو اختیار ہے چاہے بیچ کی اجازت دے اور چاہے اس کو نسخ کر دے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ فضولی کی بیچ منعقد نہیں ہوتی ہے کیونکہ یہ بیع کسی ولایت شرعیہ سے صادر نہیں ہوئی۔ کیونکہ ولایت شرعیہ ملک سے ہوتی ہے یا مالک کی اجازت سے ہوتی ہے حالانکہ یہ دونوں مفقود ہیں اور بغیر قدرت شرعیہ کے انعقاد نہیں ہوتا اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ بیج مالک کرنے کا تصرف ہے اور یہ اپنے محل میں اپنے اہل سے صادر ہوا ہے۔ اسلئے اس کا انعقاد کا قائل ہونا واجب ہوا کیونکہ مالک کو اختیار دینے کی وجہ سے اس کیلئے اس میں کوئی ضرر نہیں ہے بلکہ اس میں مالک کا نفع ہے۔ چنانچہ اس کو مشتری ڈھونڈنے کی مشقت اور ثمن وغیرہ پھہرانے کی مشقت سے کفایت ہے۔ اور اس میں عاقد کا بھی نفع ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کا کلام لغو ہونے سے بچ گیا اور اس میں مشتری کا بھی نفع ہے۔ پس ان وجوہ کو حاصل کرنے کے پیش نظر قدرت شرعیہ ثابت ہوگئی اور بیع کیوں کر منعقد نہ ہوگی۔ حالانکہ اجازت دلالہ ثابت ہے۔ اسلئے کہ ہر عاقل اپنے نافع تصرف کی اجازت دیتا ہے۔

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی آدمی نے دوسرے کی مملوکہ چیز کو بغیر مالک کی اجازت سے فروخت کر دیا تو مالک کو اختیار ہوگا چاہے تو بیع کی اجازت دے اور چاہے اس کو فتح کر دے۔ یہی امام مالک کا مذہب ہے اور یہی امام احمد کی ایک روایت ہے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ فضولی کی بیچ بالکل منعقد نہیں ہوگی۔ امام شافعی کے نزدیک فضولی کے تمام تصرفات باطل ہوتے ہیں۔ امام محمد کی ایک روایت بھی یہی ہے۔

امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دوسرے کی مملوکہ چیز کی بیع شرعی ولایت سے صادر نہیں ہوتی ہے کیونکہ شرعی ولا بیت یا تو مالک ہونے سے ثبات ہوتی ہے اور یا مالک کی اجازت سے ثابت ہوتی ہے حالانکہ یہاں دونوں موجود نہیں ہیں کیونکہ فضولی نہ تو خود بیع کا مالک ہے اور نہ اس کو مالک کی اجازت حاصل ہے۔ بہر حال فضولی کی بیع شرعی ولایت سے صادر نہیں ہوئی اور جو چیز شرعی ولایت سے ...... صادر نہ ہو وہ منعقد نہیں ہوتی۔ کیونکہ بغیر ولایت شرعیہ اور قدرت شرعیہ کے انعقاد نہیں ہوتا۔ اسلئے فضولی کی بیع بھی منعقد نہ ہوگی۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ بیج مالک کرنے کا تصرف ہے یعنی بیچ کے ذریعہ مشتری کو بیع کا مالک کیا جاتا ہے اور اور اس انعقاد بیچ میں مالک اور عاقدین میں کسی کا ضرر بھی نہیں ہے۔ مالک کا ضر ر تو اسلئے نہیں کہ مالک کو قبول کرنے اور نہ کرنے کا اختیار ہے یعنی اگر مالک ضرور محسوس کرے تو بی فسخ کردے اور اگر نفع محسوس قال وله الإجازة اذا كان المعقود عليه باقيا والمتعاقدان بحالهما لان الاجازة تصرف في العقد فلابد من قیامه و ذالك بقيام العاقدين والمعقود عليه واذا اجاز المالك كان الثمن مملوكا له امانة في يده بمنزلة الوكيل لان الاجازة اللاحقة بمنزلة الوكالة السابقة وللفضولى ان يفسخ قبل الاجازة دفعا للحقوق عن نفسه بخلاف الفضولى فى النكاح لانه معبر محض هذا كان الثمن دينافان كان عرضا معينا انما تصح الاجازة اذا كان العرض باقيا ايضا ثم الاجازة اجازة نقد لا اجازة عقد حتى يكون العرض الثمن مملوكا للفضولي وعليه مثل المبيع ان كان مثليا او قيمته ان لم يكن مثليا لانه شراء من وجه والشراء لا يتوقف على الاجازة و لو هلك المالك لا ينفذ باجازة الوارث فى الفصلين لانه توقف على اجازة المورث لنفسه فلا
Chapter on the sale of a non-owner (fuduli). He said: Whoever sells the property of another without his permission, then the owner has the choice: if he wishes he may ratify the sale, and if he wishes he may annul it. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not concluded because it did not issue from a valid legal capacity (wilaya), for legal capacity is through ownership or the owner's permission, and both are absent, and there can be no conclusion except with legal capacity. Our proof is that it is a transfer of ownership and it issued from its proper subject in its proper place, so it must be considered concluded, for there is no harm to the owner given his option; rather there is benefit for him as it saves him the trouble of seeking a buyer and settling the price, etc. And there is benefit for the contracting party (fuduli) in preserving his words from being void, and there is benefit for the buyer. So legal capacity is established to achieve these objectives. Moreover, permission is established implicitly because a rational person permits a beneficial transaction. The explanation of the issue is that if a person sells another's property without the owner's permission, the owner has the option to ratify or annul. This is the view of Imam Malik and one narration from Imam Ahmad. Imam Shafi'i said the sale is absolutely not concluded; according to him all transactions of a fuduli are invalid. There is also a narration from Imam Muhammad to that effect. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that the sale of another's property does not issue from legal capacity because legal capacity is established either by being the owner or by the owner's permission, and both are absent here; the fuduli is neither the owner nor has the owner's permission. Since the sale did not issue from legal capacity, it is not concluded. Our proof is that the sale is a transfer of ownership: through the sale the buyer becomes owner of the sold item and the seller becomes owner of the price, and this transaction issued from its proper subject in its proper place. The subject is proper because the fuduli is a sane adult; the place is proper because the sold item is valuable property. The fact that the fuduli does not own it does not negate the value and appraisability of the item. So when the person acting (fuduli) is qualified and the object of the transaction is suitable, there is no obstacle to conclusion. Moreover, there is no harm to the owner because he has the choice to accept or reject; indeed there is profit for the owner as he is saved the trouble of finding a buyer, setting the price, and finding an agent if unable to sell. The fuduli benefits because his words are not rendered vain, and the buyer benefits because he acted willingly. To achieve these benefits, legal capacity is established for the fuduli. The commentator of al-Hidayah responds to al-Shafi'i saying: Your statement that legal capacity is through ownership or permission and both are absent is incorrect, because permission is established implicitly—since there is benefit for the owner, and the owner is rational, and every rational person permits a beneficial transaction. So permission is established. Therefore the fuduli has legal capacity and his sale is concluded. The owner has the right to ratify as long as the subject matter remains and the contracting parties are still in their original state. He said: He (the owner) may ratify as long as the subject matter remains and the two contracting parties are in their state, because ratification is a disposition on the contract, so the contract must be extant; that is through the existence of the two parties and the subject matter. If the owner ratifies, the price becomes owned by him as a trust in his hand like an agent, because subsequent ratification is like prior agency. The fuduli may cancel before ratification to avoid liabilities upon himself, unlike the fuduli in marriage because he is merely an intermediary. If the price is a debt (dayn), it is a debt; if it is a specific commodity ('ayn), ratification is valid only if that commodity remains. Then ratification is ratification of the price (cash), not ratification of the contract, so that the commodity is owned by the fuduli, and he owes the like of the sold item if it is fungible (mithli), or its value if not fungible, because it is a purchase in some respect, and purchase is not suspended on ratification. If the owner dies, it is not effective by the ratification of the heir in both cases, because it was suspended on the ratification of the deceased himself, so...
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the sale of another's property without permission (bay' al-fuduli). The Hanafi position, stated by Imam Abu Hanifa and supported by the author of al-Hidayah, is that such a sale is suspended on the owner's ratification (mawquf). The owner has the choice to either ratify (ijazah) or annul (faskh). Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the sale is absolutely void (batil) because it lacks legal capacity (wilayah). The Shafi'i argument is that a valid sale requires either ownership or authorization from the owner; since the fuduli has neither, the sale cannot be concluded. The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) The fuduli is a qualified person (sane adult) and the object is valuable property, so the act is from its proper subject in its proper place, thus it can be concluded; the contract is merely suspended pending ratification. (2) Permission is implicitly established because the owner is rational and would naturally permit a beneficial transaction. Thus the fuduli has implicit legal capacity. The passage then explains the conditions for ratification: the subject matter must still exist, and the contracting parties must be in the same state. If the owner ratifies, the price becomes his property and the fuduli is considered like an agent. The fuduli may cancel the sale before ratification to avoid personal liability. The passage also distinguishes between fuduli in sale and fuduli in marriage: in marriage the fuduli is a mere intermediary. The price if a debt (dayn) remains a debt; if a specific commodity ('ayn), it must still exist for ratification. The fuduli owes the like or value of the sold item because he is considered to have purchased it from himself in a sense. If the owner dies, the heirs cannot ratify because the right of ratification was personal to the deceased. The text then cuts off mid-sentence.

Key Terms
إجازة (ijāzah): Ratification or approval by the owner of a contract made without his prior permission; it makes the contract effective retrospectively.
معقود عليه (maʿqūd ʿalayh): The subject matter of the contract; in a sale, the item sold.
مثلی (mithlī): Fungible goods – items that can be replaced by like quantity/quality.
قیمی (qīmī): Non-fungible goods – items that are unique and have no exact equivalent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is required for an owner's ratification of a fuduli sale to be valid?
A) The buyer must agree to the ratification.
B) The subject matter must still exist and the contracting parties must be in their original state.
C) The fuduli must confirm the sale.
D) The price must be paid immediately.

Key Takeaway
Ratification requires the subject matter and parties to be intact; it transforms the fuduli into an agent and may impose liability for the item's value.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
12 min
The Fuduli Sale: Hanafi vs Shafi'i on its Conclusion
Inter-madhhab dispute on fuduli sale conclusion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the fuduli sale, explain the Shafi'i objection, and apply the Hanafi rebuttal using the concept of dalalah.

Core Idea
A fuduli sale is concluded but suspended; benefit to the owner implies permission.

This lesson examines a classic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on whether a sale made by a fuduli – one who sells another's property without authorization – is legally concluded. The Shafi'i school holds that such a sale is void ab initio because it lacks legal authority. The Hanafi school argues that the sale is concluded (mun'aqid) but suspended (mawquf) on the owner's ratification, based on the idea that the owner's benefit from the transaction indicates implied permission (dalalah). We will dissect both arguments and understand the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested ruling
State exactly what is in dispute: whether the fuduli sale is legally concluded (mun'aqid) before the owner confirms it.
2
Examine the Shafi'i argument
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that legal authority (wilayah) comes only from ownership or explicit permission. The fuduli has neither, so the sale cannot be concluded.
3
Analyze the Hanafi counter-argument
The Hanafi school responds that the sale is a valid transaction from a qualified person (the fuduli) concerning a suitable object. The owner's benefit implies permission (dalalah), establishing the fuduli's legal authority for the purpose of conclusion.
Focus on the concept of dalalah as an indicator of implicit consent.
4
Understand the Hanafi response to Shafi'i
Al-Hidayah refutes the Shafi'i claim that no permission exists. The owner's rational nature and benefit from the sale indicate that permission is present by indication.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi – the sale is concluded and may become binding upon ratification; Shafi'i – it is void and cannot be ratified.

کرے تو اجازت دے دے بلکہ مالک کو ایک گونہ نفع ہے اور وہ یہ کہ مالک اپنی مملوکہ چیز فروخت کرنے کیلئے مشتری تلاش کرنے کی مشقت سے نجات پا گیا اور اس طرح ثمن متعین کرنے کی محنت سے بچ گیا اور بیع سے عاجز ہے کہ مشتری نے برضاء ورغبت اس چیز کو خریدنے کا اقدام کیا ہے۔ اگر اس میں مشتری کا کوئی نفع نہ ہوتا تو وہ اقدام نہ کرتا۔ پس ان منافع کو حاصل کرنے کیلئے فضولی کیلئے قدرت شرعیہ اور ولا بیت شرعیہ ثابت ہو جائے گی اور جب فضولی کیلئے قدرت شرعیہ ثابت ہوگئی تو فضولی کی کی ہوئی بیع بھی منعقد ہو جائے گی ۔ صاحب ہدایہ امام شافعی کا جواب دیتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں کہ آپ کا یہ کہنا کہ ولایت شرعیہ ملک سے ثابت ہوتی ہے یا ما لک کی اجازت سے ثابت ہوتی ہے اور یہاں دونوں باتیں موجود نہیں ہیں ، غلط ہے۔ کیونکہ مالک کی طرف سے اجازت دلالہ ثابت ہے اسلئے کہ اس بیع میں مالک کا نفع ہے اور مالک الحمد اللہ عاقل ہے اور ہر عاقل آدمی نفع بخش تصرف کی اجازت دیتا ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ مالک کی طرف سے فضولی کو اجازت حاصل ہے اور جب فضولی کو قدرت شرعیہ حاصل ہے تو اس کی کی ہوئی بیج بھی منعقد ہو جائے گی۔ مالک کو معقود علیہ کی موجودگی تک اجازت کا اختیار ہے اور متعاقدین اپنی حالت پر ہوں
Imam al-Shafi'i's argument is that selling another's property is not issued from legal authority because legal authority is established either by ownership or by the owner's permission, and here neither exists because the fuduli is neither the owner nor has permission. Therefore, the fuduli's sale does not issue from legal authority, and what does not issue from legal authority is not concluded. Our argument is that sale is a transaction of transferring ownership, and this transaction has issued from a qualified person (fuduli is sane and adult) and in its proper place (the object is valuable property). The absence of ownership does not necessitate absence of value. Since the fuduli is qualified and the object is suitable, the sale is concluded. There is no harm to the owner because he has the option to ratify or rescind; he even benefits by avoiding effort of finding a buyer. The fuduli benefits by his speech not being futile, and the buyer benefits from his willing purchase. Thus, for these benefits, legal power and authority are established for the fuduli, and his sale is concluded. The author of al-Hidayah responds to Imam al-Shafi'i: your statement that authority is established by ownership or permission and neither exists is incorrect because the owner's permission is established by indication, as the owner is rational and permits beneficial transactions. Thus, the fuduli has authority, and his sale is concluded. The owner has the right of ratification as long as the object and the contracting parties remain as they were.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the validity of a sale made by a fuduli (one who sells another's property without authorization). The author first presents the Shafi'i argument: such a sale lacks legal authority (wilayah), so it is not concluded (mun'aqid). The Hanafi response follows: the sale is concluded because it is a valid transaction (tasarruf) from a qualified person (ahil: sane adult) concerning a suitable object (mahall: valuable property). The Hanafi argument emphasizes that the owner benefits from such a sale and can choose to ratify or reject it. The benefit to the owner implies implied permission (dalalah). The passage then records the response of the author of al-Hidayah to Imam al-Shafi'i, asserting that the owner's permission is established through indication (dalalah) because every rational person permits beneficial transactions. Thus, the fuduli possesses legal authority (wilayah shar'iyyah) from the owner's perspective, and the sale is concluded. The passage concludes by stating that the owner's right of ratification persists as long as the object of sale (ma'qud 'alayh) and the contracting parties (the fuduli and buyer) remain in their original state.

Key Terms
فضولی (fuduli): One who sells the property of another without authorization.
ولایت شرعیہ (wilayah shar'iyyah): Legal authority to effect a transaction, established by ownership or permission.
انعقاد (inqi'ad): The state of a contract being legally concluded (mun'aqid) though not yet binding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the legal status of a fuduli sale before the owner's ratification?
A) It is batil (void) and cannot be ratified.
B) It is mun'aqid (concluded) but mawquf (suspended).
C) It is makruh (disliked) but valid.
D) It is sahih (valid) and immediately binding.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a fuduli sale is concluded (mun'aqid) but suspended on ratification, unlike the Shafi'i view that it is void ab initio.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate

Conditions for Owner's Ratification in Fuduli Sale
Defines conditions for valid ratification in fuduli sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for valid owner's ratification in a fuduli sale and explain why the fuduli may rescind before ratification.

Core Idea
Ratification requires the contract to still exist — object and parties must remain as they were.

We have learned that a fuduli sale is valid but suspended on the owner's approval. Now we dive into the precise conditions that make that ratification effective. The passage from al-Hidayah lays down two key requirements: the object of sale must still exist, and the contracting parties (fuduli and buyer) must be alive and legally capable. Without these, ratification is void, because ratification is a disposition in the contract, and a contract only exists through its subject matter and parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions for ratification
From the Arabic ‘al-ijaza idha kana al-ma'qud 'alayh baqiyan wa al-muta'aqidan bi-halihima’, note that ratification requires (a) the object (ma'qud 'alayh) to still exist, and (b) the two contracting parties (fuduli and buyer) to be in their original state (i.e., alive and with legal capacity).
The condition of the parties being 'in their state' means they have not died or lost capacity (e.g., insanity).
2
Explain the rationale for these conditions
The text says: ‘because ratification is a disposition in the contract, so its existence is necessary’. The contract’s existence depends on its object and parties. If either is gone, the contract no longer exists, so ratification cannot attach.
This is a standard Hanafi legal logic: a disposition (tasarruf) cannot operate on a non-existent subject.
3
Understand the status of the price after ratification
When the owner ratifies, the price becomes the owner's property and is held by the fuduli as a trust (amanah), like an agent. The fuduli is not liable for accidental loss of the price.
This is because ‘subsequent ratification is like prior agency’ — the fuduli is retroactively an agent.
4
Recognize the fuduli's right to rescind before ratification
The fuduli may rescind the sale before the owner ratifies, in order to free himself from obligations. This is unlike a fuduli in marriage, because marriage is a protective act (he is just a messenger).
The key difference: the fuduli in sale bears liabilities (e.g., he owes the price to the owner if he has already received it), so he can protect himself.
5
Distinguish between price as debt vs specific commodity
If the price is a debt (general), ratification makes the owner the owner of the debt. If the price is a specific commodity, ratification is only valid if that commodity remains; then the fuduli owns that specific commodity and owes the owner the equivalent (mithl) or value (qimah) of the sold item.
This is because the fuduli is treated as a buyer from the owner in that case, and purchase is not suspended on ratification — it takes effect immediately upon contract.

He (al-Quduri) said: And the owner has the right of ratification as long as the object of sale remains and the two contracting parties are in their state, because ratification is a disposition in the contract, so its existence is necessary, and that is by the existence of the contracting parties and the object. When the owner ratifies, the price becomes owned by him (the owner) as a trust in the hand of the fuduli like an agent, because subsequent ratification is like prior agency. And the fuduli may rescind before ratification to remove liabilities from himself, unlike the fuduli in marriage because he is merely an expression. This applies when the price is a debt. If it is a specific commodity, ratification is only valid if that commodity also remains. Then the ratification is of the cash (specific item), not of the contract, so that the specific commodity becomes owned by the fuduli, and he owes the equivalent of the sold item if it is fungible (mithli) or its value if not fungible, because it is a purchase from one aspect, and purchase is not suspended on ratification. And if the owner dies, it is not executed by the ratification of the heir in either case, because it was suspended on the owner's own ratification. 

Explanation: It has already passed that if a fuduli sells another's property without permission, the sale is concluded, but the owner has the option to ratify or rescind. In this passage, Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri states: The owner has the right of ratification only as long as the object (mabi') exists and the contracting parties (fuduli and buyer) are in their state. That is, the suspended sale can become effective by the owner's ratification only if at the time of ratification the object exists and the contracting parties still possess legal capacity. Since ratification is a disposition in the contract, the contract must exist, and its existence depends on the existence of the parties and object. Therefore, existence of parties and object at ratification is made a condition. If the object does not exist or the parties are not in their state, the ratification is ineffective. When the owner ratifies, the price becomes owned by him and is a trust in the fuduli's hand like an agent. Thus, if the price perishes in the fuduli's hand, no guarantee (daman) is due. The author of al-Hidayah states that before ratification, the fuduli may rescind the sale to remove liabilities from himself, because the rights of sale revert to the contracting party. But if someone is a fuduli in marriage, then... (text cuts off).
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This lesson presents the rulings and conditions for the owner's ratification (ijaza) in a fuduli sale. The Arabic matn from al-Hidayah or al-Quduri sets out: The owner may ratify only if the object of sale (ma'qud 'alayh) and the contracting parties (the fuduli and the buyer) remain as they were at the time of contract. If any changes (e.g., the object destroyed, a party died or lost capacity), ratification is ineffective. Upon ratification, the price becomes the owner's property and is held by the fuduli as a trust (amanah), like an agent. The fuduli may rescind the sale before ratification to free himself from obligations. If the price is a specific item (not a debt), the fuduli owns that specific item and must give the equivalent (mithl) or value (qimah) to the owner, treated as a purchase from one aspect. If the owner dies, his heir's ratification does not validate the sale because it depended on the deceased owner's personal ratification. The commentary (tashrih) explains these points in detail, emphasizing that the existence of object and parties is a condition for valid ratification, and that the fuduli's possession is like that of an agent (wakil), so it is trust-based.

Key Terms
اجازہ (ijazah): Owner's ratification of a fuduli sale, making it binding.
معقود علیہ (ma'qud 'alayh): The object of sale that is subject of the contract.
امانت (amanah): Trust; the price in fuduli's hand after ratification is held as a trust (amanah), not guaranteed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The price must be paid immediately.
B) The object of sale and both contracting parties must still exist.
C) The fuduli must agree.
D) The buyer must approve.

Key Takeaway
Ratification only works if the sale's subject and parties remain; otherwise, the sale falls through and the fuduli bears liability.

Knowledge of Object's Existence at Ratification: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the condition of knowledge for ratification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify two Hanafi views on the requirement of knowledge for ratification and apply the principle of istishab to support the relied-upon view.

Core Idea
Ratification is valid even without knowledge of the object's existence because the original presumption (al-asl baqa'uhu) governs.

When an owner ratifies a fuduli sale, does he need to know that the sold object still exists? The Hanafi school has an important inner difference. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and the earlier position of Imam Abu Yusuf hold that the original legal presumption (istishab) of the object's continuation is sufficient. Later, Abu Yusuf retracted and demanded positive knowledge. This lesson walks through both positions and explains why the earlier view remains the relied-upon fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Establish the scenario
The owner ratifies a fuduli sale but has no information about the current existence of the sold object.
The owner is not certain whether the object still exists.
2
Identify the first Hanafi view
Muhammad and earlier Abu Yusuf say the sale is valid. Their evidence: al-asl baqa'uhu (original presumption of existence).
This is recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Identify the retraction and second view
Later Abu Yusuf requires knowledge of existence at ratification. His evidence: doubt (shakk) cannot establish a condition.
Abu Yusuf's retraction (ruju') is noted in the text.
4
Trace the thamarah al-khilaf
If the owner ratifies without knowledge, the sale is valid per the first view, invalid per the second.
The practical difference turns on whether knowledge is a condition.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The first view is relied upon; it is the position of Muhammad and earlier Abu Yusuf.
The text presents this view as the default, implying it is stronger.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يجوز باجازة غيره ولو اجاز المالك فى حياته ولا يعلم حال المبيع جاز البيع فى قول أبي يوسف اولا وهو قول محمد لان الاصل بقاؤه ثم رجع ابويوسف وقال لا يصح حتى يعلم قيامه عند الاجازة لان الشك وقع في شرط الاجازة فلايثبت مع الشك
ترجمہ اور مالک کو اجازت کا اختیار اس وقت تک حاصل ہے جبکہ معقود علیہ موجود ہو اور عاقدین اپنی حالت پر ہوں کیونکہ اجازت دینا عقد میں تصرف ہے۔ اسلئے عقد کا قائم ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اور عقد کا قیام عاقدین اور معقود علیہ کے موجود ہونے سے ہوتا ہے۔ اور جب مالک نے بیچ کی اجازت دیدی تو شن مالک کا مملوک ہوگا جو فضولی کے پاس بمنزلہ وکیل کے امانت ہوگا۔ اسلئے کہ اجازت لاحقہ وکالت سابقہ کے مرتبہ میں ہوتی ہے اور فضولی کو مالک کے اجازت دینے سے پہلے اپنے اوپر سے حقوق دور کرنے کیلئے بیچ مسح کرنے کا اختیار ہے۔ بخلاف نکاح فضولی کے کیونکہ وہ محض تعبیر کرنے والا ہوتا ہے۔ یہ حکم اس وقت ہے جبکہ ثمن ، دین ہو پس اگر شین معین سامان ہو تو مالک کی اجازت اس وقت صحیح ہو گی جبکہ سامان بھی موجود ہو۔ پھر اجازت مذکورہ اجازت نقد ہے نہ کہ اجازت عقد حتی کہ جو سامان ثمن ہے وہ فضولی کا ملوک ہوگا۔ اور فضولی پر میچ کا مثل واجب ہے اگر بیچ مشکلی چیز ہو یا اس کی قیمت واجب ہے اگر مبیع مثلی چیز نہ ہو کیونکہ یہ من وجہ خریداری ہے اور خریداری اجازت پر موقوف نہیں ہوتی اور اگر مالک مر گیا تو اس کے وارث کی اجازت سے دونوں صورتوں میں فضولی کی بیچ نافذ نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ بیع مذکور مورث کی ذاتی اجازت پر موقوف تھی۔ لہذا غیر کی اجازت سے جائز نہ ہوگی اور اگر مالک نے اپنی زندگی میں بیچ کی اجازت دے دی۔ حالانکہ مبیع کا حال معلوم نہیں ہے تو ابو یوسف کے قول اول کے مطابق بیع جائز ہو جائے گی اور یہی امام محمد کا قول ہے۔ کیونکہ اصل میچ کا باقی ہونا ہے۔ پھر ابو یوسف نے اس سے رجوع کیا اور کہا کہ بیچ صحیح نہیں ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ اجازت کے وقت مبیع کا موجود ہونا معلوم ہو۔ کیونکہ اجازت کی شرط میں شک واقع ہو گیا ہے اسلئے شک کے ساتھ اجازت ثابت نہ ہوگی۔
It is permitted by the ratification of another (the owner). If the owner ratifies during his lifetime without knowing the condition of the sold item, the sale is valid according to the earlier opinion of Abu Yusuf, and that is also the opinion of Muhammad, because the original presumption is its existence. Then Abu Yusuf retracted and said: It is not valid until he knows of its existence at the time of ratification, because doubt has occurred concerning the condition of ratification, so it is not established with doubt.

Translation: And the owner has the right of ratification only as long as the object exists and the contracting parties are in their state, because ratification is a disposition in the contract. When the owner ratifies, the price becomes owned by him and is held by the fuduli as a trust like an agent. The fuduli may rescind before ratification to remove liabilities from himself, unlike the fuduli in marriage. This ruling applies when the price is a debt. If it is a specific commodity, the owner's ratification is only valid if that commodity also exists. Then the ratification is of the cash (specific item), not of the contract, so that the specific commodity becomes owned by the fuduli, and he owes the equivalent of the sold item if fungible or its value if not fungible. If the owner dies, the heir's ratification does not execute the sale in either case. If the owner ratifies during his lifetime without knowing the condition of the sold item, according to the first opinion of Abu Yusuf and the opinion of Muhammad, the sale is valid because the original presumption is its existence. Then Abu Yusuf retracted and said: It is not valid until he knows of its existence at the time of ratification, because doubt occurred concerning the condition of ratification, so it is not established with doubt.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This lesson presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani concerning a scenario where the owner ratifies a fuduli sale without knowing whether the object of sale still exists. The matn records: The owner may ratify, and if he does so during his lifetime without knowledge of the object's condition, the sale is valid according to the earlier opinion of Abu Yusuf and the opinion of Muhammad al-Shaybani. Their reasoning: the original presumption (al-asl) is that the object continues to exist (baqa'). Later, Abu Yusuf retracted and held that ratification is not valid unless the owner positively knows the object exists at the time of ratification, because doubt (shakk) has arisen concerning a condition of ratification, and a condition cannot be established with doubt. The Urdu commentary expands on this: the owner's right of ratification is conditioned on the existence of the object and parties; if the owner does not know whether the object exists, the original presumption is that it exists (istishab al-hal), so ratification is valid. But Abu Yusuf's final view requires certainty. The commentary also reiterates the earlier rulings on when price is a debt vs. specific item, and that heir's ratification is invalid.

Key Terms
اصل (asl): Legal presumption (istishab) that something continues to exist until proven otherwise.
شک (shakk): Doubt about the fulfillment of a condition, which prevents the condition from being established.
رجوع (ruju'): Retraction of a legal opinion by a mujtahid (here Abu Yusuf).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, if the owner ratifies a fuduli sale without knowing whether the object still exists, is the ratification valid?
A) No, because doubt invalidates the condition.
B) Yes, because the original presumption is that the object exists.
C) Yes, but only if the fuduli agrees.
D) No, the sale is void ab initio.

Key Takeaway
The owner's ratification of a fuduli sale is valid under the relied-upon Hanafi opinion even without knowledge of the object's existence, due to the legal presumption of its continuation (istishab).

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Knowledge of Mabi' Existence at Ratification
Intra-Hanafi dispute on condition of knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for owner ratification in a fuduli sale and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on knowledge of mabi' existence.

Core Idea
Ratification requires existence of the sold item, but knowledge of its existence is disputed: default assumption vs. certainty.

A fuduli (unauthorized agent) sale is suspended on the owner's ratification. But what if the owner ratifies without knowing if the item still exists? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement: some say the default assumption of existence suffices, others demand certainty. This lesson unpacks that dispute and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the base rule
Identify that a fuduli's sale is mawquf (suspended) and requires owner's ratification to become valid.
The condition for ratification is that the subject matter (mabi') must exist and the parties must be legally fit.
2
Identify the dispute
Recognize that the dispute is about whether the owner must know that the mabi' exists at the time of ratification.
Two positions: Abu Yusuf's first view (and Muhammad) vs. Abu Yusuf's later view.
3
Trace each position's proof
For the first view: al-asl baqa'uh (the default is existence). For the later view: doubt in the condition prevents ratification.
The later view uses the principle 'al-shakk la yuthbitu' (doubt cannot establish).
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If the mabi' is later found to have been destroyed, the first view holds the sale valid (buyer can claim from fuduli), the later view invalid.
This practical difference affects who bears the loss.
5
Note the tarjih
The text does not give a tarjih; later Hanafi works often adopt the cautious view (requiring knowledge).
In contemporary fatwa, the cautious view is often preferred.

معنی یہ ہیں کہ ثمن معین مالک کو دیا جائے اور اس سے مبیع لے لی جائے اور اگر اس نے اجازت نہ دی حالانکہ عقد لازم ہو گیا تو فضولی پر مبیع کا مثل واجب ہوگا۔ اگر مبیع مثلی ہو اور اگر مثلی نہ ہو تو اس پر بیع کی قیمت واجب ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر مالک اجازت دینے سے پہلے مر گیا تو فضولی کی بیع مالک کے وارث کی اجازت سے نافذ نہ ہو گی ۔ ثمن خواہ دین ہو خواہ سامان معین ہو۔ کیونکہ فضولی کی بیع مورث یعنی مالک کی ذاتی اجازت پر موقوف تھی اسلئے اس کے علاوہ کسی دوسرے کی اجازت سے جائز نہ ہوگی۔ اور اگر مالک نے اپنی زندگی میں بیع کی اجازت دے دی اور پھر مر گیا حالانکہ بیع کا حال معلوم نہیں کہ وہ موجود ہے یا معدوم ہے تو امام ابو یوسف کے قول اول کے مطابق بیع جائز ہو جائے گی اور یہی امام محمد کا قول ہے کیونکہ اصل یہی ہے کہ مبیع موجود ہو اور جب مبیع کا موجود ہونا اصل ہے تو مالک کی اجازت درست ہوگی اور جب اس کی اجازت درست ہے تو بیع بھی جائز ہوگی۔ پھر امام ابو یوسف نے اس سے رجوع کیا اور کہا کہ بیع نہ ہوگی یہاں تک کہ اجازت کے وقت مبیع کا موجود ہونا یقینی طور پر معلوم نہ ہو کیونکہ اجازت کی شرط یعنی بیع موجود ہونے میں شک واقع ہو گیا ہے۔ اسلئے شک کے ساتھ اجازت ثابت نہ ہوگی اور جب اجازت ثابت نہ ہوئی تو فضولی کی بیع جائز بھی نہ ہوگی
The owner has the right to ratify only while the subject matter exists and the parties remain in their state, because ratification is an act of disposal in the contract. So the contract must exist, and its existence is through the existence of the parties and the subject matter. When the owner ratifies the sale, the price becomes owned by him and is held in trust by the fuduli like an agent, because subsequent ratification is like prior agency. The fuduli can rescind the sale before ratification to remove its rights from himself, unlike a fuduli in marriage. This applies when the price is a debt. If the price is a specific commodity, the owner's ratification is valid only if the commodity exists. Then the ratification is of the specific commodity, not of the suspended contract, so the specific commodity becomes owned by the fuduli, and he must pay the equivalent or value. If the owner dies, his heir's ratification is ineffective because the sale was suspended on the owner's personal ratification. And if the owner ratifies during his life while the state of the sold item is unknown, then according to Abu Yusuf's first view (also Muhammad's view) the sale is valid because the original state is existence. Then Abu Yusuf retracted and said it is invalid until the existence is known at the time of ratification because doubt occurs in the condition of ratification, so ratification cannot be established with doubt.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a fuduli sale when the owner ratifies it but the existence of the sold item (mabi') is unknown. The rule: a sale by a fuduli (unauthorized person) is suspended on the owner's ratification. The owner's right to ratify is conditional upon the existence of the subject matter and the continued legal capacity of the fuduli and buyer at the time of ratification. The price (thaman) becomes the owner's property and is held by the fuduli as a trust (amanah) like an agent's possession. Before ratification, the fuduli can rescind the sale to discharge his own liability, unlike in marriage where he cannot. If the price is a specific commodity (mu'ayyan), then the contract becomes binding on the fuduli from his side (as a muqayadha transaction), so ratification is only concerning that commodity, not the contract. The owner's death before ratification prevents his heirs from ratifying. The dispute: If the owner ratifies without knowing whether the mabi' still exists, Abu Yusuf's first opinion (shared by Muhammad) is that the sale is valid because the default assumption is existence (al-asl baqa'uh). Abu Yusuf later retracted, saying knowledge of existence is required because the condition (existence) is doubtful, and ratification cannot be established with doubt. The commentary follows the order of the original matn (from Al-Hidayah), explaining each condition and the debate.

Key Terms
فضولی (fuduli): A person who conducts a transaction on behalf of another without prior authorization, acting as an unauthorized agent.
اجازت (ijazah): The owner's subsequent ratification (approval) of a suspended contract, rendering it valid and enforceable.
موقوف (mawquf): A suspended contract or action that depends on the approval of a principal (the owner) for its validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf's first view, if the owner ratifies a fuduli sale without knowing whether the sold item still exists, the sale is:
A) Invalid because of doubt in the condition of ratification.
B) Valid because the original state is that the item exists.
C) Suspended until the item's existence is confirmed.
D) Void because the owner did not have certain knowledge.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute: ratification by the owner can be valid without knowledge of the mabi's existence (default assumption) or requires certain knowledge (cautious view).

Fuduli Sale and Manumission: Istihsan vs Qiyas in Retroactive Ownership
Intra-Hanafi dispute on retroactive validity of manumission after ratification of fuduli sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad on the validity of manumission by a buyer before ratification, and explain how istihsan overrides qiyas in this case.

Core Idea
Ratification of a fudūlī sale can retroactively validate the buyer's manumission through istihsan.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: a person usurps a slave, sells it without the owner's permission (fudūlī sale), and the buyer frees the slave before the owner ratifies. Does the subsequent ratification make the manumission valid? Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say yes, istihsanan; Imam Muhammad says no, based on strict qiyas and the hadith 'La 'itqa fi ma la yamlik'. We will dissect their arguments and the underlying usul principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the legal act
Begin with the facts: usurpation (ghasb), a fuduli sale, buyer manumission ('itq), and later owner ratification. The key question is the legal effect of ratification on the manumission.
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
They rule that the manumission is valid (jā'iz) istihsānan. Understand that istihsan overrides the strict analogy that would require ownership at the moment of manumission.
Istihsan is a distinctive Hanafi source that allows flexibility for public benefit.
3
State Imam Muhammad's position and his dalil
He rules that the manumission is invalid because ownership was absent. He cites the hadith and argues that a suspended contract (mawquf) does not confer ownership, and ratification creates new ownership, not retroactive.
Muhammad's position relies on the principle that an act of manumission requires ownership at the time of act.
4
Analyze the difference in usul: istihsan vs qiyas
The dispute is rooted in whether the retroactive effect (lahq) of ratification applies to manumission. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf treat ratification as confirming ownership from the start (ittifāq), while Muhammad sees it as a new event.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
If Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf's view is followed, the slave becomes free; if Muhammad's view, the slave remains the owner's property. Later Hanafi practice generally adopts the istihsan position.
The dispute is recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah but the mufta bihi is the view of the majority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن غصب عبدا فباعه واعتقه المشترى ثم اجاز المولى البيع فالعتق جائز استحسانا وهذا عندابي حنيفة وابى يوسف وقال محمد لا يجوز لانه لا عتق بدون الملك قال عليه السلام لاعتق فيما لا يملك ابن ادم والموقوف لا يفيد الملك ولويثبت فى الاخرة يثبت مستندا وهو ثابت من وجه دون وجه
He said: And whoever usurps a slave and sells him, and the buyer manumits him, then the owner ratifies the sale, the manumission is valid istihsanan. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: It is not valid because there is no manumission without ownership. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no manumission in what the son of Adam does not own.' And the suspended (sale) does not confer ownership. And if it were to be established later, it would be established as a new act, but it is established from one aspect and not from another.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of manumission ('itq) by a buyer of a usurped slave before the owner's ratification of the sale. The example: A person usurps a slave (ghasb), sells it to a buyer, and the buyer manumits the slave. Subsequently, the original owner ratifies the sale. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the manumission is valid (istihsanan) because ratification retroactively confirms the buyer's ownership from the time of sale, so the manumission becomes effective. Muhammad argues that it is invalid because at the time of manumission, the buyer did not own the slave (the sale was suspended and ownership was not transferred). He cites the hadith 'La 'itqa fi ma la yamliku ibn Adam' (There is no manumission in what a person does not own). He further argues that a suspended contract (mawquf) does not confer ownership, and even if ownership is established later (by ratification), it would be as a new event, not retroactively. However, the statement 'huwa thabit min wajhin duna wajhin' indicates that the manumission is valid from one angle (istihsan) and invalid from another (qiyas). The text presents both positions without explicit tarjih.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a ruling that is more equitable or facilitates transactions.
عتق ('itq): Manumission; the act of freeing a slave, which requires ownership of the slave at the time.
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended; referring to the sale that is dependent on later ratification for its legal effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, why is the manumission of a slave by the buyer invalid before the owner's ratification?
A) Because the buyer did not pay the full price.
B) Because the buyer cannot manumit without the owner's consent.
C) Because the buyer did not own the slave at the time of manumission.
D) Because the manumission must occur after the sale is ratified.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of a buyer's manumission of a usurped slave depends on whether ratification retroactively establishes ownership; Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf accept this via istihsan, while Muhammad rejects it via qiyas.

Ruling on Fuduli Sale: Specified Price and Owner's Permission
Ruling on fuduli sale with specified price and owner's permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a fuduli sale when the price is a specified item and explain the effect of the owner's permission or refusal, including the intra-Hanafi difference on the need for certainty of the sold item's existence.

Core Idea
A fuduli sale with a specified price binds the fuduli even without the owner's permission.

In this passage, the author of al-Hidayah clarifies a key aspect of the fuduli (unauthorized agent) contract in Hanafi fiqh. When the price is a specified item, the contract becomes binding on the fuduli immediately, unlike when the price is a debt. Understanding this distinction is crucial for knowing when a fuduli is personally liable and how the owner's permission affects the transaction.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish between debt and specified price
Identify the two scenarios: price as a debt (dayn) vs. price as a specified item (mu'ayyan). Only in the latter does the sale become binding on the fuduli without the owner's permission.
Debt includes dirhams, dinars, or described fungibles.
2
Understand why specified price sale binds the fuduli
The passage argues that when both price and subject matter are specified items, the sale is an exchange (mu'awadah), making each party a buyer. Purchase is not suspended on another's permission, so the fuduli is bound.
This reasoning applies only in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Trace the effect of owner's permission or refusal
If the owner permits, the specified price is given to the owner and the sold item is taken from him. If the owner refuses or dies before permission, the fuduli must compensate the buyer with the like or value of the sold item.
Owner's death before permission nullifies the contract; heir's permission is ineffective.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on existence uncertainty
If the owner gives permission but the sold item's existence is uncertain, Imam Abu Yusuf's first opinion (shared by Imam Muhammad) validates the sale based on the principle that existence is the default. Abu Yusuf later retracted, requiring certainty.
Al-Marghinani presents both without explicit tarjih, leaving the matter open.

Source Text
