صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مالک کی اجازت کے وقت معقود علیہ اور عاقدین کا موجود ہونا اس وقت ضروری ہے جبکہ ثمن دین ہو یعنی دراہم یا دنانیر ہوں یا فلوس ہوں یا غیر معین کیلی یا وزنی چیز ہو بشرطیکہ اس کے جملہ اوصاف بیان کر دئیے ہوں اور اگر ثمن کوئی معین سامان ہو تو اجازت کے وقت معقود علیہ اور عاقدین کے موجود ہونے کے علاوہ اس معین سامان کا موجود ہونا بھی ضروری ہے اور اس صورت میں مالک کی طرف سے جو اجازت ہے وہ اس بات کی اجازت ہے کہ فضولی مالک کے مال میں سے اس چیز کو ادا کر دے جس کو بیچا ہے عقد موقوف کی اجازت نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں فضولی پر عقد بغیر مالک کی اجازت کے لازم اور نافذ ہو گیا ہے حتی کہ جو معین سامان، ثمن مقرر کیا گیا ہے وہ فضولی کا مملوک ہوگا اور مالک اگر اجازت دینے سے پہلے مر گیا یا معین ثمن دینے سے انکار کر دیا تو مبیع اگر ذوات الامثال میں سے ہو تو فضولی پر اس کا مثل واجب ہوگا اور اگر ذوات القیم میں سے ہو تو مبیع کی قیمت واجب ہوگی۔ اور بیع اس صورت میں اسلئے لازم ہو جاتی ہے کہ جب ثمن بھی معین سامان ہو اور مبیع بھی سامان ہے تو یہ بیع معاوضہ ہوگئی اور بیع معاوضہ من وجہ ہر ایک جانب میں شراء ہوتی ہے تو گویا فضولی کے حق میں من وجہ شراء ہے اور شراء کسی کی اجازت پر موقوف نہیں ہوتی۔ اسلئے فضولی کے حق میں یہ بیع لازم اور نافذ ہوگی۔ پھر اگر مالک نے اجازت دیدی تو اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ ثمن معین مالک کو دیا جائے اور اس سے مبیع لے لی جائے اور اگر اس نے اجازت نہ دی حالانکہ عقد لازم ہو گیا تو فضولی پر مبیع کا مثل واجب ہوگا۔ اگر مبیع مثلی ہوا در اگر مثلی نہ ہو تو اس پر بیع کی قیمت واجب ہوگی۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر مالک اجازت دینے سے پہلے مرگیا تو فضولی کی بیع مالک کے وارث کی اجازت سے نافذ نہ ہو گی ۔ ثمن خواہ دین ہو خواہ سامان معین ہو۔ کیونکہ فضولی کی بیع مورث یعنی مالک کی ذاتی اجازت پر موقوف تھی اسلئے اس کے علاوہ کسی دوسرے کی اجازت سے جائز نہ ہوگی۔ اور اگر مالک نے اپنی زندگی میں بیع کی اجازت دے دی اور پھر مر گیا حالانکہ بیع کا حال معلوم نہیں کہ وہ موجود ہے یا معدوم ہے تو امام ابو یوسف کے قول اول کے مطابق بیع جائز ہو جائے گی اور یہی امام محمد کا قول ہے کیونکہ اصل یہی ہے کہ مبیع موجود ہو اور جب مبیع کا موجود ہونا اصل ہے تو مالک کی اجازت درست ہوگی اور جب اس کی اجازت درست ہے تو بیع بھی جائز ہوگی۔ پھر امام ابو یوسف نے اس سے رجوع کیا اور کہا کہ بیع جائز نہ ہوگی یہاں تک کہ اجازت کے وقت مبیع کا موجود ہونا یقینی طور پر معلوم نہ ہو کیونکہ اجازت کی شرط یعنی بیع موجود ہونے میں شک واقع ہو گیا ہے۔ اسلئے شک کے ساتھ اجازت ثابت نہ ہوگی اور جب اجازت ثابت نہ ہوئی تو فضولی کی بیع جائز بھی نہ ہوگی۔
The author of al-Hidayah says: At the time of the owner's permission, it is necessary for the subject matter and the contracting parties to be present when the price is a debt, i.e., dirhams or dinars or fulus or an unspecified measurable or weighable item, provided that all its attributes are described. And if the price is a specified item, then in addition to the presence of the subject matter and the contracting parties, the presence of that specified item is also necessary. In this case, the permission from the owner is permission for the fuduli to pay that item from the owner's property which he sold, not permission for the suspended contract. Because in this case, the contract became binding and effective on the fuduli without the owner's permission, such that the specified price item becomes owned by the fuduli. If the owner dies before giving permission or refuses to give the specified price, then if the sold item is from fungibles (mithliyyat), the like (mithl) is obligatory on the fuduli; if from valuables (qimiyyat), the price is obligatory. The sale becomes binding because when the price is a specified item and the sold item is also a specified item, this sale becomes an exchange (mu'awadah), and an exchange is in one respect a purchase for each side. So for the fuduli, it is in one respect a purchase, and a purchase is not suspended on anyone's permission. Therefore, this sale is binding and effective for the fuduli. Then if the owner gives permission, its meaning is that the specified price is given to the owner and the sold item is taken from him. If he does not give permission even though the contract became binding, then the like of the sold item is obligatory on the fuduli. If the sold item is mithli, then its like; if not mithli, then its price. The author of al-Hidayah says: If the owner dies before giving permission, the fuduli's sale will not be effective by the permission of the owner's heir, whether the price is a debt or a specified item. Because the fuduli's sale was suspended on the owner's personal permission, so it will not be valid with anyone else's permission. If the owner gave permission during his lifetime and then died while the status of the sale is unknown (whether the sold item exists or not), then according to Imam Abu Yusuf's first opinion, the sale becomes valid, and this is also Imam Muhammad's opinion, because the principle is that the sold item exists, and when its existence is the principle, the owner's permission is valid, and when his permission is valid, the sale is valid. Then Imam Abu Yusuf retracted and said the sale will not be valid until the existence of the sold item at the time of permission is known with certainty, because doubt has occurred in the condition of permission (i.e., existence of the sale). Permission cannot be established with doubt, and when permission is not established, the fuduli's sale is not valid.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on a sale by a fuduli (unauthorized agent) when the price is specified and the owner's permission is given or withheld. The author of al-Hidayah begins by distinguishing two scenarios: when the price is a debt (dain) versus a specified item (mu'ayyan). For a debt price, only the contracting parties and subject matter need to be present at the time of permission. For a specified price, the price item itself must also be present. In the latter case, the contract becomes binding on the fuduli without owner's permission because it is an exchange (mu'awadah); each party is both buyer and seller in a sense. If the owner refuses or dies, the fuduli must deliver the like or value of the sold item. The passage then discusses the effect of the owner's death: if permission is given before death but the sold item's existence is uncertain, Imam Abu Yusuf's first opinion (also Imam Muhammad's) holds the sale valid based on the principle of existence, but Abu Yusuf later retracted, requiring certainty. This illustrates the Hanafi reliance on legal principles (usul) and the process of tarjih among opinions.

Key Terms
فضولی (fudūlī): An unauthorized agent who acts for another without permission; the contract is suspended on the owner's ratification.
دین (dayn): A debt or obligation, here referring to a price that is not a specific item but currency or measurable goods described in the contract.
معین (muʿayyan): Specified or particularized; here, the price is a specific item (e.g., a particular horse or cloth) rather than currency.
مثل (mithl): Like or similar; for fungible goods (mithliyyat), compensation is the like (same quantity and quality).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The sale becomes void
B) The fuduli must deliver the like or price of the sold item
C) The sale is automatically ratified
D) The buyer can demand the price from the owner

Key Takeaway
A fuduli sale with a specified price binds the fuduli immediately; the owner's permission only transfers ownership, while refusal makes the fuduli personally liable for the like or value of the sold item.

Emancipation by Buyer of Usurped Slave: Istihsan vs. Qiyas
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of emancipation by buyer of usurped slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the validity of emancipation by a buyer of a usurped slave before ratification and evaluate the opposing proofs from Imam Muhammad and other schools.

Core Idea
Suspended ownership can support emancipation if the transaction is absolute and intended to transfer ownership.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs) and Imam Muhammad on whether a buyer who frees a usurped slave before the owner's ratification can validly emancipate him. The two shaykhs uphold validity by istihsan, while Imam Muhammad rejects it by qiyas. The dispute hinges on the nature of ownership required for emancipation: complete ownership (milk kamil) at the moment of the act or delayed ownership through suspension.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
State the scenario: a usurper sells a slave; the buyer frees him before the owner ratifies. After ratification, does the slave become free? Two shaykhs say yes (istihsan); Imam Muhammad says no (qiyas).
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute; other schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) side with Imam Muhammad.
2
Follow Imam Muhammad's proof (qiyas)
Imam Muhammad cites the hadith 'La itq lima la yamlik' (no emancipation for what one does not own). He argues ownership must be complete (milk kamil) at the moment of emancipation. Since the buyer's ownership is suspended (milk mawquf) before ratification, and later ownership through istinad (attribution) is deficient, the emancipation is invalid.
He also uses analogies: the usurper himself cannot free and then pay compensation; a buyer with a conditional option cannot free.
3
Follow the two shaykhs' proof (istihsan)
The two shaykhs argue the sale is an absolute transaction (tasarruf mutlaq) intended to transfer ownership, even if suspended. There is no harm in suspending the effect. Emancipation, like sale, can be suspended and takes effect upon ratification. They analogize to a buyer from a pledgor and an heir freeing a slave from an encumbered estate.
They also distinguish the usurper's case (usurpation is not meant for ownership) and the case of a conditional sale (which prevents conclusion of sale entirely).
4
Examine the rebuttals and counter-rebuttals
Imam Muhammad responds that ownership via istinad is deficient; the two shaykhs reply that the sale itself is a valid cause, and suspension does not prevent effectiveness. The hadith is interpreted as requiring ownership at the root, not necessarily at the moment.
The core difference is whether the hadith's 'yamlik' means actual present possession or potential ownership through a valid cause.
5
Identify the tarjih and its basis
The commentator states that Hilal mentioned the view of the two shaykhs and that it is the most correct (al-ashah). The mufta bihi is that the emancipation is valid. This is based on istihsan, which overrides qiyas when there is a clear benefit and no harm.
Practical result: if the owner ratifies, the slave becomes free; the buyer does not owe compensation to the usurper beyond the price.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيوع
اشرف الهداية شرح اردو هداية جلد هشتم
والمصحح للاعتاق الملك الكامل لماروينا ولهذا لا يصح ان يعتق الغاصب ثم يؤدى الضمان ولا ان يعتق المشترى والخيار للبائع ثم يجيز البائع ذالك وكذا لا يصح بيع المشترى من الغاصب فيما نحن فيه مع انه اسرع نفاذا حتى نفذ من الغاصب اذا ادى الضمان وكذا لا يصح اعتاق المشترى من الغاصب اذا ارى الغاصب الضمان ولهما ان الملك ثبت موقوفا بتصرف مطلق موضوع لافادة الملك ولا ضرر فيه على مامر فيتوقف الاعتاق مرتبا عليه وينفذ بنفاذه وصار كاعتاق المشترى من الراهن وكاعتاق الوارث عبدا من التركة وهى مستغرقة بالدين يصح وينفذ اذا قضى الديون بعد ذالك بخلاف اعتاق الغاصب بنفسه لان الغصب غير موضوع لافادة الملك وبخلاف ما اذا كان فى البيع خياراً للبائع لانه ليس بمطلق وقران الشرط به يمنع انعقاده في حق الحكم اصلا وبخلاف المشترى من الغاصب اذا باع لان بالاجازة يثبت للبائع ملك بات فاذا طرأ على ملك موقوف لغيره ابطله واما اذا ادى الغاصب الضمان ينفذ اعتاق المشترى منه كذا ذكره هلال وهو الأصح
ترجمہ اور اگر ایک آدمی نے دوسرے آدمی کا غلام غصب کر کے اس کو فروخت کر دیا اور مشتری نے اس کو آزاد کر دیا۔ پھر مولیٰ نے بیچ کی اجازت دی تو استحسانا آزاد کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور یہ تیخین کے نزدیک ہے اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ بغیر ملکیت کے عشق نہیں ہوتا۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جس کا آدمی مالک نہ ہو اس میں عشق نہیں ہے اور جو بیع موقوف ہے وہ مفید ملک نہیں ہے اور اگر انجام کار میں ملکیت ثابت ہوئی تو وہ (سب سابق کی جانب) منسوب ہو کر ثابت ہوگی۔ اور جو چیز منسوب ہو کر ثابت ہو وہ من وجہ ثابت ہوتی ہے اور من وجہ ثابت نہیں ہوتی۔ حالانکہ آزاد کرنے کو صحیح کرنے والی ملک کامل ہوتی ہے اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ہے۔ اور اسی وجہ سے یہ بات صحیح نہیں ہے کہ غاصب آزاد کر کے تاوان ادا کر دے اور یہ بھی صحیح نہیں کہ مشتری آزاد کرے اور بائع کیلئے خیار ہو۔ پھر بائع اس بیع کی اجازت دے دے اور ایسے ہی ہمارے اس مسئلہ میں غاصب سے خرید کر فروخت کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے باوجود یکہ آزادی کی بہ نسبت بیچ جلدی نافذ ہوتی ہے۔ حتی کہ جب غاصب تاوان دے دے تو اس کی بیع نافذ ہو جاتی ہے۔ اور اسی طرح غاصب سے خریدنے والے کا آزاد کرنا صحیح نہیں ہوتا۔ جبکہ غاصب تاوان ادا کر دے۔
شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مشتری کی ملکیت، مالک کی اجازت پر موقوف ایسے تصرف سے ثابت ہوئی جو مطلق ہے اور وہ ملک کا فائدہ دینے کے واسطے موضوع ہے اور اس میں کسی کافر بھی نہیں ہے۔ جیسا کہ سابق میں گذر چکا تو اعتماق اسی پر مرتب ہو کر موقوف ہو گا۔ اور اس کے نافذ ہونے سے نافذ ہو جائے گا اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے راہن سے خریدنے والے کا آزاد کرنا اور جیسے وارث نے ترکہ کا کوئی غلام آزاد کیا اور حال یہ کہ ترکہ قرضہ میں گھرا ہوا ہے تو یہ صیح ہوتا ہے اور اعتاق کے بعد جب قرضہ ادا کر دیا گیا تو وارث کا اعتماق نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ برخلاف اس کے اگر غاصب نے بذات خود آزاد کیا ہو کیونکہ غصب افادہ ملک کیلئے موضوع نہیں ہے اور برخلاف اس کے جبکہ بیع میں بائع کا خیار ہو۔ اسلئے کہ یہ بیع مطلق نہیں ہے اور اس کے ساتھ شرط کا مقارن ہونا حکم کے حق میں اس کے انعقاد کو بالکل روکتا ہے اور برخلاف غاضب سے خریدنے والے کے جبکہ یہ اس کو فروخت کرے۔ اسلئے کہ اجازت کی وجہ سے بائع کیلئے قطعی ملک ثابت ہوگی اور جب ملک موقوف پر یہ ملک قطعی طاری ہوئی تو اس کو باطل کرے گی۔ اور جب غاسب نے تاوان ادا کیا تو غاصب سے خریدے والے کا اعتاق نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ ایسا ہی اس کو ہلال نے ذکر کیا اور یہی اصح ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک آدمی نے کسی کا غلام مغصب کیا پھر غاصب نے اس کو فروخت کیا اور مشتری نے اس کو آزاد کیا۔ پھر مولیٰ نے بیع کی اجازت دی تو شیخین کے نزدیک مشتری کا آزاد کرنا استحسانا جائز ہو گیا یعنی مولی کے بیج کی اجازت کے بعد یہ غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ قیاس کے تقاضہ کے مطابق یہ آزادی درست نہیں ہے۔ یعنی مشتری من الغاصب کے آزاد کرنے سے یہ غلام آزاد نہ ہوگا۔ اگر چہ مولیٰ نے بیچ کی اجازت دے دی ہے۔ یہی قول امام زفر، امام شافعی، امام مالک اور امام احمد کا ہے۔ امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بغیر ملک کے آزادی نہیں ہوتی ہے یعنی انسان جس کا مالک نہ ہو اس کو آزاد کرنے سے آزادی متحقق نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ چنانچہ صاحب شریعت نے فرمایا ہے لانذر لابن آدم فيما لا يملك ولا عتق له فيما لا يملك ولا طلاق له فيما لا يملك (ترندی) یعنی آدمی کیلئے نہ تو غیر مملوکہ چیز میں نذر ہوتی ہے اور نہ غیر مملوکہ چیز میں آزادی ہوتی ہے اور نہ غیر مملوکہ (غیر منکوحہ) پر طلاق واقع ہوتی ہے۔ بہر حال آدمی جس کا مالک نہ ہو وہ اس کو آزاد نہیں کر سکتا ہے اور اس مسئلہ میں غاصب سے خریدنے والا غلام کا مالک نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ غاصب کی طرف سے جو بیع ہوئی ہے اس کا نفاذ مالک یعنی مغصوب منہ کی اجازت پر موقوف ہے اور مشتری من الغاصب کے آزاد کرتے وقت چونکہ مالک کی اجازت موجود نہیں تھی اسلئے مشتری، آزاد کرتے وقت غلام کا مالک نہیں تھا۔ آپ زیادہ سے زیادہ یہ کہہ سکتے ہیں کہ انجام کار کے اعتبار سے یعنی مالک کی اجازت کے وقت مشتری کیلئے ملکیت ثابت ہو گئی تو ہم کہتے ہیں کہ یہ ملکیت، سبب سابق یعنی غاصب کی بیع کی طرف منسوب ہو کر ثابت ہوگی۔ اور جو ملک بطریق استناد اور منسوب ہو کر ثابت ہو وہ من وجہ ثابت ہوتی ہے اور من وجہ ثابت نہیں ہوتی۔ اور جو ملک من وجہ ثابت ہو اور من وجہ ثابت نہ ہو وہ ملک ناقص ہوتی ہے حالانکہ آزاد کرنے کیلئے کامل ملک کا ہونا ضروری ہے کیونکہ حدیث لا عتق فيما لا يملك ابن آدم میں ملک مطلق ہے اور مطلق جب بولا جائے تو اس سے کامل مراد ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا حدیث میں ملک سے مراد ملک کامل ہے اور یہاں مشتری من الغاصب کیلئے چونکہ ملک کامل نہیں پائی گئی اسلئے یہ غلام مشتری من الغاصب کی جانب سے آزاد نہ ہوگا۔ بغیر ملک کے چونکہ آزادی واقع نہیں ہوتی اسی لئے اگر غاصب نے پہلے غلام مغصوب آزاد نہ کیا اور پھر مالک کو ضمان ادا کیا تو یہ غلام غاصب کی طرف سے آزاد نہ ہوگا۔ اور اسی طرح اگر بیچ میں بائع کیلئے خیار شرط ہو اور مشتری غلام کو آزاد کر دے تو غلام آزاد نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ غاصب کو تاوان ادا کرنے سے پہلے اور مشتری کو، بائع کی اجازت سے پہلے ملکیت نہیں ہے۔ اور تاوان ادا کرنے کے بعد غاصب کو اور بائع کی اجازت کے بعد مشتری کو جو ملک حاصل ہوئی ہے وہ بطریق استناد اور سبب سابق کی طرف منسوب ہو کر حاصل ہے جس سے ملک ناقص ثابت ہوتی ہے ملک استناد اور سبب سابق کی طرف منسوب ہو کر حاصل ہے جس سے ملک ناقص ثابت ہوتی ہے ملک استناد اور سبب سابق کی طرف منسوب ہو کر حاصل ہے جس سے ملک ناقص ثابت ہوتی ہے ملک کامل ثابت نہیں استناد ہو ہوتی۔ حالانکہ آزاد کرنے کیلئے کامل ملک کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر کسی نے غلام غاصب سے خرید کر کسی دوسرے کے ہاتھ فروخت کر دیا پھر مالک نے بیج اول کی اجازت دے دی تو یہ بیع ثانی صحیح نہیں ہے۔ پس اسی طرح اگر مشتری من الغاصب غلام کو آزاد کر دے تو آزاد کرنا درست نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ بہ نسبت آزادی کے بیچ جلدی نافذ ہو جاتی ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر غاصب نے غلام بیچا پھر اس کا تاوان ادا! کیا تو ناصب کی بیع نافذ ہو جائے گی اور اگر غاصب نے غلام آزاد کیا پھر تاوان ادا کیا تو اس کا آزاد کرنا نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ پس جب مشتری من
Book of Sales. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume 8. And the corrector for emancipation is complete ownership because of what we have narrated. Therefore, it is not valid that the usurper frees (the slave) and then pays the guarantee, nor that the buyer frees while the seller has an option, and then the seller ratifies that. Similarly, it is not valid for the buyer from the usurper to sell in this case of ours, even though it is quicker in execution, so that it takes effect from the usurper when he pays the guarantee. Similarly, it is not valid for the buyer from the usurper to emancipate when the usurper shows the guarantee. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), ownership is established as suspended (mawquf) by an absolute transaction placed to benefit ownership, and there is no harm in it as previously mentioned. So emancipation is suspended based on it and takes effect with its effectiveness, and it is like the emancipation of a buyer from a pledgor, and like the emancipation of an heir of a slave from an estate while it is overwhelmed by debts - it is valid and takes effect when the debts are paid after that. Contrary to the emancipation by the usurper himself because usurpation is not placed to benefit ownership, and contrary to when the sale has an option for the seller because it is not absolute, and the conjunction of a condition with it prevents its conclusion in terms of the ruling entirely, and contrary to the buyer from the usurper when he sells, because by ratification the seller acquires absolute ownership, and when it occurs upon a suspended ownership belonging to another, it nullifies it. But when the usurper pays the guarantee, the emancipation of the buyer from him takes effect. Hilal mentioned it thus, and it is the most correct. Translation: And if a person usurped another's slave and sold him, and the buyer freed him, then the master ratified the sale, then by istihsan the emancipation is valid. And this is according to the two shaykhs. Imam Muhammad said it is not valid because emancipation without ownership does not occur. The Prophet ﷺ said: 'One cannot free what he does not own.' And a suspended sale does not benefit ownership, and if ownership is established at the end, it is established by attribution to the preceding cause, and what is established by attribution is established in one respect and not in another, while liberation requires complete ownership because of the hadith we narrated. And for this reason, it is not valid that the usurper frees and then pays compensation, nor that the buyer frees while the seller has an option and then the seller ratifies. Similarly, in our case, sale by the buyer from the usurper is not valid even though it is quicker in execution than emancipation; indeed, when the usurper pays compensation his sale takes effect. Similarly, emancipation by the buyer from the usurper is not valid when the usurper pays compensation. The proof of the two shaykhs is that the buyer's ownership is established, suspended on the master's ratification, by an absolute transaction placed to benefit ownership, and there is no harm in it as previously mentioned, so emancipation is suspended upon it and takes effect with its taking effect. And this is like the emancipation by the buyer from the pledgor, and like an heir freeing a slave from an estate while it is burdened with debts - it is valid and when the debts are paid afterward, the heir's emancipation takes effect. Contrary to the usurper freeing by himself because usurpation is not placed to benefit ownership, and contrary to when the sale has an option for the seller because that sale is not absolute, and the conjunction of a condition with it prevents its conclusion entirely, and contrary to the buyer from the usurper selling because by ratification the seller (the buyer) gains absolute ownership, and when that absolute ownership occurs upon a suspended ownership it invalidates it. And when the usurper pays compensation, the emancipation of the buyer from him takes effect. Hilal mentioned it thus, and it is the most correct. Explanation of the scenario: A person usurped someone's slave, then the usurper sold him, and the buyer freed him. Then the master ratified the sale. According to the two shaykhs, the buyer's emancipation is valid by istihsan, meaning after the master's ratification the slave becomes free. Imam Muhammad said that according to qiyas, this emancipation is not valid - i.e., the slave will not be freed by the buyer's emancipation even if the master ratified the sale. This is also the view of Imam Zufar, Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad. Imam Muhammad's proof is that emancipation without ownership does not occur - i.e., a person cannot actually free what he does not own. Thus the Lawgiver said: 'There is no vow for the son of Adam regarding what he does not own, nor emancipation for him regarding what he does not own, nor divorce for him regarding what he does not own.' (Tirmidhi) That is, a person cannot make a vow regarding something he does not own, nor free what he does not own, nor divorce a woman he does not own (i.e., not his wife). In any case, a person cannot free what he does not own, and in this case the buyer from the usurper does not own the slave because the sale by the usurper is suspended on the owner's ratification, and at the time the buyer freed him, the owner's ratification was not present, so the buyer did not own the slave at that time. At most you can say that eventually, when the owner ratified, ownership was established for the buyer. But we say this ownership becomes established by attribution to the preceding cause (the usurper's sale), and ownership established by attribution is established in one respect and not another, and such ownership is deficient (naqis), while for emancipation complete ownership is necessary because the hadith 'no emancipation regarding what he does not own' mentions ownership in absolute terms, and when absolute is used, it means complete. Therefore, the hadith intends complete ownership, and here the buyer from the usurper does not have complete ownership, so the slave will not be freed by his emancipation. Since emancipation does not occur without ownership, for this reason if the usurper first freed the usurped slave and then paid compensation to the owner, the slave is not freed by the usurper. Similarly, if the sale had a stipulated option for the seller and the buyer freed the slave, the slave is not freed because before the usurper pays compensation and before the seller's ratification, the buyer has no ownership. And the ownership that the usurper gains after paying compensation and the buyer gains after the seller's ratification is obtained by attribution to the preceding cause, which gives deficient ownership, not complete ownership, while for emancipation complete ownership is necessary. Similarly, if someone bought a slave from a usurper and then sold him to another, then the owner ratified the first sale, the second sale is not valid. So likewise, if the buyer from the usurper frees the slave, the emancipation is not valid because sale takes effect more quickly than emancipation. For example, if the usurper sold the slave and then paid compensation, his sale takes effect; if he freed the slave and then paid compensation, his emancipation does not take effect. Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, a commentary on al-Hidayah, presents an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs, Sahibayn) on one side and Imam Muhammad on the other, concerning the validity of emancipation performed by a person who buys a usurped slave before the original owner ratifies the sale. The issue is whether the emancipation becomes effective when the owner later ratifies the sale. According to the two shaykhs (and the relied-upon ruling), the emancipation is valid by istihsan: the buyer's ownership, though suspended at the time of emancipation, becomes effective retroactively upon ratification, as the sale was an absolute transaction intended to transfer ownership. This is analogized to a buyer from a pledgor or an heir freeing a slave from an encumbered estate. Imam Muhammad, however, holds by qiyas that the emancipation is invalid because at the time of the act the buyer did not own the slave. He cites the hadith 'La itq lima la yamlik' and argues that ownership must be complete and present at the moment of emancipation. Ownership acquired through ratification is attributed to the original cause and is deficient (naqis), not complete. The passage also clarifies related rulings: the usurper himself cannot free the slave and then pay compensation; a sale with a stipulated option for the seller prevents the buyer's emancipation; and a subsequent sale by the buyer is also invalid. The correct position, according to Hilal, is that the buyer's emancipation takes effect only when the usurper pays compensation (i.e., the usurper's liability is discharged), which differs from the earlier scenario. The passage emphasizes that emancipation demands perfect ownership, and ownership that is suspended or retroactive does not suffice.

Key Terms
ملک موقوف (milk mawquf): Suspended ownership: ownership that is contingent upon a condition or ratification; it is not absolute until the condition occurs.
ملک کامل (milk kamil): Complete ownership: ownership that is absolute, unrestricted, and fully effective at the time of the act, as opposed to deficient (naqis) or suspended ownership.
استناد (istinad): Attribution: the legal principle that a subsequent ratification can attribute ownership back to the original cause, but such ownership is considered deficient (naqis) because it is not established independently.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), why is emancipation by the buyer of a usurped slave valid upon the owner's subsequent ratification?
A) Because the buyer owned the slave at the time of emancipation.
B) Because the sale is an absolute transaction placed to benefit ownership, and the emancipation is suspended on the ratification and takes effect with it.
C) Because the usurper's payment of compensation completes the ownership.
D) Because the hadith 'la itq lima la yamlik' only applies to usurpers, not buyers.

Key Takeaway
The two shaykhs uphold the validity of emancipation by a buyer of a usurped slave before ratification by istihsan, based on the concept of suspended ownership (milk mawquf) and analogies to similar cases, overriding the apparent qiyas requiring complete ownership at the moment of the act.

Dispute Over Manumission by Buyer from Usurper: Shaykhayn vs. Imam Muhammad
Dispute over validity of manumission by buyer from usurper after owner's ratification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two positions in the dispute over manumission by a buyer from a usurper, identify the proofs for each, and evaluate which position is relied upon in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Contingent ownership (mulk mawquf) can suffice for valid manumission upon ratification – a key Hanafi istihsan.

This lesson examines a classical intra-Hanafi and cross-madhhab dispute: a usurper sells a slave, the buyer frees him, and later the owner ratifies the sale. Is the manumission valid? The Shaykhayn say yes by istihsan; Imam Muhammad says no by qiyas. We will unpack the proofs, analogies, and responses, culminating in the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify the ruling of Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad on the validity of the manumission. Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).
2
Examine Imam Muhammad's proof
Analyze the hadith 'لا عتق له فيما لا يملك' and the three qiyas arguments (ghasib, khiyar, second sale) he uses to support his position.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), so it can be overridden by istihsan in Hanafi usul.
3
Examine Shaykhayn's proof
Understand the istihsan reasoning: contingent ownership suffices because the transaction is absolute and designed for ownership transfer. Study the analogies of the mortgaged slave and the heir freeing from an encumbered estate.
4
Understand the responses to Imam Muhammad's analogies
See how the Shaykhayn distinguish the ghasib's own freeing, the khiyar case, and the second sale, reaffirming the validity of the buyer's manumission.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The text indicates 'wa hadha huwa al-ashah' (this is the most correct), favoring the Shaykhayn. This is the operative position for fatwa.

كتاب البيوع
خریدنے والے کا اعتاق نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ ایسا ہی اس کو ہلال نے ذکر کیا اور یہی اصح ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک آدمی نے کسی کا غلام مغصب کیا پھر غاصب نے اس کو فروخت کیا اور مشتری نے اس کو آزاد کیا۔ پھر مولیٰ نے بیع کی اجازت دی تو شیخین کے نزدیک مشتری کا آزاد کرنا استحسانا جائز ہو گیا یعنی مولی کے بیج کی اجازت کے بعد یہ غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ قیاس کے تقاضہ کے مطابق یہ آزادی درست نہیں ہے۔ یعنی مشتری من الغاصب کے آزاد کرنے سے یہ غلام آزاد نہ ہوگا۔ اگر چہ مولیٰ نے بیچ کی اجازت دے دی ہے۔ یہی قول امام زفر ، امام شافعی ، امام مالک اور امام احمد کا ہے ۔ امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بغیر ملک کے آزادی نہیں ہوتی ہے یعنی انسان جس کا مالک نہ ہو اس کو آزاد کرنے سے آزادی متحقق نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ چنانچہ صاحب شریعت نے فرمایا ہے لانذر لابن آدم فيما لا يملك ولا عتق له فيما لا يملك ولا طلاق له فيما لا یملک
(ترندی)
یعنی آدمی کیلئے نہ تو غیر مملوکہ چیز میں نذر ہوتی ہے اور نہ غیر مملوکہ چیز میں آزادی ہوتی ہے اور نہ غیر مملوکہ (غیر منکوحہ ) پر طلاق واقع ہوتی ہے۔ بہر حال آدمی جس کا مالک نہ ہو وہ اس کو آزاد نہیں کر سکتا ہے اور اس مسئلہ میں غاصب سے خریدنے والا غلام کا مالک نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ غاصب کی طرف سے جو بیع ہوئی ہے اس کا نفاذ مالک یعنی مغصوب منہ کی اجازت پر موقوف ہے اور مشتری من الغاصب کے آزاد کرتے وقت چونکہ مالک کی اجازت موجود نہیں تھی اسلئے مشتری، آزاد کرتے وقت غلام کا مالک نہیں تھا۔ آپ زیادہ سے زیادہ یہ کہہ سکتے ہیں کہ انجام کار کے اعتبار سے یعنی مالک کی اجازت کے وقت مشتری کیلئے ملکیت ثابت ہو گئی تو ہم کہتے ہیں کہ یہ ملکیت ، سبب سابق یعنی غاصب کی بیع کی طرف منسوب ہو کر ثابت ہوگی۔ اور جو ملک بطریق استناد اور منسوب ہو کر ثابت ہو وہ من وجہ ثابت ہوتی ہے اور من وجہ ثابت نہیں ہوتی۔ اور جو ملک من وجہ ثابت ہو اور من وجہ ثابت نہ ہو وہ ملک ناقص ہوتی ہے حالانکہ آزاد کرنے کیلئے کامل ملک کا ہونا ضروری ہے کیونکہ حدیث لا عتق فيما لا يملك ابن آدم میں ملک مطلق ہے اور مطلق جب بولا جائے تو اس سے کامل مراد ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا حدیث میں ملک سے مراد ملک کامل ہے اور یہاں مشتری من الغاصب کیلئے چونکہ ملک کامل نہیں پائی گئی اسلئے یہ غلام مشتری من الغاصب کی جانب سے آزاد نہ ہوگا۔ بغیر ملک کے چونکہ آزادی واقع نہیں ہوتی اسی لئے اگر غاصب نے پہلے غلام مغصوب آزاد نہ کیا اور پھر مالک کو ضمان ادا کیا تو یہ غلام غاصب کی طرف سے آزاد نہ ہوگا۔ اور اسی طرح اگر بیچ میں بائع کیلئے خیار شرط ہو اور مشتری غلام کو آزاد کر دے تو غلام آزاد نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ غاصب کو تاوان ادا کرنے سے پہلے اور مشتری کو، بائع کی اجازت سے پہلے ملکیت نہیں ہے۔ اور تاوان ادا کرنے کے بعد غاصب کو اور بائع کی اجازت کے بعد مشتری کو جو ملک حاصل ہوئی ہے وہ بطریق استناد اور سبب سابق کی طرف منسوب ہو کر حاصل ہے جس سے ملک ناقص ثابت ہوتی ہے ملک استناد اور سبب سابق کی طرف منسوب ہو کر حاصل ہے جس سے ملک ناقص ثابت ہوتی ہے ملک استناد اور سبب سابق کی طرف منسوب ہو کر حاصل ہے جس سے ملک ناقص ثابت ہوتی ہے ملک کامل ثابت نہیں استناد ہو ہوتی۔ حالانکہ آزاد کرنے کیلئے کامل ملک کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر کسی نے غلام غاصب سے خرید کر کسی دوسرے کے ہاتھ فروخت کر دیا پھر مالک نے بیج اول کی اجازت دے دی تو یہ بیع ثانی صحیح نہیں ہے۔ پس اسی طرح اگر مشتری من الغاصب غلام کو آزاد کر دے تو آزاد کرنا درست نہ ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ بہ نسبت آزادی کے بیچ جلدی نافذ ہو جاتی ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر غاصب نے غلام بیچا پھر اس کا تاوان اد! کیا تو ناصب کی بیع نافذ ہو جائے گی اور اگر غاصب نے غلام آزاد کیا پھر تاوان ادا کیا تو اس کا آزاد کرنا نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ پس جب مشتری من الغاصب کی بیع صحیح نہیں حالانکہ بہ نسبت آزادی کے بیچ جلدی نافذ ہوتی ہے تو مشتری من الغاصب کا آزاد کرنا بدرجہ اولی صحیح نہ ہوگا۔ اور جس طرح مشتری من الغاصب کا آزاد کرنا صحیح نہیں ہوتا جبکہ غاصب تاوان ادا کر دے تو اسی طرح مشتری من الغاصب کو آزاد کرنا صحیح نہیں ہوگا ۔ جیسا کہ مالک بیع کی اجازت دے دے۔ شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مشتری من الغاصب کی ملک غلام کے مالک کی اجازت پر موقوف ہو کر ایسے تصرف سے ثابت ہوئی ہے جو مطلق ہے یعنی اس میں خیار وغیرہ کی شرط نہیں ہے اور ملکیت کا فائدہ دینے کیلئے وضع کیا گیا ہے اور مشتری من الغاصب کیلئے ملک موقوف ثابت کرنے میں مالک کا کوئی نقصان بھی نہیں ہے جیسا کہ پہلے گزر چکا۔ پس جب مشتری من الغاصب کی ملک، مالک کی اجازت پر موقوف ہے تو اس کا آزاد کرنا بھی مالک کی اجازت پر موقوف ہوگا اور جب مالک کی اجازت سے بیع نافذ ہوگی تو اس کے ساتھ ساتھ آزاد کرنا بھی نافذ ہو جائے گا اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے ایک آدمی نے کسی سے قرض لے کر اس کے پاس اپنا غلام رہن رکھا۔ پھر راہن نے بغیر مرتین کی اجازت کے غلام کو فروخت کر دیا پس مشتری نے اس کو آزاد کر دیا تو یہ آزادی مرتبہن کی اجازت یا رہن چھڑانے پر موقوف رہے گی۔ یعنی اگر مرتہن نے بیع کی اجازت دے دی تب بھی مشتری من الراہن کا آزاد کرنا نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر راہن نے مرتین کا قرضہ ادا کر دیا تب بھی آزادی کا نفاذ ہو جائے گا۔ پس جس طرح مشتری من الراہن کا آزاد کرنا درست اور جائز ہے اسی طرح مشتری من الغاصب کا آزاد کرنا بھی درست اور جائز ہے اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسے ایک وارث نے میت کے ترکہ میں سے ایک غلام آزاد کیا درانحالیکه میت کا ترکہ لوگوں کے قرضوں سے گھرا ہوا ہے تو یہ آزاد کرنا موقوف ہو کر صحیح ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر وارث نے غلام آزاد کرنے کے بعد میت کا قرضہ ادا کر دیا تو وارث کا آزاد کرنا نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ امام محمد میں دلیل کا جواب بخلاف اعتاق الغاصب ... الخ سے امام محمد کی طرف سے بیان کردہ مسائل کا جواب ہے۔ چنانچہ فرمایا کہ اگر غاصب نے بذات خود غلام آزاد کیا اور پھر تاوان ادا کیا تو آزاد کرنا اسلئے صحیح نہیں کہ غصب ملکیت ثابت کرنے کے واسطے وضع نہیں کیا گیا ہے یعنی غصب سے غاصب کیلئے ملک ثابت نہیں ہوتی اسلئے کہ غاصب، مالک کا دشمن ہے اور اداء ضمان کے وقت غاصب کیلئے ملکیت ضرورۃ ثابت ہوتی ہے۔ تا کہ دونوں بدل یعنی غلام اور ضمان ایک آدمی کی ملک یعنی مالک کی ملک میں جمع نہ ہو سکیں۔ پس غصب ، ادائے عمان کے وقت ملکیت حاصل ہونے کا سبب ہوگا گویا غاصب غلام کا ملک ادائے عمان کے وقت ہوا اور اس کو آزاد پہلے کر چکا ہے تو یہ غیر ملک کو آزاد کرنا ہوا اور غیر مملوک کو آزاد کرنا صحیح نہیں ہوتا۔ اسلئے غاصب کا آزاد کرنا درست نہ ہوگا اور خیار بائع کی صورت میں مشتری کا آزاد کرنا اس لئے صحیح نہیں ہے کہ یہ بیع مطلق نہیں ہے بلکہ خیار شرط کے ساتھ مقید ہے اور بائع کیلئے اگر خیار شرط ہو تو مشتری مبیع کا مالک نہیں ہوتا۔ پس اس صورت میں آزادی کے وقت مشتری غلام کا مالک نہیں تھا اور جب مشتری، آزاد کرتے وقت غلام کا مالک نہیں تھا تو اس کا آزاد کرنا بھی لغو ہوگا کیونکہ غیر مملوک کو آزاد کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔
تیسرے مسئلہ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جب مشتری من الغاصب نے غلام فروخت کیا تو یہ درست نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ جب مالک یعنی مغصوب منہ نے بیج اول کی اجازت دے دی تو بائع یعنی مشتری من الغاصب کیلئے ملک قطعی ثابت ہوگئی اور مشتری من الغاصب کیلئے ملک موقوف ثابت ہے۔ پس مالک کی اجازت سے مشتری من الغاصب کیلئے جب ملک قطعی ثابت ہوئی اور وہ ملک موقوف پر طاری ہوئی تو یہ ملک قطعی ، ملک موقوف کو باطل کر دے گی اور جب ملک موقوف باطل ہوگئی تو اس کو اجازت لاحق نہ ہوگی اور جب اس کو اجازت لاحق نہ
Kitab al-Buyu: The buyer's manumission will be effective. Hilal mentioned the same, and this is the most correct. Explanation: A man usurped someone's slave, then the usurper sold him, and the buyer freed him. Then the owner permitted the sale. According to the Shaykhayn, the buyer's manumission is valid by istihsan, i.e., after the owner's permission for the sale, the slave becomes free. Imam Muhammad said: According to the requirement of qiyas, this manumission is not valid, i.e., the slave will not become free by the buyer's freeing, even if the owner permitted the sale. This is also the view of Imam Zufar, Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad. Imam Muhammad's proof: Freedom does not occur without ownership, i.e., a person cannot actualize freedom for one whom he does not own. For the Lawgiver said: 'There is no vow for the son of Adam in what he does not own, and no manumission for him in what he does not own, and no divorce for him in what he does not own' (and it is narrated by Tirmidhi). That is: A person cannot make a vow, free, or divorce something he does not own. In this issue, the buyer from the usurper does not own the slave because the sale by the usurper is contingent upon the permission of the owner, and at the time of freeing, the owner's permission was not present, so the buyer was not the owner at that time. At most, you can say that eventually, at the time of permission, ownership was established for the buyer. But we say: This ownership is established by attribution to the prior cause, i.e., the usurper's sale. Ownership established by way of attribution is ownership from one aspect and not from another; it is defective ownership. For freeing, complete ownership is necessary because the hadith 'no manumission in what he does not own' uses absolute ownership, and when absolute is mentioned, it means complete ownership. Here the buyer does not have complete ownership, so the slave will not be freed by the buyer. Since freedom does not occur without ownership, if the usurper freed the usurped slave first and then paid compensation to the owner, the slave is not freed by the usurper. Similarly, if the sale includes a stipulation of option for the seller and the buyer frees the slave, the slave is not freed. Because before the usurper pays compensation and before the buyer obtains the seller's permission, there is no ownership. The ownership gained afterward is by attribution to the prior cause, resulting in defective ownership, not complete ownership. Complete ownership is necessary for freeing. Similarly, if someone bought from the usurper and then sold to another, then the owner permitted the first sale, the second sale is not valid. Likewise, if the buyer from the usurper frees the slave, the freeing is not valid because sale takes effect more quickly than manumission. If the usurper sold and then paid compensation, his sale becomes effective; but if he freed and then paid compensation, his freeing is not effective. Since the buyer's sale is not valid, his freeing is even less likely to be valid. The proof of the Shaykhayn: The buyer's ownership is contingent upon the owner's permission, and it is established by a transaction that is absolute (no condition like khiyar) and designed to transfer ownership. There is no harm to the owner in establishing contingent ownership for the buyer. Since the buyer's ownership is contingent on permission, his freeing is also contingent on permission. When the sale becomes effective by the owner's permission, the freeing becomes effective simultaneously. This is like a man who borrows money and pledges his slave as collateral; then the pledgor sells the slave without the pledgee's permission, and the buyer frees him. This freeing is contingent on the pledgee's permission or redemption of the pledge. If the pledgee permits the sale, the freeing by the buyer from the pledgor becomes effective; similarly, if the pledgor repays the debt, the freeing takes effect. Just as the freeing by the buyer from the pledgor is valid, so too is the freeing by the buyer from the usurper. It is also like an heir who frees a slave from the deceased's estate while the estate is encumbered by debts: this freeing is valid but contingent. If the heir pays off the debts after freeing, the freeing becomes effective. The response to Imam Muhammad's proof: The cases he cited (ghasib's own freeing, khiyar, second sale) are answered. Regarding the usurper freeing the slave: It is not valid because usurpation is not designed to establish ownership; the usurper is an enemy of the owner. Ownership is established for the usurper only by necessity at the time of paying compensation, to prevent both the slave and the compensation from being in the same ownership (the owner's). So the usurper's ownership arises only at payment; since he freed earlier, it is freeing without ownership. Regarding the khiyar case: The sale is not absolute but conditional on khiyar; during khiyar, the buyer does not own the slave. So at the time of freeing, he was not the owner, making the freeing void. Regarding the third issue (second sale): When the owner permits the first sale, the first buyer (who sold to another) acquires absolute ownership, which overrides the contingent ownership he had. The contingent ownership is annulled, and permission cannot attach to it.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage is a detailed inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi dispute. The core issue: A usurper (ghasib) sells a stolen slave, then the buyer (mushtari min al-ghasib) frees the slave. Later, the original owner (mawla) ratifies the sale. The question is whether the manumission becomes valid after ratification. The Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) say yes, by istihsan. Imam Muhammad says no, by qiyas, and is joined by Imam Zufar, Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad. Imam Muhammad's proof is the hadith 'no manumission for what one does not own' (la 'itq li ma la yamlik). At the time of manumission, the buyer did not own the slave because the sale was conditional on ratification. Even if ownership later arises by attribution (istinad) to the original sale, it is defective (naqis) ownership, not complete (kamil). The hadith requires complete ownership. He supports this with three analogies: (1) If the usurper himself frees the slave and then pays compensation, the freeing is invalid. (2) If the sale has a stipulation of option (khiyar al-shart) for the seller, the buyer's freeing is invalid. (3) If the first buyer resells the slave, the second sale is invalid even after ratification. The Shaykhayn respond: The buyer's ownership is contingent (mawquf) upon ratification. Since the transaction was absolute (no khiyar), it is designed for ownership transfer. There is no harm to the owner. Therefore, the manumission, like the sale, becomes effective upon ratification. They analogize to two cases: (a) A mortgaged slave sold by the pledgor without permission: if the pledgee later permits the sale or the debt is paid, the buyer's freeing becomes effective. (b) An heir frees a slave from an estate with debts: the freeing is contingent and becomes effective when the heir pays the debts. The text then provides Imam Muhammad's rebuttal to these analogies: The ghasib case differs because usurpation does not intend ownership; ownership arises only by necessity at payment, so prior freeing fails. The khiyar case differs because the sale is conditional, not absolute. The second sale case differs because absolute ownership, once established, annuls the contingent ownership. Thus each party's proofs are presented and countered. The relied-upon position (al-mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated here, but the text says 'and this is the most correct' (wa hadha huwa al-ashah) at the beginning, indicating preference for the Shaykhayn's view.

Key Terms
ملک موقوف (mulk mawquf): Ownership that is suspended (contingent) upon a future condition, such as ratification by the rightful owner.
شیخین (Shaykhayn): The two Shaykhs: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. In this passage, they hold the istihsan position.
استحسان (istihsan): Juridical preference over qiyas; here used to validate the manumission despite the apparent qiyas against it.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; here the qiyas says manumission is invalid because buyer lacked complete ownership at time of freeing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Shaykhayn), when does the buyer's manumission of a slave purchased from a usurper become effective?
A) At the moment the buyer frees the slave, before any ratification.
B) Only after the owner ratifies the sale.
C) Only after the slave pays a compensation.
D) It never becomes effective because the buyer never owns the slave.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school, by istihsan, validates the buyer's manumission upon ratification, treating contingent ownership as sufficient when perfected.

Freeing by Buyer from Usurper: Suspended Ownership and Authorization
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of freeing by buyer from usurper.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a purchaser from a usurper freeing a slave and explain the intra-madhhab dispute between the Shaykhain and Imam Muhammad regarding the effect of the owner's subsequent authorization.

Core Idea
Suspended ownership can sustain a freeing that becomes effective upon authorization – a key Hanafi principle in muamalat.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the validity of a slave's emancipation by a buyer who purchased from a usurper, without the original owner's permission. The central question is whether the freeing becomes valid when the owner later authorizes the sale. The two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) argue that the buyer's ownership is suspended (milk mawquf) and the freeing is likewise suspended, becoming effective retroactively upon authorization. Imam Muhammad disagrees, holding that since ownership was not absolute at the time of freeing, the act is void. We will follow the arguments and the eventual tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue and the two positions
State the scenario: a usurper sells a slave without the owner's permission; the buyer frees the slave; later the owner authorizes the sale. Identify the opposing views: Shaykhain say freeing becomes valid; Imam Muhammad says it remains invalid.
2
Analyze the Shaykhain's proof via analogy
Examine the analogies: (1) pawner selling without permission – freeing becomes effective upon pawnee's authorization; (2) heir freeing a slave from an encumbered estate – freeing becomes effective upon debt payment. The common illa: ownership is suspended and intended to give benefit, so the freeing is also suspended and becomes effective when ownership becomes absolute.
3
Trace Imam Muhammad's objections
Imam Muhammad raises four issues: (a) if the usurper himself frees and then pays compensation, it is invalid because ownership arises only at payment; (b) if the seller has an option, the buyer is not owner; (c) if the buyer resells the slave; (d) if the usurper pays compensation after the buyer frees. Understand how these are meant to disprove the analogies.
4
Examine the Hanafi response to each objection
The text provides responses: (a) usurpation is not a cause of ownership, unlike a valid contract; (b) option cases involve conditional ownership, whereas here the sale is absolute; (c) upon authorization, absolute ownership voids the suspended ownership, so resale fails; (d) the correct view (Hilal al-Ra'y) is that the freeing becomes effective after compensation, contrary to Imam Muhammad.
This shows the strength of the Shaykhain's reasoning.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its practical consequence
The text endorses the Shaykhain's position as 'more correct' based on the authority of Hilal al-Ra'y. Thus, the operative ruling is that if the owner authorizes, the freeing is valid and the slave becomes free. The practical effect: the purchaser's act is not wasted, and the slave gains freedom retroactively.

The sale by a usurper is not valid. Yet, compared to freeing, sale is implemented quickly. So the freeing by the purchaser from the usurper would a fortiori not be valid. And just as the freeing by the purchaser from the usurper is not valid when the usurper pays the compensation, similarly the freeing by the purchaser from the usurper will not be valid, as if the owner authorized the sale. The proof of the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that the ownership of the purchaser from the usurper is suspended on the permission of the owner of the slave, and it is established through a transaction that is absolute (i.e., without any condition like option), and it is designed to give the benefit of ownership, and in establishing suspended ownership for the purchaser from the usurper, there is no loss to the owner, as previously mentioned. So when the ownership of the purchaser from the usurper is suspended on the owner's permission, his freeing is also suspended on the owner's permission. When the sale becomes effective with the owner's permission, simultaneously the freeing also becomes effective. This becomes like a person who takes a loan and pawns his slave with the creditor. Then the pawner sells the slave without the permission of the pawnee. Then the purchaser frees him. This freeing will remain suspended on the permission of the pawnee or on the redemption of the pawn. That is, if the pawnee permits the sale, the freeing by the purchaser from the pawner will become effective. And if the pawner pays the debt of the pawnee, the freeing will also become effective. So just as the freeing by the purchaser from the pawner is valid and permissible, similarly the freeing by the purchaser from the usurper is valid and permissible. And this is like an heir freeing a slave from the estate of the deceased while the estate is encumbered by debts of people. This freeing is suspended and valid. Thus, if the heir pays the debt of the deceased after freeing the slave, the freeing of the heir becomes effective. The response to Imam Muhammad's proof from the statement 'contrary to the freeing of the usurper... etc.' is the answer to the issues presented by Imam Muhammad. He said: If the usurper himself frees the slave and then pays the compensation, the freeing is not valid because usurpation is not designed to establish ownership, i.e., usurpation does not establish ownership for the usurper because the usurper is the enemy of the owner, and at the time of payment of the guarantee, ownership is established for the usurper out of necessity so that the two counterparts (the slave and the guarantee) do not combine in the ownership of one person, namely the owner. So usurpation becomes a cause for obtaining ownership at the time of payment of the guarantee. It is as if the usurper's ownership of the slave occurred at the time of payment of the guarantee, and he had already freed him earlier. So this is freeing a non-owned (slave), and freeing a non-owned is not valid. Therefore, the freeing by the usurper will not be correct. And in the case of the seller having an option, the freeing by the purchaser is not valid because this sale is not absolute but rather restricted by a stipulated option, and if the seller has a stipulated option, the purchaser is not the owner of the sold item. So at the time of freeing, the purchaser was not the owner of the slave, and when the purchaser was not the owner of the slave at the time of freeing, his freeing is also futile because freeing a non-owned is not valid. The answer to the third issue: When the purchaser from the usurper sold the slave, this is not valid because when the owner (the one from whom it was usurped) authorized the first sale, the seller (the purchaser from the usurper) acquired absolute ownership, and the purchaser from the usurper had suspended ownership. So when absolute ownership was established for the purchaser from the usurper by the owner's permission, and that absolute ownership supervened on the suspended ownership, this absolute ownership will void the suspended ownership. When the suspended ownership is voided, authorization will not attach to it, and since authorization did not attach to it, this (sale) will also not be valid. Therefore, the sale by the purchaser from the usurper to another person will not be correct. The answer to the fourth issue: When the usurper pays the compensation, the non-effectiveness of the freeing by the purchaser from the usurper is not accepted by us, as Imam Muhammad holds the view of non-effectiveness. Rather, after the usurper pays the compensation, the freeing by the purchaser from the usurper becomes effective, as mentioned by Hilal al-Ra'y ibn Yahya al-Basri, the author of Kitab al-Waqf, and this is the more correct opinion. So just as after the usurper pays the compensation, the freeing by the purchaser from the usurper is valid and effective, similarly after the owner gives permission, the freeing by the purchaser from the usurper is valid and effective.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad regarding the validity of a slave's freeing by a purchaser from a usurper when the original owner later authorizes the sale. The text presents the position of the Shaykhain first: they argue that the purchaser's ownership is suspended on the owner's permission, and since the sale contract is absolute (without options), the freeing is also suspended and becomes effective upon authorization. They support this with analogies: a pawner's sale without permission followed by freeing, and an heir freeing a slave from an encumbered estate. Imam Muhammad's counter-argument is then presented: if the usurper himself frees and then pays compensation, it is invalid because usurpation is not a cause of ownership; ownership arises only at payment, so the freeing preceded ownership. Similarly, if the seller has an option, the purchaser is not owner at the time of freeing. The text then addresses three specific issues raised by Imam Muhammad: (1) the case of the purchaser selling the slave to another—this is invalid because upon authorization, absolute ownership replaces suspended ownership, voiding the latter and preventing the sale from being effective; (2) the case of the usurper paying compensation—the correct view (according to Hilal al-Ra'y) is that the freeing becomes effective, contrary to Imam Muhammad's stance. The overall conclusion is that the Shaykhain's position is upheld: the purchaser's freeing is valid and effective upon the owner's authorization.

Key Terms
ملک موقوف (milk mawquf): Suspended ownership; an ownership that is contingent upon a future event, such as authorization by the true owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shaykhain, what is the status of a slave freed by a purchaser from a usurper when the original owner later authorizes the sale?
A) The freeing is invalid because the purchaser was not the owner at the time.
B) The freeing becomes valid retroactively upon authorization.
C) The freeing is valid only if the usurper also pays compensation.
D) The freeing is void ab initio.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a purchaser from a usurper can validly free a slave if the owner later authorizes the sale, because the buyer's suspended ownership (milk mawquf) becomes absolute and retroactively validates the freeing.

Retroactive Ownership and Compensation: The Case of a Cut Slave Hand
Intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation entitlement after sale authorization

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on compensation for a cut slave hand when the sale is later authorized, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute between the Shaykhain and Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
Authorization perfects ownership retroactively, so compensation belongs to the purchaser — proving that freeing should also be valid.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a nuanced case within the Hanafi school: a slave purchased from a usurper has his hand cut off, compensation is taken, and then the original owner authorizes the sale. Who keeps the compensation? The answer reveals a deeper principle about retroactive ownership and its limits. This ruling also serves as a proof against Imam Muhammad's position on freeing in suspended ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
The scenario: a slave purchased from a usurper, hand cut, compensation taken, then owner authorizes. Ruling: compensation goes to the purchaser.
This is the starting point.
2
Understand the principle of retroactive ownership
Authorization perfects ownership from the time of purchase (milk tamma min waqt al-shira), so the injury occurred on the purchaser's property.
This is the key legal principle.
3
Analyze Imam Muhammad's objection and his analogies
Imam Muhammad argues that partial ownership suffices for compensation, citing the mukatab case and khiyar sale.
He does not dispute the compensation ruling itself but its implications.
4
See how the ruling is used as a proof against Imam Muhammad on freeing
The text argues that if compensation is due to full retroactive ownership, then freeing should also be valid upon authorization, contradicting Imam Muhammad's view.
This exposes a tension in Imam Muhammad's position.
5
Note the charity condition for excess over half the price
Any compensation exceeding half the sale price must be given in charity because the slave never fully entered the purchaser's liability.
This is an additional nuance.

قال فإن قطعت يد العبد فاخذ ارشها ثم اجاز البيع فالارش للمشترى لان الملك تم له من وقت الشراء فتبين ان القطع حصل على ملكه وهذه حجة على محمد والعذر له ان الملك من وجه یکفی لاستحقاق الارش كالمكاتب اذا قطعت يده واخذ الارش ثم رد فى الرق يكون الارش للمولى وكذا اذا قطعت يد المشترى في يد المشترى والخيار للبائع ثم اجيز البيع فالارش للمشترى بخلاف الاعتاق على مامر و يتصدق بما زاد على نصف الثمن لانه لم يدخل في ضمانه و فيه شبهة عدم الملک ترجمہ پس اگر غلام کا ہاتھ کاٹا گیا اور مشتری من الغاصب نے اس کا جرمانہ وصول کر لیا پھر بیع کی اجازت دی تو یہ جرمانہ مشتری کے واسطے ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مشتری کی ملکیت خرید کے وقت سے پوری ہوگئی۔ پس ظاہر ہوا کہ ہاتھ کا نا جانا مشتری کی ملکیت پر واقع ہوا اور یہ مسئلہ امام محمد" پر حجت ہے۔ اور امام محمد کا عذر یہ ہے کہ ہاتھ کی دیت کے مستحق ہونے کے واسطے ایک طرح کی ملکیت کافی ہوتی ہے۔ جیسے مکاتب کا ہاتھ کاٹا گیا اور جرمانہ لیا پھر وہ رقیق ہو گیا تو یہ جرمانہ کا مال مولیٰ کیلئے ہوتا ہے۔ اور جیسے اگر مشتری کے پاس مبیع کا ہاتھ کاٹا گیا۔ حالانکہ بائع کیلئے خیار ہے پھر بیع کی اجازت دے دی گئی تو یہ جرمانہ مشتری کو ملے گا بر خلاف اعتقاق کے جیسا کہ اوپر گذر چکا ہے اور نصف ثمن سے جو زائد ہے اس کو صدقہ کر دے اس لئے کہ غلام مشتری کے منمان میں داخل نہیں ہوا تھا یا اس میں ملک نہ ہونے کا شبہ ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مشتری من الغاصب کے پاس غلام کا ہاتھ کاٹا گیا اور مشتری نے اس کا جرمانہ لے لیا پھر مولیٰ نے غاصب کی بیع کی اجازت دی تو یہ جرمانہ مشتری من الغاصب کے لئے ہوگا کیونکہ اجازت کی وجہ سے مشتری کی ملکیت خرید کے وقت سے پوری ہوگئی۔ پس ظاہر ہوا کہ ہاتھ کا کانٹا جانا مشتری کی ملکیت پر واقع ہوا اور جب ہاتھ مشتری کی ملکیت میں کا نا گیا تو جرمانہ بھی مشتر می ہی کیلئے ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ مسئلہ امام محمد کے خلاف حجت ہے اسلئے کہ امام محمد ملک موقوف میں آزاد کرنا جائز قرار نہیں دیتے ہیں۔ حالانکہ اگر مشتری کو ملکیت حاصل نہ ہوتی تو مالک کی اجازت کے وقت اس کو ہاتھ کا جرمانہ حاصل نہ ہوتا۔ پس مشتری من الغاصب کیلئے جرمانہ کا حاصل نہ ہونا اس بات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اجازت کی وجہ سے مشتری کیلئے خرید کے وقت سے ملکیت حاصل ہو گئی ہے اور جب مشتری کیلئے ملکیت حاصل ہو گئی تو اس کی طرف سے آزاد کرنا بھی درست ہوگا ۔ حالانکہ امام محمد آزاد کرنا جائز قرار نہیں دیتے ہیں۔ حضرت
The slave's hand was cut off, its compensation was taken, then the sale was declared valid. Then the compensation will be for the purchaser. He said: 'If the slave's hand is cut off, and its arsh (compensation) is taken, then the sale is authorized, the arsh is for the purchaser, because ownership is perfected for him from the time of purchase. So it becomes clear that the cutting occurred on his property. And this is a proof against Muhammad. And his excuse is that ownership from one aspect is sufficient for entitlement to arsh, like the mukatab (slave under contract of manumission): if his hand is cut off and he takes the arsh, then he is returned to slavery, the arsh is for the master. And similarly, if the hand of the purchased item is cut off while in the possession of the purchaser and the seller has an option, then the sale is authorized, the arsh is for the purchaser, contrary to freeing as previously mentioned. And he should give in charity what exceeds half the price because it did not enter his liability, and there is a semblance of non-ownership.' Translation: So if the slave's hand was cut off and the purchaser from the usurper took its compensation, then the owner authorized the sale, this compensation will be for the purchaser. Because the purchaser's ownership is perfected from the time of purchase. So it becomes clear that the loss of the hand occurred on his property, and this issue is a proof against Imam Muhammad. And Imam Muhammad's excuse is that ownership from one aspect is sufficient for entitlement to the compensation for the hand. Like the mukatab: if his hand is cut off and he takes the compensation, then he becomes a slave again, the compensation's property is for the master. And like if the hand of the sold item is cut off while in the possession of the purchaser and the seller has an option, then the sale is authorized, and this compensation will go to the purchaser, contrary to freeing as previously mentioned. And he should give in charity what exceeds half the price because the slave did not enter his guarantee, and there is a suspicion of non-ownership. Explanation of the scenario: If the slave's hand was cut off while with the purchaser from the usurper, and the purchaser took its compensation, then the master authorized the usurper's sale, this compensation will be for the purchaser from the usurper, because due to authorization, the purchaser's ownership is perfected from the time of purchase. So it becomes apparent that the cutting of the hand occurred on his property, and when the hand was cut off while in the purchaser's ownership, the compensation will be for the purchaser himself. The author of Hidayah says: This issue is a proof against Imam Muhammad because Imam Muhammad does not consider freeing valid in suspended ownership. But if the purchaser did not have ownership, at the time of the owner's authorization, he would not have obtained the compensation for the hand. So the fact that the purchaser from the usurper obtains the compensation is evidence that due to authorization, the purchaser obtained ownership from the time of purchase, and when he obtained ownership, his act of freeing is also valid. Yet Imam Muhammad does not consider freeing valid.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling and an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding compensation for a slave's cut hand when the sale by a usurper is later authorized. The ruling: If a slave's hand is cut while in the possession of a purchaser from a usurper, and the compensation (arsh) is taken, then the original owner authorizes the sale, the compensation belongs to the purchaser. The reason: Authorization retroactively perfects the purchaser's ownership from the time of purchase, so the injury occurred on his property. The text explicitly states this is a proof against Imam Muhammad, who holds that freeing by such a purchaser is invalid even after authorization. Imam Muhammad's counter-argument is that a partial ownership suffices for entitlement to compensation, using analogies: (1) a mukatab (slave under contract for manumission) who takes compensation and then is returned to slavery—the compensation goes to the master; (2) a sale with a seller's option—if the item is injured before authorization, the compensation goes to the purchaser upon authorization. However, the text notes that for freeing, the ruling is different, as previously discussed. Additionally, any amount received as compensation that exceeds half the price of the slave must be given in charity because the slave never fully entered the purchaser's liability (damān), indicating a semblance of non-ownership. The author of Hidayah then argues that this case undermines Imam Muhammad's position: if the purchaser obtains compensation due to retroactive ownership, then freeing should also be valid upon authorization, contrary to Imam Muhammad's view.

Key Terms
ارش (arsh): Compensation paid for a bodily injury to a slave, equivalent to the diminution in value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a slave purchased from a usurper, if the slave's hand is cut and compensation taken, then the owner authorizes the sale, who gets the compensation?
A) The original owner
B) The usurper
C) The purchaser
D) It is given in charity

Key Takeaway
Authorization perfects ownership retroactively from the time of purchase, so compensation for pre-authorization injuries belongs to the purchaser, supporting the validity of freeing.

Compensation for Injured Slave After Ratification of Sale
Ruling on compensation after ratification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on compensation for an injured slave sold by a usurper and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on partial ownership.

Core Idea
Ratification perfects ownership retroactively; compensation belongs to the buyer, but excess profit must be given in charity.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a case where a slave sold by a usurper is injured, compensation is taken, and then the original owner ratifies the sale. The ruling hinges on retroactive ownership and the concept of partial ownership (milk min wajh). It also reveals an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and the two seniors. By the end, you will trace the legal reasoning and understand the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
A slave sold by a usurper; the slave's hand is cut; compensation (arsh) is taken; later the original owner ratifies the sale. Determine who owns the compensation.
2
State the Ruling and Its Basis
The compensation belongs to the buyer because ratification retroactively establishes complete ownership from the time of purchase, so the injury occurred on the buyer's property.
3
Examine the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Imam Muhammad argues that partial ownership suffices for compensation but not for emancipation. The text uses this as a proof against him: if partial ownership works for compensation, why not for emancipation?
4
Understand the Charity Obligation
If the compensation exceeds half the price, the excess must be given in charity because it is not secured by liability (daman) and has an element of non-ownership.
5
Apply the Analogies
The ruling analogizes to the mukatab (partial ownership suffices for compensation) and to cases with khiyar (sale with option). Recognize these patterns to solidify the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال فإن قطعت يد العبد فاخذ ارشها ثم اجاز البيع فالارش للمشترى لان الملك تم له من وقت الشراء فتبين ان القطع حصل على ملكه وهذه حجة على محمد والعذر له ان الملك من وجه یکفی لاستحقاق الارش كالمكاتب اذا قطعت يده واخذ الارش ثم رد فى الرق يكون الارش للمولى وكذا اذا قطعت يد المشترى في يد المشترى والخيار للبائع ثم اجيز البيع فالارش للمشترى بخلاف الاعتاق على مامر و يتصدق بما زاد على نصف الثمن لانه لم يدخل في ضمانه و فيه شبهة عدم الملک
He said: If the slave's hand is cut and its compensation is taken, then the sale is ratified, then the compensation is for the buyer because ownership is perfected for him from the time of purchase, so it becomes clear that the cutting occurred on his property. And this is an argument against Muhammad. His excuse is that partial ownership suffices for entitlement to compensation, like the mukatab when his hand is cut and he takes compensation, then he returns to slavery, the compensation is for the master. Similarly, if the hand of the bought slave is cut while in the buyer's possession and the seller has an option, then the sale is ratified, the compensation is for the buyer, contrary to emancipation as passed. And he should give in charity whatever exceeds half the price because it did not enter his liability, and there is an element of non-ownership in it.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling of the Hanafi school regarding a slave sold by a usurper. The case: the buyer from the usurper takes the slave, the slave's hand is cut, and the buyer receives compensation (arsh). Later, the original owner ratifies the sale. The ruling states that the compensation belongs to the buyer, because ratification retroactively establishes the buyer's complete ownership from the time of purchase. This positions the buyer as owner at the time the hand was cut, so he deserves the compensation. The author (al-Marghinani) notes that this is a proof against Imam Muhammad, who holds that emancipation by the buyer is not valid before ratification. Imam Muhammad's response is that for entitlement to compensation, partial ownership suffices, not complete ownership. He gives examples: a mukatab (slave on a contract of manumission) whose hand is cut—if he later returns to slavery, the compensation goes to the master, not the mukatab, because the mukatab had only partial ownership. Another example: a slave sold with an option (khiyar) for the seller; the hand is cut while in buyer's possession, then the sale is ratified—compensation goes to the buyer. However, in the case of emancipation by the buyer before ratification, Imam Muhammad does not consider it valid because complete ownership is necessary for emancipation. The passage also rules that if the compensation exceeds half the price (thaman), the excess must be given in charity because that excess is profit not secured by liability (daman) or has an element of non-ownership.

Key Terms
أرش (arsh): Compensation paid for injury to a slave, equivalent to the reduction in value.
ملك من وجه (milk min wajh): Partial or incomplete ownership that is valid for some legal effects but not others.
ضمان (daman): Liability; the obligation to compensate for loss or damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what must the buyer do if the compensation (arsh) for the slave's hand exceeds half the price?
A) Keep the entire amount as profit
B) Return the excess to the original owner
C) Give the excess in charity
D) Give the excess to the usurper

Key Takeaway
Compensation for injury to a slave sold by a usurper belongs to the buyer after ratification, but any profit exceeding half the price must be given in charity due to lack of full liability.

Second Sale Invalid After Owner's Ratification Due to Gharar
Ruling on validity of second sale when owner ratifies first sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the second sale after ratification and explain why gharar invalidates it, while distinguishing the Hanafi position on emancipation.

Core Idea
Gharar in a sale invalidates it, even if the original owner later ratifies the first transaction.

This lesson examines a scenario where a buyer from a usurper sells a stolen slave to a second person before the original owner ratifies the first sale. After ratification, we determine the validity of the second sale. The ruling hinges on the concept of gharar (uncertainty) and the retroactive effect of ownership, with an important intra-Hanafi difference regarding emancipation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
Identify the parties: original owner (mawla), first buyer (from usurper), second buyer. The first buyer sells the slave to a second person before the owner ratifies the first sale. Then the owner ratifies.
The first sale is suspended on ratification.
2
Identify the ruling and its reasons
The second sale is not valid. Two reasons: (1) Ratification perfects the first buyer's ownership retroactively, overriding the second sale; (2) The second sale involved gharar because its validity depended on future ratification.
Gharar invalidates sales in Hanafi law.
3
Contrast with emancipation
Compare the second sale to emancipation (itq) by the first buyer. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, emancipation is valid even before ratification because gharar does not affect it. The author (al-Marghinani) implies that emancipation should also be invalid, indicating an ikhtilaf.
The two (Sahibayn) distinguish sales from emancipation regarding gharar.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah) is that the second sale is invalid. For emancipation, the text seems to side with Imam Muhammad that it is invalid, but the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it valid. The practical consequence: second sale always invalid; emancipation may be valid according to some.
Al-Marghinani's matn presents the invalidity of the second sale as the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال فإن باعه المشترى من اخر ثم اجاز المولى البيع الأول لم يجز البيع الثاني لما ذكرنا و لان فيه غرر الانفساخ على اعتبار عدم الاجازة فى البيع الاول والبيع يفسد به بخلاف الاعتاق عندهما لانه لا يؤثر فيه الغرر
He said: If the buyer sells it to another, then the owner ratifies the first sale, the second sale is not valid due to what we mentioned, and because there is gharar (uncertainty) of dissolution based on considering the non-ratification of the first sale, and a sale is invalidated by it, contrary to emancipation according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because gharar does not affect it.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage discusses a scenario where the buyer from a usurper sells the slave to a second person before the original owner ratifies the first sale. After the owner ratifies the first sale, the question arises: is the second sale valid? The ruling states that the second sale is not valid. Two reasons are given: First, as mentioned earlier, when complete ownership (from ratification) overrides the suspended ownership, it invalidates the earlier sale (the second sale is actually later in time but based on the first buyer's defective ownership). Second, there is gharar (uncertainty) because the validity of the second sale depends on whether the owner will ratify the first sale; this uncertainty makes the second sale invalid. The passage contrasts this with emancipation (itq) by the first buyer: according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), emancipation is valid even before ratification because gharar does not affect the validity of emancipation. The author (al-Marghinani) does not accept this view, as indicated by the phrase 'bikhilaf al-i'taq 'indahuma' — meaning the ruling is contrary to their view on emancipation. Thus, the relied-upon position is that the second sale is invalid, while emancipation is also invalid according to Imam Muhammad but valid according to the two; the text here seems to follow the view of Imam Muhammad? Actually, the phrasing 'bikhilaf al-i'taq 'indahuma' suggests that for emancipation, the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it valid despite gharar, while the author's position is that it is invalid (like the second sale). The commentary clarifies that the difference is that gharar invalidates sales but not emancipation according to the two; the author implies that gharar does invalidate emancipation as well, hence the contrast.

Key Terms
غرر (gharar): Uncertainty or risk that invalidates a sale, such as uncertainty about the existence or delivery of the object of sale.
انفساخ (infisakh): Dissolution or annulment of a contract automatically due to a condition or event.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the buyer from a usurper sells the slave to another person, and then the original owner ratifies the first sale, what is the status of the second sale?
A) It becomes valid
B) It is invalid due to gharar
C) It remains suspended until the second buyer agrees
D) It is valid if the second buyer knew the situation

Key Takeaway
A sale dependent on a future uncertain event (like ratification) is invalid due to gharar, even if the event later occurs.
